The Duration of Breastfeeding: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
States the duration of breastfeeding and the intra-Hanafi dispute on its limit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the duration of breastfeeding that establishes prohibition, identify the proofs for each view, and explain which position is mufta bihi and why.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school, in its relied-upon ruling, limits breastfeeding prohibition to two years, despite Abu Hanifa's cautious extension to thirty months.

This passage from the Quduri matn presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the maximum period within which breastfeeding creates marital prohibition (tahrim al-nikah). While Abu Hanifa held a cautious view extending the period to thirty months, his two leading disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, restricted it to exactly two years. We will examine the textual proofs cited by each side and understand how the school ultimately settled on the shorter period as the operative ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested ruling
The dispute is about the timeframe within which breastfeeding establishes a foster relationship that makes marriage between the child and certain relatives prohibited. What is the exact duration that triggers this legal effect?
Abu Hanifa: 30 months. Sahibayn: 2 years.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his reasoning
Abu Hanifa holds that the period is thirty months (two years plus six months). He bases this on the hadith 'No breastfeeding except within the two years' and the Quranic verse (2:233), but adds a six-month caution based on the possibility that some pregnancies extend to thirty months, as mentioned in a narration from Mu'atta Malik.
This cautious extension is an example of istihsan (juristic preference) for precaution.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their evidence
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the period is exactly two years. They interpret the same hadith and verse literally. They also cite the hadith from Aisha: 'Breastfeeding is from hunger,' which indicates that only the milk that satisfies hunger (i.e., during early infancy) matters, and the hadith of Ibn Abbas with the explicit limit of two years.
The Sahibayn's literal reading is the default usul position unless a strong reason for extension exists.
4
Analyse the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If a child is breastfed between the ages of two and two-and-a-half years, Abu Hanifa says it creates prohibition; the Sahibayn say it does not. This directly affects whom the child may marry in the future.
This is the key practical difference that a mufti must be aware of.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and reason for tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is that of the Sahibayn: two years. The tarjih is based on the strength of the hadith evidence and the fact that the literal interpretation is safer and avoids extending the prohibition beyond what the text explicitly states.
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah and later authorities adopt the Sahibayn's view as the preponderant opinion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الرَّضَاع
وَمُدَّةُ الرَّضَاعِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ ثَلَاثُونَ شَهْرًا. وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ سَنَتَانِ فَإِذَا مَضَتْ مُدَّةُ الرَّضَاعَ لَمْ يَتَعَلَّقَ بِالرَّضَاعَ تَحْرِيمٌ

وجه (۱) قول ابي حنيفة لثبوت وَمُدَّةُ الرَّضَاعِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ \ وَكَانَ أَبُو حَنِيفَةَ رحمه الله يَحْتَاطُ بِسِتَّةِ أَشْهُرٍ بَعْدَ الْخَوْلَيْنِ، فَيَقُولُ: يُحَرِّمُ مَا كَانَ فِي الْحَوْلَيْنِ وَبَعْدَهُمَا إِلَى تَمَامِ سِتَّةِ أَشْهُرٍ، وَذَلِكَ ثَلاثُونَ شَهْرًا ، وَلا يُحَرِّمُ مَا كَانَ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ، وَنَحْنُ لا نَرَى أَنَّهُ يُحَرِّمُ، وَنَرَى أَنَّهُ لَا يُحَرِّمُ مَا كَانَ بَعْدَ الْحَوْلَيْنِ (مؤطا مالك: باب: الرضاع، نمبر 628)
وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَمُدَّةُ الرَّضَاعِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ اعَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ ، قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم : «لَا رَضَاعَ إِلَّا مَا كَانَ فِي الْحَوْلَيْنِ». (دار قطني : كتاب الرضاع، نمبر 4364, سنن بيهقي: باب ما جاء في تحديد ذلك بالحولي،نمبر 15663)
وجه: (٢) الآية لثبوت وَمُدَّةُ الرَّضَاعِ عِنْدَ أَبي حَنِيفَةَ وَالْوَالِدَاتُ يُرْضِعْنَ أَوْلَدَهُنَّ حَوْلَيْنِ كَامِلَيْنِ لِمَنْ أَرَادَ أَن يُتِمَّ الرَّضَاعَةَ ) (القرآن،سورة البقرة2، الآية، نمبر 29)
ج
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت فَإِذَا مَضَتْ مُدَّةُ الرَّضَاعِ لَمْ يَتَعَلَّقْ بِالرَّضَاعَ تَحْرِيمُ \ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ لي : .... فَقَالَ : انْظُرْنَ مَنْ إِخْوَانُكُنَّ، فَإِنَّمَا الرَّضَاعَةُ مِنَ الْمَجَاعَةِ . » بخار شريف: باب من قال لا رضاع بعد حولين نمبر 5102 / ابي داؤد شريف: باب في رضاعة الكبير،نمبر2058) وجه : (٢) الحديث لثبوت فَإِذَا مَضَتْ مُدَّةُ الرَّضَاعَ لَمْ يَتَعَلَّقُ بِالرَّضَاعِ تَحْرِيمُ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسِ ، قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم : «لَا رَضَاعَ إِلَّا مَا كَانَ فِي الْحَوْلَيْنِ». دار قطني : كتاب الرضاع، نمبر 4364)
Book of Breastfeeding: And the period of breastfeeding according to Abu Hanifa is thirty months. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: two years. So when the breastfeeding period passes, prohibition is not established by breastfeeding. 
Proof (1) for establishing Abu Hanifa's view: And Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) was cautious with six months after the two years, so he said: it prohibits what was in the two years and after them up to the completion of six months, and that is thirty months, and it does not prohibit what was after that, and we do not see that it prohibits, and we see that it does not prohibit what was after the two years. (Mu'atta Malik: Bab al-Rada', no. 628)
Proof (2) the hadith for establishing Abu Hanifa's view: from Ibn Abbas, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'No breastfeeding except within the two years.' (Dar Qutni: Book of Rada', no. 4364, Bayhaqi: Bab ... no. 15663)
Proof (2) the Quranic verse for establishing Abu Hanifa's view: (The mothers shall breastfeed their children two complete years for whoever wishes to complete the breastfeeding) (Quran 2:29) 
Proof (1) the hadith for establishing that when the breastfeeding period passes, prohibition is not established by breastfeeding: from Aisha: ... he said: 'Look to who are your brothers, for breastfeeding is from hunger.' (Bukhari: Bab ... no. 5102, Abu Dawud: Bab ... no. 2058)
Proof (2) the hadith for establishing that when the breastfeeding period passes, prohibition is not established by breastfeeding: from Ibn Abbas, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'No breastfeeding except within the two years.' (Dar Qutni: Book of Rada', no. 4364)
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage introduces the duration of breastfeeding (muddah al-rada') that establishes marital prohibition. The matn presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa holds the period to be thirty months (two years plus six additional months as a caution), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn) hold it to be exactly two years. The commentator then provides proofs: Abu Hanifa's reasoning from a narration in Mu'atta Malik about caution, a hadith from Ibn Abbas that 'no breastfeeding except within two years,' and the Quranic verse from Surah al-Baqarah. The Sahibayn also use the same hadith but interpret it literally. The passage then states the practical consequence: breastfeeding after the two-year period does not create prohibition, supporting the Sahibayn's view which is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position. Additional hadiths from Aisha and Ibn Abbas reinforce this. The key point: the Hanafi school, in its operative fatwa, limits prohibition through breastfeeding to the first two years of life.

Key Terms
رضاع (radāʿ): Breastfeeding that establishes the legal relationship of fosterage (riḍāʿ) with marriage prohibitions
مدة الرضاع (muddah al-riḍāʿ): The legal duration during which breastfeeding can create prohibition

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school, what is the maximum period of breastfeeding that establishes marital prohibition?
A) 30 months
B) 2 years
C) 18 months
D) 3 years

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's operative ruling is that breastfeeding creates a marriage prohibition only if it occurs within the first two years of the child's life.

6 min
The General Principle of Prohibition through Breastfeeding and Its Exceptions
States general rule and three exceptions with Quranic proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general Hanafi rule that breastfeeding creates the same marriage prohibitions as blood lineage and identify the three specific exceptions.

Core Idea
Breastfeeding creates marriage prohibitions like blood, but with three explicit exceptions.

The rule seems simple: if breastfeeding makes someone like a blood relative, then all marriage prohibitions of lineage transfer. Yet the Hanafi school recognizes that the analogy is not perfect in every case. This passage from al-Quduri lays down the general principle, then carves out three exceptions where the prohibition does not apply, supported by the Quranic verse on wives of sons.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Identify the overarching principle: 'what is prohibited from breastfeeding is what is prohibited from lineage.' This is the foundation of all rulings on foster relationships.
The ruling applies symmetrically: a foster-mother is like a mother, a foster-sister like a sister, etc.
2
List the exceptions
The passage explicitly names three cases where the rule does NOT apply: the mother of one's foster-brother, the sister of one's foster-son, and the sister of one's foster-brother. Understand why each is permissible.
These exceptions are specific to the Hanafi school; other schools may differ.
3
Analyze the Quranic proof
The passage cites Quran 4:23 for the prohibition of marrying the wife of one's son. This includes foster sons, as breastfeeding makes a child like a biological son. Understand the wajh al-dalalah (point of inference) from the verse.
The verse does not explicitly mention foster sons; the extension is via the hadith that 'breastfeeding makes prohibited what is prohibited by lineage.'
4
Apply the rule to a new case
Consider a scenario: a man wants to marry his foster-daughter-in-law. Is it permissible? Apply the general rule and see if any exception applies.
Foster-daughter-in-law is prohibited under the rule; no exception covers her.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَحْرُمُ مِنْ الرَّضَاعَ مَا يَحْرُمُ مِنْ النَّسَبِ إِلَّا أُمَّ أَخِيهِ مِنْ الرَّضَاعَ فَإِنَّهُ يَجُوزُ لَهُ أَنْ يَتَزَوَّجَهَا وَلَا يَجُوزُ أَنْ يَتَزَوَّجَ أُمَّ أَخِيهِ مِنْ النَّسَبِ وَيَجُوزُ أَنْ يَتَزَوَّجَ أُخْتَ ابْنِهِ مِنْ الرَّضَاعِ

ه وَلَا يَجُوزُ مِنْ النَّسَبِ وَامْرَأَةَ ابْنِهِ مِنْ الرَّضَاعِ لَا يَجُوزُ أَنْ يَتَزَوَّجَهَا كَمَا لَا يَجُوزُ ذَلِكَ مِنْ النَّسَبِ

وَيَجُوزُ أَنْ يَتَزَوَّجَ أُخْتَ أَخِيهِ مِنْ الرَّضَاعَ كَمَا يَجُوزُ مِنْ النَّسَبِ وَذَلِكَ مِثْلَ الْآخِ مِنْ الْأَبِ إِذَا كَانَ لَهُ أُخْتٌ مِنْ أُمِّهِ جَازَ لِأَخِيهِ مِنْ أَبِيهِ أَنْ يَتَزَوَّجَهَا

وجه: (1) الأية لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ مِنْ النَّسَبِ وَامْرَأَةَ ابْنِهِ مِنْ الرَّضَاعَ) ﴿وَرَبَيبُكُمُ الَّتِي فِي حُجُورِكُم مِّن نِّسَابِكُمُ الَّتِي دَخَلْتُم بِهِنَّ فَإِن لَّمْ تَكُونُوا دَخَلْتُم بِهِنَّ فَلَا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْكُمْ وَحَلَبِلُ أَبْنَابِكُمُ الَّذِينَ مِنْ أَصْلَبِكُمْ ﴾(،سورة النساء4، الآية، نمبر 23) وجه : (۲) قول التابعى لثبوت وَمُدَّةُ الرَّضَاع عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ احَدَّثَنِي عَمِّي إِيَاسُ بْنُ عَامِرٍ قَالَ: " قَالَ لَا تَنْكِحْ مَنْ أَرْضَعَتْهُ امْرَأَةُ أَبِيكَ، وَلَا امْرَأَةُ ابْنِكَ، وَلَا امْرَأَةُ أَخِيكَ " (سنن بيهقي: باب: يحرم من الرضاع ما يحرم من الولادة وأن لبن الفحل يحرم، نمبر 15616)

اصول: رضاعت سے وہ رشتے حرام ہونگے جو نسب سے حرام ہوتے ہیں، سوائے چند کے مثلار ضاعی بہن کی ماں سے ، اور رضاعی بیٹے کی بہن سے ، اور رضاعی بھائی کی بہن سے۔
And what is prohibited from breastfeeding is what is prohibited from lineage, except the mother of his brother from breastfeeding, for it is permissible for him to marry her, and it is not permissible for him to marry the mother of his brother from lineage, and it is permissible for him to marry the sister of his son from breastfeeding.
And from lineage it is not permissible, and the wife of his son from breastfeeding is not permissible for him to marry, just as that is not permissible from lineage.
And it is permissible for him to marry the sister of his brother from breastfeeding, just as it is permissible from lineage. That is like the brother from the father: if he has a sister from his mother, his brother from his father is allowed to marry her.
Proof (1) the verse for establishing 'and the wife of his son from breastfeeding is not permissible from lineage': (and your step-daughters in your care from your wives... and the wives of your sons from your loins) (Quran 4:23). Proof (2) the saying of the Tabi'i for establishing the duration of breastfeeding according to Abu Hanifa: My uncle Iyas ibn 'Amir narrated to me: he said, 'Do not marry the one who was breastfed by your father's wife, nor the wife of your son, nor the wife of your brother.' (Bayhaqi: Bab ... no. 15616)
Principle: Through breastfeeding, those relations become prohibited that are prohibited through lineage, except a few such as the mother of the foster-sister, and the sister of the foster-son, and the sister of the foster-brother.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage states the general rule that breastfeeding creates the same marriage prohibitions as blood lineage, with explicit exceptions. The matn lists exceptions: (1) the mother of one's foster-brother is permissible to marry (because she is only a foster-mother to one's brother, but not one's own foster-mother); (2) the sister of one's foster-son is permissible (she is not a foster-sibling to oneself); (3) the wife of one's foster-son (foster-daughter-in-law) is prohibited, exactly as in lineage (Quran 4:23). The passage also clarifies that one may marry the sister of one's foster-brother, just as a half-brother from the father may marry the sister of his half-brother from the mother (since they share no blood relation). The proofs include the Quranic verse prohibiting marriage to wives of sons (whether biological or foster) and a saying of a Tabi'i. An Urdu summary at the end reiterates the general principle and the exceptions. This passage guards against the misconception that all lineage prohibitions are exactly mirrored without exception.

Key Terms
نسب (nasab): Blood lineage; biological relationship
رضاع (radā'): Breastfeeding; foster relationship created by nursing

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Is it permissible for a man to marry the mother of his foster-brother?
A) Yes, it is permissible
B) No, it is prohibited
C) It is makruh
D) It is mubah

Key Takeaway
Breastfeeding creates marriage prohibitions identical to blood lineage, except for three explicitly permitted relations: the mother of one's foster-brother, the sister of one's foster-son, and the sister of one's foster-brother.

The Prohibition of the Milk of the Husband (Laban al-Fahl)
Ruling and proofs for laban al-fahl.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of laban al-fahl and explain its basis using the hadith of Aisha and the saying of Ibn Abbas.

Core Idea
Breastfeeding from the husband's milk creates permanent fosterage prohibitions as if the husband were the biological father.

Islamic law establishes fosterage relationships through breastfeeding, but what about the husband's role? The concept of laban al-fahl (milk of the stallion) shows that the husband's milk—produced by his wife due to their marriage—also creates prohibitions. This lesson examines the ruling and its proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the core ruling: if a woman breastfeeds a girl, that girl becomes mahram to the woman's husband, his father, and his sons. The husband becomes a foster-father.
The ruling applies to both boys and girls; the passage specifies a girl for illustration.
2
Define laban al-fahl
Understand that laban al-fahl is the milk produced by a woman due to her marital relationship, legally attributed to the husband for determining fosterage.
The term 'fahl' (stallion) metaphorically refers to the husband.
3
Examine the primary proof
Analyze the hadith of Aisha: the Prophet (peace be upon him) told her to admit her foster-uncle (husband of the woman who breastfed her), establishing that the husband is a mahram.
The hadith is cited from Tirmidhi and Muslim.
4
Examine the secondary proof
Analyze the saying of Ibn Abbas: if two women married to the same man each breastfeed a child, those children are foster-siblings because the milk of the stallion is one.
This companion saying is also from Tirmidhi.
5
Consider the ikhtilaf
Note that a minority, such as the Zahiris, reject attributing fosterage to the husband, but the Hanafi school and the majority accept it based on these proofs.
The practical effect: Hanafis consider the husband a foster-father; Zahiris do not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَبَنُ الْفَحْلِ يَتَعَلَّقُ بِهِ التَّحْرِيمُ، وَهُوَ إِنْ ارْتَضَعَ الْمَرْأَةَ صَبِيَّةٌ فَتَحْرُمُ هَذِهِ الصَّبِيَّةُ عَلَى زَوْجِهَا وَعَلَى آبَائِهِ وَأَبْنَائِهِ وَيَصِيرُ الزَّوْجُ الَّذِي نَزَلَ مِنْهُ اللَّبَنُ أَبًا لِلْمِرْضَعَةِ

د وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَبَنُ الْفَحْلِ يَتَعَلَّقُ بِهِ التَّحْرِيمُ \ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ قَالَتْ: جَاءَ عَمِّي مِنَ الرَّضَاعَةِ يَسْتَأْذِنُ عَلَيَّ، فَأَبَيْتُ أَنْ آذَنَ لَهُ، حَتَّى أَسْتَأْمِرَ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم : فَلْيَلِجُ عَلَيْكِ فَإِنَّهُ عَمُّكِ»، قَالَتْ: إِنَّمَا أَرْضَعَتْنِي المَرْأَةُ وَلَمْ يُرْضِعْنِي الرَّجُلُ، قَالَ: «فَإِنَّهُ عَمُّكِ فَلْيَلِجْ عَلَيْكِ» (ترمذی شریف: باب ما جاء في لبن الفحل،نمبر 1148 ، باب لبن الفحل، نمبر 5103 ، مسلم شریف : (۲) باب تحريم الرضاعة من ماء الفحل،نمبر 1445) وجه (۲)قول الصحابي لثبوت وَلَبَنُ الْفَحْلِ يَتَعَلَّقُ بِهِ التَّحْرِيمُ اعَنْ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، أَنَّهُ سُئِلَ عَنْ رَجُلِ لَهُ جَارِيتَانِ أَرْضَعَتْ إِحْدَاهُمَا جَارِيَةً، وَالأُخْرَى غُلَامًا ، أَيَحِلُّ لِلْغُلَامِ أَنْ يَتَزَوَّجَ بِالجَارِيَةِ؟ فَقَالَ: «لَا اللَّقَاحُ وَاحِدٌ» (ترمذي شريف: باب ما جاء في لبن الفحل،نمبر 1149)
And the milk of the stallion (husband) establishes prohibition, and it is that if a woman breastfeeds a girl, then this girl becomes prohibited to her husband (the woman's husband) and to his fathers and his sons, and the husband from whom the milk originated becomes a father to the breastfed girl.
Proof (1) the hadith for establishing the prohibition of laban al-fahl: from Aisha, she said: My paternal uncle from breastfeeding came seeking permission to enter, so I refused to permit him until I asked the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). The Messenger said: 'Let him enter upon you, for he is your uncle.' She said: 'Only the woman breastfed me, not the man.' He said: 'He is your uncle, so let him enter upon you.' (Tirmidhi: Bab ma ja'a fi laban al-fahl, no. 1148; Muslim: (2) Bab tahrim al-rada' min ma' al-fahl, no. 1445)
Proof (2) the saying of the Companion for establishing the prohibition of laban al-fahl: from Ibn Abbas, that he was asked about a man who had two women servants: one breastfed a girl and the other breastfed a boy. Is it permissible for the boy to marry the girl? He said: 'No, the milk of the stallion is one.' (Tirmidhi: Bab ma ja'a fi laban al-fahl, no. 1149)
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage addresses the concept of laban al-fahl (milk of the stallion), which refers to the milk produced by a woman that is attributed to her husband (the 'fahl' or 'stallion') for legal purposes. The ruling: if a woman breastfeeds a girl, then that girl becomes mahram (prohibited to marry) to the woman's husband, the husband's father, and his sons. The husband himself becomes a foster-father to the girl. The proofs are a hadith from Aisha where the Prophet confirmed that the husband of the breastfeeding woman is considered a foster-uncle, and a saying of Ibn Abbas stating that if two children are breastfed by two different women but both women are married to the same man, then the children are foster-siblings due to the common 'milk of the stallion' and cannot marry. This establishes that the husband's role in creating fosterage relations is significant: the milk is linked to him even though he is not the direct source.

Key Terms
لبن الفحل (laban al-faḥl): Milk produced by a woman due to her husband's sexual relationship, legally attributed to the husband for determining fosterage relations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling of laban al-fahl according to the Hanafi school?
A) It establishes no prohibition; only the woman's milk matters.
B) It establishes prohibition: the girl becomes haram to the husband, his father, and his sons.
C) It only applies if the husband himself breastfeeds.
D) It makes the girl mahram to the breastfeeding woman's brother.

Key Takeaway
The milk of the husband (laban al-fahl) creates permanent fosterage prohibitions, making the husband a foster-father and his male ascendants/descendants mahram to the breastfed child.

Two Infants Sharing the Same Breast Become Foster Siblings
Ruling with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on foster-sibling relationship when two infants share the same breast and identify the proof from the hadith.

Core Idea
Sharing the same breast milk during infancy creates a permanent prohibition of marriage.

In this lesson, we examine a clear ruling from al-Quduri: if two infants (a boy and a girl) both breastfeed from the same woman during the recognized breastfeeding period, they become foster-siblings. This makes marriage between them permanently prohibited. The proof comes from a hadith where Zainab bint Abi Salama explains that she and Abu Salama were foster-siblings because they were both breastfed by Thuwaybah. This ruling is based on the general principle that fosterage creates the same prohibitions as lineage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The text states that any two infants who shared one breast during the breastfeeding period cannot marry each other.
The ruling is unconditional regarding the order of feeding.
2
Determine the legal effect
They become foster-siblings, making marriage prohibited (haram) and invalid.
The prohibition is analogous to blood siblingship.
3
Examine the proof
The hadith of Zainab bint Abi Salama (Bukhari) shows that sharing the same wet nurse creates siblinghood; she declared Abu Salama as her foster-brother.
The hadith is a dalil naqli of ahad status.
4
Apply the condition
Both infants must have been breastfed by the same woman during the period of rada' (under two years). The specific timing or breast is not critical; the shared milk is key.
The Hanafi school holds that any amount of milk reaching the stomach creates the prohibition.
5
Note the scope
This applies regardless of whether the infants are from the same mother or different mothers; the crucial factor is the shared milk from the same woman.
The rule is based on the generality of the hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَكُلُّ صَبِيَّيْنِ اجْتَمَعَا عَلَى ثَدْيِ وَاحِدٍ فِي مُدَّةِ الرَّضَاعِ لَمْ يَجُزْ لِأَحَدِهِمَا أَنْ يَتَزَوَّجَ بِالْآخَرِ

دوجه (۱) قول الصحابية لثبوت وَكُلُّ صَبِيَّيْنِ اجْتَمَعَا أَنَّ زَيْنَبَ ابْنَةَ أَبِي سَلَمَةَ أَخْبَرَتْهُ: ٠٠٠ إِنَّهَا لابْنَةُ أَخِي مِنَ الرَّضَاعَةِ ، أَرْضَعَتْني وَأَبَاسَلَمَةَ ثُوَيْبَةُ، فَلَا تَعْرِضْنَ عَلَيَّ بَنَاتِكُنَّ وَلَا أَخَوَاتِكُنَّ» (بخاري: با وأمهاتكم اللاتي أرضعنكم ويحرم من الرضاعة ما يحرم من النسب، 5101)
And any two infants who shared one breast during the breastfeeding period, it is not permissible for one of them to marry the other.
Proof (1) the saying of the female Companion for establishing that two infants who shared: that Zainab bint Abi Salama informed him: ... 'She is the daughter of my foster-brother; Thuwaybah breastfed me and Abu Salama, so do not propose to me your daughters nor your sisters.' (Bukhari: Bab 'O your mothers who breastfed you...' no. 5101)
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage states that if two infants (a boy and a girl) both breastfeed from the same breast during the legally recognized breastfeeding period, they become foster-siblings and are therefore prohibited from marrying each other. The proof is a narration from Zainab bint Abi Salama, who was breastfed by Thuwaybah along with Abu Salama; because they had shared the same milk, Abu Salama was her foster-brother, and she told the Prophet's wives not to propose their relatives to her because she was already related to them through fosterage. This ruling applies regardless of whether the two children are from the same mother or different mothers; the key is that they fed from the same woman (and the same breast, though 'same breast' is often interpreted as 'same milk' from the same woman). The period of breastfeeding is the same two years discussed earlier.

Key Terms
صبي (ṣabiyy): An infant or young child still within the breastfeeding period (under two years)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a baby boy and a baby girl both breastfeed from the same woman during her period of lactation, can they marry each other when they grow up?
A) Yes, they are not blood relatives
B) No, they become foster siblings and marriage is prohibited
C) Yes, if they did not feed simultaneously
D) It is makruh but not haram

Key Takeaway
Any two infants who share the same woman's milk during the breastfeeding period become foster-siblings, and marriage between them is permanently prohibited.

Zihar – Prohibition and Expiation
Definition and ruling of zihar with Quranic and hadith proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of zihar, list the three steps of expiation in order, and explain the consequence if intercourse occurs before expiation.

Core Idea
Zihar forbids intimacy until expiation; one expiation covers even if intimacy precedes it.

Zihar was a pre-Islamic practice that Islam abolished. The Quran directly addresses it in Surah al-Mujadilah. This lesson unpacks the definition, the immediate prohibition, and the sequential expiation required to remove the bar. We'll also see a hadith confirming that premature intercourse does not multiply the expiation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is zihar? The husband says to his wife 'You are to me like the back of my mother.' This makes her forbidden for intercourse, touching, and kissing until expiation is performed.
Zihar is not divorce; the marriage remains, but intimacy is temporarily prohibited.
2
Locate the primary proof
The Quranic verse (58:3-4) is the main evidence. It commands freeing a slave, then fasting two months, then feeding sixty poor – all before physical contact.
The verse uses imperative forms indicating obligation.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'fatahriru raqabah' shows obligation (wujub). The sequence ('then if he cannot...') indicates a descending order; one must attempt the first before moving to the next.
Hanafi usul treats commands as obligations unless otherwise specified.
4
Examine the secondary ruling
If the husband commits intimacy before expiating, the hadith of Salamah ibn Sakhr teaches that only one expiation is needed, plus repentance.
The single expiation suffices; it is not repeated for the violation.
5
Confirm the scope
The wife must be in a valid marriage. The utterance of the specific words constitutes the act (rukn). The expiation is wajib (obligatory) to lift the prohibition.
All schools agree on these fundamentals; Hanafi details align with the Quran and Sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الظُّهَارِ قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللهُ - إِذَا قَالَ الرَّجُلُ لِامْرَأَتِهِ أَنْتِ عَلَىَ كَظَهْر أُمّي فَقَدْ حَرُمْت عَلَيْهِ وَلَا يَحِلُّ لَهُ وَطْؤُهَا وَلَا لَمْسُهَا وَلَا تَقْبِيلُهَا حَتَّى يُكَفِّرَ عَنْ ظِهَارِهِ : فَإِنْ وَطِئَهَا قَبْلَ أَنْ يُكَفِّرَ اسْتَغْفَرَ اللَّهَ تَعَالَى وَلَا شَيْءَ عَلَيْهِ غَيْرُ الْكَفَّارَةِ الْأُولَى وجه: (1) الآية لثبوت إِذَا قَالَ الرَّجُلُ لِامْرَأَتِهِ أَنْتِ عَلَيَّ كَهْرٍ أَمِي \ ﴿وَالَّذِينَ يُظْهِرُونَ مِن ج نِّسَآبِهِمْ ثُمَّ يَعُودُونَ لِمَا قَالُواْ فَتَحْرِيرُ رَقَبَةٍ مِّن قَبْلِ أَن يَتَمَاسَّأْ ذَلِكُمْ تُوعَظُونَ بِهِ وَاللَّهُ بِمَا تَعْمَلُونَ خَبِيرٌ فَمَن لَّمْ يَجِدْ فَصِيَامُ شَهْرَيْنِ مُتَتَابِعَيْنِ مِن قَبْلِ أَن يَتَمَاسَّا فَمَن لَّمْ يَسْتَطِعْ فَإِطْعَامُ سِتِّينَ مِسْكِينَا) (القرآن سورة المجادلة58،الأية، نمبر 3/4) وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت إذَا قَالَ الرَّجُلُ لِامْرَأَتِهِ أَنْتِ عَلَيَّ كَظَهْرٍ أُمِّي عَنْ خُوَلَةَ بِنْتِ مَالِكِ بْنِ ثَعْلَبَةَ قَالَتْ: «ظَاهَرَ مِنّي زَوْجِي أَوْسُ بْنُ الصَّامِتِ فَجِنْتُ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَشْكُو إِلَيْهِ، وَرَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يُجَادِلُنِي فِيهِ، وَيَقُولُ: اتَّقِي اللَّهَ فَإِنَّهُ ابْنُ عَمِّكِ فَمَا بَرِحْتُ حَتَّى نَزَلَ الْقُرْآنُ {قَدْ سَمِعَ اللَّهُ قَوْلَ الَّتِي تُجَادِلُكَ فِي زَوْجِهَا إِلَى الْفَرْضِ فَقَالَ: يُعْتِقُ رَقَبَةً قَالَتْ: لَا يَجِدُ قَالَ: فَيَصُومُ شَهْرَيْنِ مُتَتَابِعَيْنِ قَالَتْ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ إِنَّهُ شَيْخٌ كَبِيرٌ مَا بِهِ مِنْ صِيَامٍ قَالَ: فَلْيُطْعِمْ سِتِينَ مِسْكِينًا قَالَتْ: مَا عِنْدَهُ مِنْ شَيْءٍ يَتَصَدَّقُ بِهِ قَالَتْ: فَأَتِيَ سَاعَتَئِذٍ بِعَرَقٍ مِنْ تَمرٍ قُلْتُ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ فَإِنِّي أُعِينُهُ بِعَرَقٍ آخَرَ قَالَ: قَدْ أَحْسَنْتِ اذْهَبِي فَأَطْعِمِي بِمَا عَنْهُ سِتِّينَ مِسْكِينًا، وَارْجِعِي إِلَى ابْنِ عَمِّكِ» قَالَ: وَالْعَرَقُ سِتُّونَ صَاعًا ( ابوداؤد شریف: باب في الظهار،نمبر 2214.) وجه (۳) قول التابعى لثبوت إذَا قَالَ الرَّجُلُ لِامْرَأَتِهِ أَنْتِ عَلَيَّ كَفَهْرٍ أُمِّي قُلْتُ لِعَطَاءِ : الظَّهَارُ هُوَ أَنْ يَقُولَ: هِيَ عَلَيَّ كَأُمِّي؟ قَالَ : نَعَمْ، هُوَ (مصنف عبدالرزاق: باب كيف الظهار؟،11476) ل وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ وَطِئَهَا قَبْلَ أَنْ يُكَفِّرَ اسْتَغْفَرَ اللَّهَ \ عَنْ سَلَمَةَ بْنِ صَخْرٍ البَيَاضِيِّ، عَنْ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فِي المُظَاهِرِ يُوَاقِعُ قَبْلَ أَنْ يُكَفِّرَ قَالَ: «كَفَّارَةٌ وَاحِدَةً» (سنن ترمذي شريف: باب ما جاء في المظاهر يواقع قبل أن يكفر، نمبر 1198) اصول: اپنی بیوی کو محرم عورت کی پیٹھ سے تشبیہ دینا، یعنی جیسے محرم عورتوں کی پیٹھ سے استفادہ حرام ہے اسی طرح بیوی کی پیٹھ سے استفادہ حرام ہے۔
The Book of Zihar. He (the author) said - may Allah have mercy on him -: When a man says to his wife, 'You are to me like the back of my mother,' then she becomes forbidden to him. It is not permissible for him to have intercourse with her, nor to touch her, nor to kiss her until he makes expiation for his zihar. If he has intercourse with her before making expiation, he should seek forgiveness from Allah, the Exalted, and nothing is required from him other than the first expiation. Proof (1): The verse to establish when a man says to his wife 'You are to me like the back of my mother': {And those who make zihar from their wives and then retract what they said, then the freeing of a slave before they touch each other...} (Quran, Surah al-Mujadilah 58:3-4) Proof (2): The hadith to establish when a man says to his wife 'You are to me like the back of my mother': from Khawlah bint Malik ibn Tha'labah who said: 'My husband Aws ibn al-Samit made zihar with me, so I came to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) complaining to him, and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) argued with me about him, saying: Fear Allah, for he is your cousin. I did not leave until the Quran was revealed: {Indeed Allah has heard the statement of the one who argues with you concerning her husband...} until the obligation. He said: He should free a slave. She said: He does not have [the means]. He said: Then let him fast two consecutive months. She said: O Messenger of Allah, he is an old man; he cannot fast. He said: Then let him feed sixty poor people. She said: He has nothing to give in charity. She said: Then at that moment a basket of dates was brought. I said: O Messenger of Allah, I will help him with another basket. He said: You have done well; go and feed with it sixty poor people from him, and return to your cousin.' He said: And the basket was sixty sa' (Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-Zihar, no. 2214). Proof (3): The saying of the tabi'i to establish when a man says to his wife 'You are to me like the back of my mother': I said to 'Ata: 'Is zihar that he says: 'She is like my mother'?' He said: 'Yes, it is.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab Kayfa al-Zihar, no. 11476) Proof (1): The hadith to establish if he has intercourse before expiating: from Salamah ibn Sakhr al-Bayadi from the Prophet (peace be upon him) concerning the one who makes zihar and has intercourse before expiating: he said: 'One expiation.' (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi al-muzahir yuwagi' qabl an yukaffir, no. 1198) Principle: Comparing one's wife to the back of a prohibited woman (such as mother) means that just as benefiting from the back of a prohibited woman is forbidden, so benefiting from the wife's back is forbidden.
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage introduces the Book of Zihar, a form of prohibited speech in which a husband compares his wife to a female relative within the prohibited degrees (like his mother), making her temporarily forbidden to him. The ruling is a clear prohibition of marital relations until expiation. The primary proof is the Quranic verses from Surah al-Mujadilah (58:3-4), which prescribe a sequential expiation: freeing a slave, if unable then fasting two consecutive months, and if unable then feeding sixty poor people. The passage also includes the famous hadith of Khawlah bint Malik, which provides the occasion of revelation and confirms the ruling. Additionally, it cites the practice of the Companion 'Ata' defining zihar. A secondary ruling: if the husband has intercourse before expiating, he must seek forgiveness but only one expiation is required (as per the hadith of Salamah ibn Sakhr). The principle explains that the prohibition is analogized to the sanctity of a mahram. This passage is a foundational text for the Hanafi understanding of zihar.

Key Terms
ظِهَار (zihar): A pre-Islamic practice wherein a husband says to his wife 'You are to me like the back of my mother,' making her forbidden until expiation.
كَفَّارَة (kaffarah): The expiation required for zihar: freeing a slave, fasting two months, or feeding sixty poor.
مُظَاهِر (muzahir): A man who performs zihar on his wife.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the required expiation for zihar if the husband cannot fast two consecutive months?
A) Feed 60 poor people
B) Give charity of 100 dirhams
C) Free two slaves
D) Fast one month

Key Takeaway
Zihar prohibits intimacy until the sequential expiation is fulfilled; one expiation suffices even if intimacy precedes it.

10 min
Kaffarat al-Zihar: Expiation Options and Valid Slaves
States the three-tiered expiation for zihar and conditions of the slave to be freed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three-tiered expiation for zihar and identify which slaves are valid for expiation according to Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
The expiation of zihar follows a fixed order: free a slave, fast two months, or feed sixty poor, each only if the previous is impossible.

In this passage from al-Quduri's Kitab al-Zihar, we learn the precise obligations of a husband who pronounces zihar. The Quranic verses (58:3-4) establish a sequential expiation, and the author explains both the general rule and the specific conditions for the type of slave that may be freed. Understanding these conditions is crucial for the validity of expiation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Zihar triggers a wajib expiation before resuming marital relations. Identify the hukm level: wajib, not fard, due to the Hanafi principle that the imperative from a zanni dalil indicates obligation.
2
Trace the three-tiered sequence
The expiation must be performed in order: free a slave; if unable, fast two consecutive months; if unable, feed sixty poor. Each option is only available if the previous is impossible.
The sequence is mandatory; skipping a step without inability invalidates the expiation.
3
Identify the conditions of a valid slave
Not all slaves are acceptable. The text lists disqualifications: blindness, missing both hands or feet, missing both thumbs, insanity. It also permits the deaf, any gender, age, Muslim or non-Muslim.
The hadith from al-Bara' on sacrificial animals is used by analogy to establish that severe defects disqualify.
4
Analyze the special case of mukatab and the Shafi'i dispute
A mukatab who has paid part of his kitaba is invalid; one who has paid nothing is valid. The Hanafi proof is from Umm Salama's hadith, while the Shafi'i proof is from 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb. The Hanafi response distinguishes degrees of slavery.
The practical consequence (thamarah) is that a Hanafi may free a mukatab with no payments, a Shafi'i may not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الظَّهَارِ
فَصْلٌ فِي كَفَّارَةِ الظَّهَارِ
وَكَفَّارَةُ الظَّهَارِ عِتْقُ رَقَبَةٍ فَإِنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ صَامَ شَهْرَيْنِ مُتَتَابِعَيْنِ فَإِنْ لَمْ يَسْتَطِعْ فَإِطْعَامُ سِتِّينَ مِسْكِينًا كُلُّ ذَلِكَ قَبْلَ الْمَسِيسِ ، وَيُجْزِي فِي الْعِتْقِ الرَّقَبَةُ الْمُسْلِمَةُ وَالْكَافِرَةُ وَالذَّكَرُ وَالْأُنْثَى وَالصَّغِيرُ وَالْكَبِيرُ وَلَا تَجُوزُ الْعَمْيَاءُ وَلَا مَقْطُوعَةُ الْيَدَيْنِ أَوْ الرِّجْلَيْنِ وَيَجُوزُ الْأَصَمُ وَلَا يَجُوزُ مَقْطُوعُ إِبْهَامَيْ الْيَدَيْنِ وَلَا الْمَجْنُونُ الَّذِي لَا يَعْقِلُ وَلَا يَجُوزُ عِتْقُ الْمُدَبَّرِ وَأُمُّ الْوَلَدِ وَلَا الْمُكَاتَبُ الَّذِي أَدَّى بَعْضَ الْمَالِ فَإِنْ أَعْتَقَ مُكَاتَبًا لَمْ يُؤَدِّ شَيْئًا جَازَ 
لوجه: (1) الآية لثبوت وَكَفَّارَةُ الظَّهَارِ عِتْقُ رَقَبَةٍ 
وَالَّذِينَ يُظْهِرُونَ مِن نِّسَائِهِمْ ثُمَّ يَعُودُونَ لِمَا قَالُوا فَتَحْرِيرُ رَقَبَةٍ مِّن قَبْلِ أَن يَتَمَاسَّا ذَلِكُمْ تُوعَظُونَ بِهِ وَاللَّهُ بِمَا تَعْمَلُونَ خَبِيرٌ فَمَن لَّمْ يَجِدْ فَصِيَامُ شَهْرَيْنِ مُتَتَابِعَيْنِ مِن قَبْلِ أَن يَتَمَاسَّا فَمَن لَّمْ يَسْتَطِعْ فَإِطْعَامُ سِتِّينَ مِسْكِينًا﴾ (القرآن) سورة المجادلة58، الآية، نمبر 3/4 
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ مَقْطُوعُ إِبْهَامَيْ الْيَدَيْنِ 
«سَأَلْتُ الْبَرَاءَ بْنَ عَازِبٍ مَا لَا يَجُوزُ فِي الْأَضَاحِيِّ؟ فَقَالَ: قَامَ فِينَا رَسُولُ اللهِ ، وَأَصَابِعِي أَقْصَرُ مِنْ أَصَابِعِهِ، وَأَنَامِلِي أَقْصَرُ مِنْ أَنَامِلِهِ فَقَالَ: أَرْبَعٌ لَا تَجُوزُ فِي الْأَضَاحِيّ: الْعَوْرَاءُ بَيِّنٌ عَوَرُهَا، وَالْمَرِيضَةُ بَيِّنٌ مَرَضُهَا، وَالْعَرْجَاءُ بَيِّنْ ظَلْعُهَا، وَالْكَسِيرُ الَّتِي لَا تَنْقَى»(ابوداؤد شريف: باب ما يكره من الضحايا،نمر 2802) 
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلا يَجُوزُ عِتْقَ الْمُدَبَّر وَأُمُّ الْوَلَدِ 
سَمِعْتُ أُمَّ سَلَمَةَ تَقُولُ: «قَالَ لَنَا رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: إِذَا كَانَ لِإِحْدَاكُنَّ مُكَاتَبٌ فَكَانَ عِنْدَهُ مَا يُؤَدِّي فَلْتَحْتَجِبْ مِنْهُ.» (ابوداؤد شريف: باب في المكاتب يؤدي بعض كتابته فيعجز أو يموت،نمر 3928) 
وجه : (۱) دليل الشافعى الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ عِتْقُ الْمُدَبَّرِ وَأُمُّ الْوَلَدِ اعَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ شُعَيْبٍ ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ ، عَنْ جَدِهِ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «الْمُكَاتَبُ عَبْدٌ مَا بَقِيَ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ كِتَابَتِهِ دِرْهَمْ.»(ابوداؤد شريف : باب في المكاتب يؤدي بعض كتابته فيعجز أو يموت،نمر 3926)
أصول: ظہار کا کفارہ میں سب سے اول غلام آزاد کرے اگر ممکن نہ ہو تو دوماہ مسلسل روزے ، ورنہ ساٹھ مسکینوں کو کھلائے۔
Book of Zihar. Chapter on the expiation of Zihar. The expiation of Zihar is freeing a slave. If he does not find one, he fasts two consecutive months. If he is unable, then feeding sixty poor people. All of that before touching. And for the freeing, the slave, Muslim or disbeliever, male or female, young or old is sufficient. The blind woman is not permissible, nor one cut off of both hands or both feet. The deaf is permissible. One cut off of both thumbs is not permissible, nor the insane one who does not understand. Freeing the mudabbar and umm al-walad is not permissible, nor the mukatab who has paid some of the money. But if he frees a mukatab who has not paid anything, it is permissible. Proof: (1) The verse for establishing 'the expiation of Zihar is freeing a slave': 'And those who pronounce zihar from their wives and then return to what they said, then the freeing of a slave before they touch each other...' (Quran 58:3-4). Proof: (1) The hadith for establishing 'one cut off of both thumbs is not permissible': 'I asked al-Bara' ibn 'Azib what is not permissible in sacrifices? He said: The Messenger of Allah stood among us... four are not permissible in sacrifices: the obviously blind, the obviously sick, the obviously lame, and the broken that has no marrow.' (Abu Dawud). Proof: (1) The hadith for establishing 'freeing the mudabbar and umm al-walad is not permissible': 'I heard Umm Salama say: The Messenger of Allah said to us: When one of you has a mukatab and he has what he can pay, then she should veil from him.' (Abu Dawud). Proof: (1) The proof of al-Shafi'i for establishing 'freeing the mudabbar and umm al-walad is not permissible' from 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather from the Prophet: 'The mukatab is a slave as long as a dirham of his kitaba remains.' (Abu Dawud). Principle: In the expiation of Zihar, first free a slave; if not possible, then fast two months consecutively; otherwise feed sixty poor people.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Kitab al-Zihar of al-Quduri. It opens with the three-tiered expiation for zihar: freeing a slave, fasting two consecutive months, or feeding sixty poor people. The author stresses that all three must be completed before marital intercourse. Then he specifies which slaves are acceptable for the first option: any slave, Muslim or non-Muslim, male or female, young or old, and even a deaf slave, is sufficient. However, slaves with major disabilities are excluded: the blind, those missing both hands or feet, those missing both thumbs (because this severely impairs work), and the insane. The mudabbar (a slave promised freedom upon the owner's death) and umm al-walad (a slave mother of her owner's child) are also not valid for expiation because their freedom is already determined. A mukatab (a slave under a contract of emancipation) who has paid part of his kitaba is not acceptable because he still owes; but a mukatab who has paid nothing can be freed and counts for expiation. The author then provides hadith proofs: the Quranic verse (58:3-4) for the basic ruling; a hadith from al-Bara' about sacrificial animals (used by analogy to show that severe defects disqualify); a hadith from Umm Salama indicating that a mukatab with means is no longer fully a slave; and a hadith from 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb (which is a proof for al-Shafi'i) stating that a mukatab remains a slave as long as any debt remains, which the Hanafis accept but interpret differently. The Urdu summary reiterates the order of expiation.

Key Terms
ظهار (zihar): A form of divorce-like pronouncement where a husband says to his wife 'You are to me like the back of my mother', making her temporarily prohibited until expiation is performed.
كفارة (kaffarah): An expiatory act required to remove a prohibition incurred by a sin or legal impediment. In zihar, it is obligatory before resuming marital relations.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave whom the owner has promised to free upon the owner's death. Such a slave is considered partially free and thus cannot be used for kaffarah.
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave under a contract (kitaba) to purchase his emancipation by paying installments to his owner. The status changes depending on payments made.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi fiqh as stated in al-Quduri, which of the following slaves is valid for the expiation of zihar?
A) A blind female slave
B) A deaf male slave
C) A slave missing both thumbs
D) A mukatab who has paid half of his kitaba

Key Takeaway
The expiation of zihar is wajib in a fixed order, and only slaves without major disabilities or pending emancipation are valid for freeing.

6 min
Zihar Kaffarah: Intercourse During Expiation and Multiple Obligations
Ruling with proof from Quran and usul principle

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intercourse during zihar kaffarah and apply the principle of same genus (jins) to multiple kaffarahs.

Core Idea
You do not need to specify which expiation act belongs to which zihar when both are of the same type.

This lesson explores two key rulings from Kitab al-Zihar. First, if a man has intercourse with his wife while completing his kaffarah (expiation) for zihar by feeding sixty poor people, he does not need to restart the feeding. Second, when multiple zihar kaffarahs are due, acts of the same type—like freeing two slaves or fasting four months—fulfill all obligations without specifying which act covers which kaffarah. The proof is the Quranic verse on kaffarah, and the underlying legal maxim (usul) is that when the genus (jins) is identical, specific designation is unnecessary; later allocation is permissible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and rulings
The first ruling: intercourse during the feeding period of zihar kaffarah does not invalidate the ongoing kaffarah; no restart is required. The second ruling: multiple kaffarahs of zihar can be satisfied by one type of act without specifying which act is for which kaffarah.
These rulings apply specifically to zihar kaffarah, not necessarily to other types of kaffarah.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The proof cited is Quran 58:4, which prescribes feeding sixty poor people as an alternative to freeing a slave for those unable. This verse establishes the permissibility of feeding as an expiation, and the ruling on multiple kaffarahs is derived by qiyas on the principle of same genus.
The dalil is qat'i al-thubut (certain transmission) but zanni al-dalala (speculative meaning) regarding the multiple kaffarah detail.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (legal inference)
The verse allows feeding as a valid kaffarah act. The Hanafi jurists extend the permissibility to multiple obligations: since the act is of the same genus (e.g., feeding sixty poor is the same type regardless of which zihar it belongs to), no separate intention is required for each.
The reasoning relies on the usul maxim: 'If the genus is the same, specific designation is not necessary.'
4
Note the ikhtilaf (scholarly difference)
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) require a specific intention for each kaffarah because each obligation is distinct. The Hanafi school disagrees, holding that general intention suffices when the acts are of the same type.
This difference stems from different interpretations of the role of intention (niyyah) in expiation.
5
Apply the usul principle
The underlying principle: when multiple obligations of the same type are due, one can fulfill them with acts of that type without assigning each act to a specific obligation. This applies to freeing, fasting, or feeding.
However, if obligations are of different types (e.g., one zihar and one yamin), they cannot be combined arbitrarily.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ قَرَبَ الَّتِي ظَاهَرَ مِنْهَا فِي خِلَالِ الْإِطْعَامِ لَمْ يَسْتَأْنِفْ كِتَابُ الظُّهَارِ ا وَمَنْ وَجَبَ عَلَيْهِ كَفَّارَتَا ظِهَارٍ فَأَعْتَقَ رَقَبَتَيْنِ لَا يَنْوِي إِحْدَاهُمَا بِعَيْنِهَا جَازَ عَنْهُمَا وَكَذَلِكَ إِنْ صَامَ أَرْبَعَةَ أَشْهُرٍ أَوْ أَطْعَمَ مِائَةً وَعِشْرِينَ مِسْكِينًا جَازَ وَإِنْ أَعْتَقَ رَقَبَةً وَاحِدَةً وَصَامَ شَهْرَيْنِ جَازَ أَنْ يَجْعَلَ ذَلِكَ عَنْ أَيْهِمَا شَاءَ ل وجه : (۱) الآية لثبوت أَفَمَن لَّمْ يَسْتَطِعْ فَإِطْعَامُ سِتِّينَ مِسْكِينًا﴾(القرآن سورة المجادلة58، الآية، نمبر 4) اصول: ایک ہی قسم کے دو کفارے ہوں اور ایک جنس کے دو غلام ہوں تو غلام کی تعیین ضروری نہیں ہے کہ کو نسا غلام کس کفارہ کا ہے، بلا تعیین کفارہ ادا ہو جائے گا۔ اصول: جنس ایک ہو تو خصوصی طور پر ہر ایک متعین کرنا ضروری نہیں، بعد میں تخصیص کرنا بھی کافی ہو جائے
If he has intercourse with the woman from whom he has performed zihar during the feeding [period], he does not start over. Book of Zihar. And whoever is obligated with two kaffarahs of zihar and frees two slaves without intending each one specifically, it suffices for both. Similarly, if he fasts four months or feeds one hundred and twenty poor persons, it suffices. And if he frees one slave and fasts two months, he may assign that to whichever of the two he wishes. For proof: (1) The verse for establishing: 'But he who cannot [find a slave] then the feeding of sixty poor people' (Quran 58:4). Principle: If there are two kaffarahs of the same type and two slaves of the same kind, then specifying which slave is for which kaffarah is not necessary; the kaffarah will be fulfilled without specification. Principle: If the type is the same, then specifying each one individually is not necessary; later specification is also sufficient.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Zihar contains two rulings with their underlying principle. First, if a man who has declared zihar (a pre-Islamic form of divorce) and is in the process of performing the kaffarah (expiation) by feeding sixty poor people has intercourse with his wife during that feeding period, he does not need to restart the kaffarah from the beginning; it remains valid. Second, concerning multiple kaffarahs: if a person owes two separate kaffarahs of zihar (e.g., for two different declarations) and performs acts of the same type (e.g., freeing two slaves, fasting four months, or feeding 120 poor), he does not need to specify which act is for which kaffarah. The general intention suffices. Similarly, if he performs one act and another (e.g., freeing one slave and fasting two months), he may assign the combination to either kaffarah as he wishes. The proof cited is the Quranic verse (58:4) that prescribes the kaffarah sequence. The two Urdu principles (usool) explain the legal maxim: when obligations are of the same genus (jins), specific designation is not required; later allocation is permissible.

Key Terms
ظهار (zihar): A pre-Islamic form of divorce where a man says to his wife 'You are like my mother's back', which obligates kaffarah before resuming marital relations.
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation required for certain violations, such as zihar; options include freeing a slave, fasting two months, or feeding sixty poor.
إطعام (it'am): Feeding as a form of kaffarah; feeding sixty poor people is the third option for zihar expiation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, if a man owes two kaffarahs of zihar and frees two slaves without specifying which slave is for which kaffarah, what is the ruling?
A) The kaffarahs are not fulfilled because intention is required for each.
B) It suffices for both because both slaves are of the same type.
C) He must free two additional slaves with specific intention.
D) He must combine freeing with fasting to fulfill them.

Key Takeaway
When multiple expiation obligations of the same type are due, the Hanafi school does not require specific designation; general intention and later allocation suffice.

Parents of Absent Child Not Liable for Spending His Wealth
Ruling on parents' spending from absent child's wealth without liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on parents spending from an absent child's wealth without liability, and identify the two hadith proofs that support this ruling.

Core Idea
Parents may spend from absent child's wealth without liability due to parental authority.

This passage from Al-Quduri addresses a practical question: when an adult son is away, can his parents use his wealth that they hold? The ruling is clear: they are not liable for repayment. The proofs come from two prophetic hadiths that establish parental authority and the principle of taking for family needs in a reasonable manner.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Spending from an absent child's wealth by parents. The hukm is that they are not liable (lā yadmanān), meaning it is permissible without obligation to repay.
The act is mubah (permissible) in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The author cites the hadith: 'أنتَ ومالُكَ لِأبيكَ' (You and your wealth belong to your father). Identify this as a prophetic hadith (Sunnah ahad).
This hadith is widely recorded in hadith collections.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'ومالك لأبيك' indicates that the wealth is under the father's authority. This grants the father, and by extension the mother, permission to use it without incurring liability.
The word 'لك' (to you) implies ownership/authority.
4
Locate the supporting dalil
The second hadith of Hind bint Utbah shows that a wife may take from her husband's wealth for family needs in a reasonable manner (bil-ma'rūf). This analogically supports parents taking from a child's wealth.
The condition 'لا إِلَّا بِالْمَعْرُوفِ' qualifies the permissibility.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
Although the text presents a clear Hanafi position, some other schools may hold parents liable for such spending. The Hanafi reliance on the hadith provides the preferred view.
The passage does not detail counterarguments, but cross-madhhab difference exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ كَانَ لِابْنِ الْغَائِبِ مَالٌ فِي يَدَيْ أَبَوَيْهِ فَأَنْفَقَا مِنْهُ لَمْ يَضْمَنَا. وَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم : «أَنْتَ وَمَالُكَ لِأَبِيكَ». وَعَنْ عَائِشَةَ قَالَتْ: جَاءَتْ هِنْدُ بِنْتُ عُتْبَةَ فَقَالَتْ: يَا رَسُولَ اللهِ إِنَّ أَبَا سُفْيَانَ رَجُلٌ مِسِّيكٌ فَهَلْ عَلَيَّ حَرَجٌ أَنْ أُطْعِمَ مِنَ الَّذِي لَهُ عِيَالَنَا؟ قَالَ: «لَا إِلَّا بِالْمَعْرُوفِ».
And if the absent son has wealth in the hands of his parents and they spend from it, they are not liable. And the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'You and your wealth belong to your father.' And from Aisha, she said: Hind bint Utbah came and said: O Messenger of Allah, Abu Sufyan is a stingy man; is there any sin upon me if I feed our children from his wealth? He said: 'No, but in a reasonable manner.'
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This ruling addresses when an adult son is absent (غائب) and his parents have his wealth in their possession. If they spend from it for their own maintenance, they are not liable (لا يضمنان) to repay. The evidence: the hadith 'You and your wealth belong to your father' which indicates the father's authority over the child's wealth. Additionally, the hadith of Hind shows that a wife may take from her husband's wealth for family needs in a reasonable manner (بالمعروف), analogically applying to parents. This is based on the principle that maintenance is reciprocal and parents' authority justifies such spending.

Key Terms
غائب (gha'ib): A person who is absent, not present to manage his own affairs.
ضمان (daman): Liability, responsibility for repayment or compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is a parent not liable for spending from their absent child's wealth?
A) When they spend it for their own maintenance
B) When they buy luxury items
C) When they save it
D) When they give it as charity

Key Takeaway
Parents may spend from absent child's wealth without liability, supported by the hadith 'you and your wealth belong to your father'.

Master's Obligation to Maintain Slaves and Options Upon Refusal
Ruling on master's duty to maintain slaves and options if he refuses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the master's wajib duty to maintain his slave and explain the two legal outcomes when the master refuses.

Core Idea
A master must maintain his slave; if he refuses, the slave earns if able, otherwise the master is forced to provide or sell.

The duty of a master to provide for his slaves is a clear wajib in the Hanafi school. This passage from al-Quduri outlines that duty and details what happens if the master refuses. Understanding this ruling clarifies that slaves have legal rights to basic necessities, and the master cannot simply neglect them without consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling
State that the master (mawla) is obligated to provide maintenance (nafaqa) for his male and female slaves. Note that this is a wajib duty.
The obligation covers food and clothing as shown in the hadith.
2
Analyze the first scenario of refusal
If the master refuses and the slave has earning ability (kasb), the slave works and spends on himself. The master is not forced to pay.
Kasb includes any lawful work the slave can perform.
3
Analyze the second scenario of refusal
If the slave has no kasb, the master is compelled either to provide maintenance or to sell the slave.
Selling transfers the duty to another master who can provide.
4
Connect to the evidence
The hadith from the Prophet (ﷺ) and the narration of Abu Dharr establish the right to food and clothing and humane treatment.
The imperative form in the hadith indicates wujub in Hanafi usul.

وَعَلَى الْمَوْلَى أَنْ يُنْفِقَ عَلَى عَبْدِهِ وَأَمَتِهِ. فَإِنِ امْتَنَعَ وَكَانَ لَهُمَا كَسْبٌ اكْتَسَبَا وَأَنْفَقَا عَلَى أَنْفُسِهِمَا. فَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُمَا كَسْبٌ أُجْبِرَ الْمَوْلَى عَلَى نَفَقَتِهِمَا أَوْ بَيْعِهِمَا. وَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «لِلْمَمْلُوكِ طَعَامُهُ وَكِسْوَتُهُ، وَلَا يُكَلَّفُ مِنَ الْعَمَلِ إِلَّا مَا يُطِيقُ». وَعَنْ أَبِي ذَرٍّ: «إِنَّ إِخْوَانَكُمْ خَوَلُكُمْ جَعَلَهُمُ اللَّهُ تَحْتَ أَيْدِيكُمْ فَمَنْ كَانَ أَخُوهُ تَحْتَ يَدِهِ فَلْيُطْعِمْهُ مِمَّا يَأْكُلُ وَلْيُلْبِسْهُ مِمَّا يَلْبَسُ».
And the master must provide maintenance for his male and female slave. If he refuses, and they have ability to earn, they earn and spend on themselves. If they have no ability to earn, the master is compelled to provide for them or to sell them. And the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The slave has his food and clothing, and he is not tasked with work beyond his capacity.' And from Abu Dharr: 'Indeed your brothers are your dependents whom Allah has placed under your authority; so whoever has his brother under his authority should feed him from what he eats and clothe him from what he wears.'
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage addresses the master's duty to maintain slaves. The burden is on the master (المولى) to provide nafaqa (food, clothing) for both male (عبد) and female (أمة) slaves. If the master refuses, there are two scenarios: (1) if the slaves can earn (income), they may work and spend on themselves—the master is not forced to pay; (2) if they cannot earn, the master is compelled either to provide nafaqa or to sell them. The evidence: the hadith stating the slave has a right to food and clothing without being overburdened, and the hadith of Abu Dharr emphasizing humane treatment and equal provision. This ruling reflects the Hanafi view that maintenance of slaves is a duty (wajib) and that the master cannot neglect it without consequences.

Key Terms
مولى (mawla): Master, owner of a slave.
كسب (kasb): Earnings, ability to work and generate income.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a master refuses to maintain his slave and the slave can earn, what happens?
A) The master is forced to pay immediately
B) The slave earns and spends on himself
C) The slave is sold automatically
D) The slave becomes free

Key Takeaway
A master's duty to maintain his slave is wajib; if he refuses, the outcome depends on the slave's ability to earn.

Obligation of the Master to Provide Maintenance for Slaves
Establishes the master's duty to maintain slaves and the judge's role in enforcement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a master's duty to provide maintenance for slaves, apply the conditions that trigger the obligation, and explain the dalil (proof) using the hadith of Abu Dharr and the cat hadith.

Core Idea
A master must feed and clothe his slave; if he refuses and the slave cannot earn, the judge forces sale.

This passage from Al-Quduri's Kitab al-Nafaqat establishes a clear legal duty for masters to provide food and clothing to their male and female slaves. It not only states the ruling but also outlines the steps when a master refuses, and supplies two powerful hadith proofs—one direct command from the Prophet and an analogy from a cat's neglect. Understanding this ruling reveals the ethical and legal responsibility that ownership entails in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and its Legal Category
First, read the matn: 'It is upon the master to spend on his male slave and his female slave.' Note that this is phrased as an imperative. In Hanafi usul, al-amr yufidu al-wujub. So the ruling is that maintenance is wajib—an obligation, not merely recommended.
The hukm level is wajib, not fard, because the proof is from ahad hadith (zanni al-thubut).
2
Examine the Conditions and Two Scenarios
The passage then describes two scenarios when the master refuses: (1) if the slaves have earnings, they earn and spend on themselves; (2) if they have no earnings, the master is compelled either to provide or to sell them. Trace the condition: the obligation falls on the master only when the slave cannot earn.
This shows that the master's duty is secondary—the slave's own earnings take priority.
3
Analyse the First Proof — Hadith of Abu Dharr
The hadith contains the imperative: 'Let him feed him from what he eats, and clothe him from what he wears.' Identify the wajh al-dalalah: the imperative 'liyut'imhu' and 'liyulbis' indicate obligation. Also note the fairness requirement—the slave should be maintained at the same level as the master.
This hadith is found in Bukhari and Muslim—it is authentic.
4
Analyse the Second Proof — Hadith of the Cat (Qiyas)
The hadith of the woman punished for neglecting a cat is used as a qiyas: if neglecting an animal leads to punishment, then neglecting a human slave (who is nobler) must be even more severe. This reinforces the obligation and the consequence of refusal.
This is an example of qiyas jaliy (clear analogy) drawn from a textual indication.
5
Summarise the Practical Consequence
If the master persistently refuses to maintain the slave and the slave cannot earn, the judge intervenes. The judge compels the master either to provide maintenance or to sell the slave. The slave is not set free—rather, the property is transferred to someone who will fulfill the duty.
This preserves the master's property rights while ensuring the slave's welfare.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ النَّفَقَاتِ
وَعَلَى الْمَوْلَى أَنْ يُنْفِقَ عَلَى عَبْدِهِ وَأَمَتِهِ. فَإِنْ امْتَنَعَ وَكَانَ لَهُمَا كَسْبٌ اكْتَسَبَا وَأَنْفَقَا عَلَى أَنْفُسِهِمَا. فَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُمَا كَسْبٌ أُجْبِرَ الْمَوْلَى عَلَى نَفَقَتِهِمَا أَوْ بَيْعِهِمَا شُرَيْئًا.
الحديث لثبوت ذلك: عَنْ أَبِي ذَرٍّ الْغِفَارِيِّ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: رَأَيْتُ أَبَا ذَرٍّ وَعَلَيْهِ حُلَّةٌ، وَعَلَى غُلَامِهِ حُلَّةٌ، فَسَأَلْنَاهُ عَنْ ذَلِكَ، فَقَالَ: إِنِّي سَابَبْتُ رَجُلًا، فَشَكَانِي إِلَى النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم، فَقَالَ لِي النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم: أَعَيَّرَتَهُ بِأُمِّهِ؟ ثُمَّ قَالَ: إِنَّ إِخْوَانَكُمْ خَوَلُكُمْ، جَعَلَهُمُ اللهُ تَحْتَ أَيْدِيكُمْ، فَمَنْ كَانَ أَخُوهُ تَحْتَ يَدِهِ، فَلْيُطْعِمْهُ مِمَّا يَأْكُلُ، وَلْيُلْبِسْهُ مِمَّا يَلْبَسُ، وَلَا تُكَلِّفُوهُمْ مَا يَغْلِبُهُمْ، فَإِنْ كَلَّفْتُمُوهُمْ مَا يَغْلِبُهُمْ فَأَعِينُوهُمْ.
وَعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهُ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: "عُذِّبَتِ امْرَأَةٌ فِي هِرَّةٍ لَمْ تُطْعِمْهَا وَلَمْ تَسْقِهَا وَلَمْ تَتْرُكْهَا تَأْكُلُ مِنْ خَشَاشِ الْأَرْضِ".
أُصُول: كُلُّكُمْ رَاعٍ وَكُلُّكُمْ مَسْئُولٌ عَنْ رَعِيَّتِهِ. لِهَذَا كُلُّ مَنْ كَانَ نَاظِرًا وَتَحْتَهُ أَفْرَادٌ، حُرًّا كَانَ أَوْ عَبْدًا، فَعَلَيْهِ الْمَسْئُولِيَّةُ الْكَامِلَةُ.
أَصْل: إِذَا أَبَى الْمَوْلَى نَفَقَةَ مَمْلُوكِهِ وَلَمْ يَبِعْهُ، يُجْبَرُ عَلَى الْبَيْعِ.
أَصْل: مَنْ مَنَعَ الطَّعَامَ عَنِ الْحَيَوَانِ وَمَاتَ يَسْتَحِقُّ الْعَذَابَ، فَالْإِنْسَانُ أَشْرَفُ الْمَخْلُوقَاتِ، فَفِي الْأَوْلَى يَسْتَحِقُّ الْعَذَابَ إِذَا مَاتَ.
Book of Maintenance. It is upon the master to spend on his male slave and his female slave. If he refuses, and they have earnings, they earn and spend on themselves. If they have no earnings, the master is compelled to provide for them or sell them as a share (?). The hadith for proving that: from Abu Dharr al-Ghifari, may Allah be pleased with him, he said: I saw Abu Dharr wearing a cloak, and his slave wearing a cloak, so we asked him about that. He said: I insulted a man, and he complained to the Prophet, peace be upon him, so the Prophet said to me: Did you reproach him for his mother? Then he said: Indeed, your brothers are your dependents, Allah has placed them under your hands, so whoever has his brother under his hand, let him feed him from what he eats, and clothe him from what he wears, and do not burden them with what overwhelms them; if you burden them with what overwhelms them, then help them. And from Abu Hurairah, may Allah be pleased with him, that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: A woman was punished because of a cat; she did not feed it, nor give it drink, nor let it eat from the vermin of the earth. Principles: All of you are shepherds and all of you are responsible for your flock. Therefore, whoever is a guardian and has individuals under him, whether free or slave, has full responsibility. Principle: If the master refuses maintenance of his slave and does not sell him, he is compelled to sell. Principle: Whoever withholds food from an animal and it dies deserves punishment; so the human, who is the noblest of creation, is even more deserving of punishment if he dies.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the Book of Maintenance (Kitab al-Nafaqat) of Al-Quduri, with hadith proofs and Hanafi principles. The ruling states that it is obligatory (wajib) upon a master to provide food and clothing for his male and female slaves. If the master refuses to provide, and the slaves have the ability to earn (e.g., through work), they may earn and spend on themselves. However, if they have no means of earning, the master is compelled by the judge either to provide maintenance or to sell the slaves. The hadith of Abu Dharr establishes the duty to feed and clothe slaves equally to one's own standard, and the obligation not to burden them beyond their capacity. The hadith of the cat serves as a qiyas (analogy): if a woman was punished for neglecting a cat, then neglecting a human slave is even more severe. The principles ('usul') summarize: (1) everyone responsible for their charges, (2) the master must either maintain or sell the slave, (3) neglecting a human being is worse than neglecting an animal. The ruling is from the zahir al-riwayah (core Hanafi texts) and is mufta bihi.

Key Terms
النفقات (al-nafaqāt): Maintenance, including food, clothing, and shelter required for dependents.
المولى (al-mawlā): The master or owner of a slave.
عبد وأمة (ʿabd wa amah): Male and female slaves.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a master refuses to provide maintenance for his slave who has no ability to earn, what is the judge's ruling?
A) The slave is set free.
B) The master is compelled to provide maintenance or sell the slave.
C) The slave must work to earn maintenance.
D) The master is fined but not forced to sell.

Key Takeaway
It is wajib upon the master to provide food and clothing for his slaves; refusal with inability to earn leads to forced sale.

Conditions and Explicit Words of Emancipation
Opens Kitab al-Itq with prerequisites and effect of explicit emancipation words.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for valid emancipation (free, adult, sane) and explain why explicit words (sarih) like 'anta hurr' effect emancipation without niyyah.

Core Idea
Explicit words of emancipation free the slave immediately, regardless of the master's intent.

This lesson opens the Book of Emancipation with the prerequisites for a valid act of freeing a slave. The Hanafi school holds that emancipation is only valid from a free, adult, sane owner, and that certain explicit words cause immediate freedom without need for intention. Understanding these conditions and the power of explicit language is essential for correctly executing and judging acts of 'itq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three conditions for valid emancipation
The text states that emancipation is valid from a free (hurr), adult (baligh), and sane (aqil) person. These conditions ensure the person has full legal capacity.
The owner must also own the slave, as implied by the hadith 'no emancipation except in what you own'.
2
List the explicit words of emancipation
The text gives six explicit terms: anta hurr, atiq, mu'taq, muharrar, harraftuka, a'taqtuka. These are sarih words that directly indicate freedom.
These words have clear, unambiguous meanings in Arabic.
3
Understand the effect of explicit words
The text rules that when any of these words are uttered, the slave becomes free 'whether the master intended emancipation or not'. This is because sarih words are conclusive in their meaning.
This contrasts with kinaya (allusive) words, which do require intention.
4
Examine the proofs
The author cites Quranic verses (90:12-14, 4:92), hadith (Bukhari, Abu Dawud), and a companion saying (Uthman) to establish the validity and virtue of emancipation and the conditions for capacity.
These proofs are from primary sources (Quran and Sunnah).
5
Apply the ruling
Given a scenario where a free adult sane master says 'You are free' to his slave without intending freedom, you should rule that the slave becomes free immediately.
No further inquiry into intention is needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْعِتْقِ
قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ - الْعِتْقُ يَصِحُ مِنْ الْحُرِّ الْبَالِغِ الْعَاقِلِ وَإِذَا قَالَ لِعَبْدِهِ أَوْ لِأَمَتِهِ أَنْتَ حُرٌّ أَوْ عَتِيقٌ أَوْ مُعْتَقٌ أَوْ مُحَرَّرٌ أَوْ قَدْ حَرَّرْتُك أَوْ أَعْتَقْتُك فَقَدْ عَتَقَ نَوَى الْمَوْلَى الْعِتْقَ أَوْ لَمْ يَنْوِ الوجه : (۱) الآية لثبوت الْعِتْقُ يَصِحُ مِنْ الْحُرِّ الْبَالِغِ الْعَاقِلِ ﴿وَمَا أَدْرَاكَ مَا الْعَقَبَةُ فَكُّ رَقَبَةٍ أَوْ إِطْعَامٌ فِي يَوْمٍ ذِي مَسْغَبَةٍ يَتِيمًا ذَا مَقْرَبَةٍ أَوْ مِسْكِينًا ذَا مَتْرَبَةٍ﴾ (القرآن سورة البلد 90، الآية 12-14) وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت الْعِتْقُ يَصِحُ مِنْ الْحُرِّ الْبَالِغِ الْعَاقِلِ قَالَ لِي أَبُو هُرَيْرَةَ : قَالَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَيُّمَا رَجُلٍ أَعْتَقَ امْرَأً مُسْلِمًا اسْتَنْقَذَ اللَّهُ بِكُلِّ عُضْوٍ مِنْهُ عُضْوًا مِنْهُ مِنَ النَّارِ (بخاري شريف، باب ما جاء في العتق وفضله، رقم 2517) وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت الْعِتْقُ يَصِحُ مِنْ الْحُرِّ الْبَالِغِ الْعَاقِلِ عَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ شُعَيْبٍ عَنْ أَبِيهِ عَنْ جَدِّهِ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: لَا طَلَاقَ إِلَّا فِيمَا تَمْلِكُ وَلَا عِتْقَ إِلَّا فِيمَا تَمْلِكُ وَلَا بَيْعَ إِلَّا فِيمَا تَمْلِكُ (ابو داود شريف، باب في الطلاق قبل النكاح، رقم 2190) وجه (۳) الحديث لثبوت الْعِتْقُ يَصِحُ مِنْ الْحُرِّ الْبَالِغِ الْعَاقِلِ عَنْ عَلِيٍّ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: رُفِعَ الْقَلَمُ عَنْ ثَلَاثَةٍ عَنِ النَّائِمِ حَتَّى يَسْتَيْقِظَ وَعَنِ الصَّبِيِّ حَتَّى يَخْتَلِمَ وَعَنِ الْمَجْنُونِ حَتَّى يَعْقِلَ (ابو داود شريف، باب في المجنون يسرق أو يصيب حداً، رقم 4403) وجه (۴) قول الصحابي لثبوت الْعِتْقُ يَصِحُ مِنْ الْحُرِّ الْبَالِغِ الْعَاقِلِ وَقَالَ عُثْمَانُ رضي الله عنه: لَيْسَ لِمَجْنُونٍ وَلَا لِسَكْرَانَ طَلَاقٌ (بخاري شريف، باب الطلاق في الإغلاق والكره، رقم 5269) وجه: (ا) الآية لثبوت وَإِذَا قَالَ لِعَبْدِهِ أَوْ لِأَمَتِهِ أَنْتَ حُرٌّ ﴿وَمَنْ قَتَلَ مُؤْمِنًا خَطَأً فَتَحْرِيرُ رَقَبَةٍ مُؤْمِنَةٍ وَدِيَةٌ مُسَلَّمَةٌ إِلَى أَهْلِهِ﴾ (القرآن سورة النساء 4، الآية 92) وجه : (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا قَالَ لِعَبْدِهِ أَوْ لِأَمَتِهِ أَنْتَ حُرٌّ قَالَ لِي أَبُو هُرَيْرَةَ : قَالَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَيُّمَا رَجُلٍ أَعْتَقَ امْرَأً مُسْلِمًا اسْتَنْقَذَ اللَّهُ بِكُلِّ عُضْوٍ مِنْهُ عُضْوًا مِنْهُ مِنَ النَّارِ (بخاري شريف، باب ما جاء في العتق وفضله، رقم 2517) اصول: آزادگی کی شرط یہ ہے کہ اولا وہ خود آزاد ، بالغ ہو اور غلام یا باندی جسکو آزاد کرنا ہے اس کی ملکیت میں ہو
Book of Emancipation. He said - may Allah have mercy on him -: Emancipation is valid from a free, adult, sane person. And when he says to his male slave or his female slave: 'You are free' or 'free' or 'emancipated' or 'liberated' or 'I have liberated you' or 'I have emancipated you,' then he becomes free, whether the master intended emancipation or not. The proof: (1) The verse for establishing that emancipation is valid from a free, adult, sane person: 'And what can make you know what is the uphill road? It is the freeing of a neck or feeding on a day of severe hunger an orphan of near relationship or a poor person in misery' (Quran 90:12-14). Proof: (1) The hadith for establishing that emancipation is valid from a free, adult, sane person: Abu Huraira said: The Prophet said: 'Any man who frees a Muslim slave, Allah will save from the Fire every limb of his body in exchange for every limb of the slave's body' (Bukhari, Chapter on Emancipation and its Virtue, no. 2517). Proof: (2) The hadith for establishing that emancipation is valid from a free, adult, sane person: From Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather that the Prophet said: 'There is no divorce except in what you own, and no emancipation except in what you own, and no sale except in what you own' (Abu Dawud, Chapter on Divorce before Marriage, no. 2190). Proof: (3) The hadith for establishing that emancipation is valid from a free, adult, sane person: From Ali from the Prophet said: 'The pen is lifted from three: from the sleeper until he wakes up, from the child until he reaches puberty, and from the insane person until he regains sanity' (Abu Dawud, Chapter on the Insane Person Stealing or Committing a Crime, no. 4403). Proof: (4) The saying of the Companion for establishing that emancipation is valid from a free, adult, sane person: Uthman said: 'There is no divorce for an insane person nor for an intoxicated person' (Bukhari, Chapter on Divorce under Duress and Coercion, no. 5269). Proof: (a) The verse for establishing that when he says to his male slave or his female slave 'You are free': 'And whoever kills a believer by mistake must free a believing slave and pay blood money to his family' (Quran 4:92). Proof: (2) The hadith for establishing that when he says to his male slave or his female slave 'You are free': Abu Huraira said: The Prophet said: 'Any man who frees a Muslim slave, Allah will save from the Fire every limb of his body in exchange for every limb of the slave's body' (Bukhari, Chapter on Emancipation and its Virtue, no. 2517). Principle: The condition for freedom is that firstly he himself should be free, adult, and the male or female slave whom he frees should be in his ownership.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Emancipation with a dual ruling. First, it states the prerequisites for a valid act of emancipation: the emancipator must be free (not a slave), adult (baligh), and sane (aqil). This is based on the capacity to validly execute legal dispositions. Second, it lists explicit words (sarih) of emancipation—such as 'anta hurr' or 'atiq'—and rules that these words cause immediate freedom regardless of the master's intention, because the apparent meaning is clear. The commentator then provides proofs: Quranic verses from Surah al-Balad (90:12-14) and Surah al-Nisa (4:92), and several hadith from Bukhari, Abu Dawud, and the saying of Uthman. The Urdu note at the end summarizes the condition: the owner himself must be free and adult, and the slave must be in his ownership.

Key Terms
العِتْق (al-'itq): Emancipation: legally, the removal of the shackles of slavery from the slave.
الْحُرّ (al-hurr): A free person, as opposed to a slave; a condition for the valid execution of emancipation.
صَرِيح (sarih): Explicit words that directly indicate emancipation without need for intention (e.g., anta hurr).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, if a master says to his slave 'anta hurr', is the slave freed even if the master did not intend emancipation?
A) Yes, because it is an explicit word.
B) No, intention is always required.
C) Only if the slave is Muslim.
D) Only if the master is free.

Key Takeaway
Emancipation is valid only from a free, adult, sane owner, and explicit words like 'anta hurr' cause immediate freedom without need for intention.
