Body Part Expressions and Kinaya in Emancipation
Ruling on body part words and indirect expressions for emancipation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify emancipation expressions as direct (sarih) or indirect (kinaya) and determine the ruling based on Hanafi jurisprudence.

Core Idea
Body part words free entirely; 'I have no ownership' frees with intention; 'I have no authority' never frees.

This lesson addresses how specific words and phrases affect the emancipation of a slave. Not all expressions of releasing ownership are effective in Hanafi law. Understanding the distinction between direct and indirect expressions (kinaya) is crucial for correctly applying the rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the expression used
Look at the exact wording: body part (e.g. 'your head is free'), or broader phrases like 'I have no ownership over you' or 'I have no authority over you'.
2
Classify as sarih or kinaya
Sarih expressions explicitly state freedom; kinaya are indirect and require intention. Body part words are considered sarih. 'La milk' is kinaya; 'la sultana' is not even kinaya.
Hanafi rules: intention is only needed for kinaya, not for sarih.
3
Apply the ruling
If sarih, the slave becomes free regardless of intention. If kinaya (like 'la milk'), freedom depends on intention. If not kinaya (like 'la sultana'), intention does not make it effective.
The test: does the phrase customarily imply emancipation? If yes, it's kinaya; if no, it's not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَكَذَلِكَ إِذَا قَالَ: رَأْسُكَ حُرٌّ أَوْ وَجْهُكَ أَوْ رَقَبَتُكَ أَوْ بَدَنُكَ وَكَذَا إِذَا قَالَ لِأُمَتِهِ فَرْجُكَ حُرٌّ وَإِنْ قَالَ: لَا مِلْكَ لِي عَلَيْكَ وَنَوَى بِهِ الْحُرِّيَّةَ عَتَقَ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَنْوِ لَمْ يَعْتِقْ وَكَذَلِكَ كِنَايَاتُ الْعِتْقِ وَإِنْ قَالَ: لَا سُلْطَانَ لِي عَلَيْكَ وَنَوَى الْعِتْقَ لَمْ يَعْتِقْ وَإِنْ قَالَ: هَذَا ابْنِي وَثَبَتَ عَلَى ذَلِكَ عَتَقَ أَوْ هَذَا مَوْلايَ أَوْ يَا مَوْلايَ عَتَقَ وَإِنْ قَالَ يَا ابْنِي أَوْ يَا أَخِي لَمْ يَعْتِقْ وَإِنْ قَالَ لِغُلَامٍ لَهُ لَا يُولَدُ مِثْلُهُ لِمِثْلِهِ هَذَا ابْنِي عَتَقَ عَلَيْهِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَإِنْ قَالَ لِأَمَتِهِ أَنْتِ طَالِقٌ يَنْوِي الْحُرِّيَّةَ لَمْ تَعْتِقْ وَإِنْ قَالَ لِعَبْدِهِ : أَنْتَ مِثْلَ الْحُرِّ لَمْ يَعْتِقْ وَإِنْ قَالَ: مَا أَنْتَ إِلَّا حُرٌّ عَتَقَ وَإِذَا مَلَكَ الرَّجُلُ ذَا رَحِمٍ مَحْرَمٍ مِنْهُ عَتَقَ عَلَيْهِ
And similarly, if he says: 'Your head is free' or 'your face' or 'your neck' or 'your body,' and likewise if he says to his female slave 'your private part is free.' And if he says: 'I have no ownership over you' and intends thereby freedom, then he becomes free; and if he did not intend, he does not become free. And similarly the indirect expressions of emancipation. And if he says: 'I have no authority over you' and intends emancipation, does not become free. And if he says: 'This is my son' and persists in that, then he becomes free; or 'This is my master' or 'O my master,' he becomes free. And if he says: 'O my son' or 'O my brother,' he does not become free. And if he says to a male slave of his, for whom no one like him is born to such a person, 'This is my son,' then he becomes free according to Abu Hanifa. And if he says to his female slave: 'You are divorced' intending freedom, she does not become free. And if he says to his male slave: 'You are like a free person,' he does not become free. And if he says: 'You are nothing but free,' he becomes free. And when a person comes into possession of a uterine relative who is a mahram to him, the slave becomes free.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage continues the Book of Emancipation with various additional rulings. It first addresses using words that refer to body parts such as 'your head is free'—such expressions are interpreted as intending the whole person, so the entire slave becomes free. Then it covers indirect (kinaya) expressions: 'I have no ownership over you' frees if intention is present, but 'I have no authority over you' does not free even with intention, because 'authority' (sultan) is broader than ownership. The passage then addresses claiming paternity: saying 'this is my son' and persisting causes freedom, but addressing as 'my son' or 'my brother' without claiming paternity does not. A special case: if the slave is of such a description that no one like him could be born to the master, yet he claims paternity, Abu Hanifa says it still frees (view not shared by the two disciples, who require possibility). Using divorce words for a slave woman ('you are divorced') aiming at freedom does not free, because these words are not used for emancipation. Saying 'you are like a free person' is not explicit enough, but 'you are nothing but free' is an emphatic declaration that frees. Finally, ownership of a mahram relative (such as a brother or uncle) results in immediate freedom, as per hadith.

Key Terms
كِنَايَة (kinaya): An indirect expression that does not explicitly state emancipation but may imply it; intention is required for it to be effective.
صَرِيح (sarih): A direct and unambiguous expression; intention is not required for the legal effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a master says to his slave 'I have no ownership over you' with the intention of freeing him, what is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) The slave becomes free because it is a kinaya with intention.
B) The slave does not become free because intention is not enough.
C) The slave becomes free regardless of intention.
D) The slave becomes free only if he is a mahram.

Key Takeaway
Body part words are sarih and free without intention; 'la milk' is kinaya requiring intention; 'la sultana' is ineffective.

Emancipation through Paternity Claims, Emphatic Declarations, and Mahram Ownership
Rulings on paternity claims, emphatic declarations, divorce words, and mahram ownership

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rulings on paternity claims, emphatic declarations, and ownership of mahram relatives as causes of emancipation, including the intra-Hanafi dispute on paternity.

Core Idea
Claiming paternity frees the slave; emphatic 'nothing but free' frees; owning a mahram relative automatically frees.

Continuing from the previous lesson, this lesson covers additional emancipation scenarios: when a master claims a slave is his son, when he uses emphatic declarations like 'you are nothing but free,' and the important rule that owning a mahram relative results in automatic freedom. It also highlights a notable difference between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples regarding paternity claims on an unlikely slave.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of statement or relationship
Distinguish between a paternity claim (e.g., 'this is my son'), an emphatic declaration (e.g., 'you are nothing but free'), and ownership of a relative (e.g., acquiring a brother as a slave).
2
Apply the specific ruling for each type
For paternity claims that are persisted, the slave is freed. For emphatic 'you are nothing but free', it is considered an effective declaration. For owning a mahram relative, freedom is automatic upon possession.
Exception: calling a slave 'my son' without a claim of paternity does not free.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on paternity
If the slave could not possibly be the master's son due to age or appearance, Abu Hanifa still rules freedom; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require possibility. The relied-upon view is Abu Hanifa's, but caution is advised.
This ikhtilaf is based on the interpretation of the master's intent.
4
Review the hadith on mahram relatives
The Prophet (ﷺ) said: 'Whoever comes into possession of a mahram relative, that relative becomes free.' This is a dalil for immediate emancipation upon acquisition.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but accepted in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَكَذَلِكَ إِذَا قَالَ: رَأْسُكَ حُرٌّ أَوْ وَجْهُكَ أَوْ رَقَبَتُكَ أَوْ بَدَنُكَ وَكَذَا إِذَا قَالَ لِأُمَتِهِ فَرْجُكَ حُرٌّ وَإِنْ قَالَ: لَا مِلْكَ لِي عَلَيْكَ وَنَوَى بِهِ الْحُرِّيَّةَ عَتَقَ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَنْوِ لَمْ يَعْتِقْ وَكَذَلِكَ كِنَايَاتُ الْعِتْقِ وَإِنْ قَالَ: لَا سُلْطَانَ لِي عَلَيْكَ وَنَوَى الْعِتْقَ لَمْ يَعْتِقْ وَإِنْ قَالَ: هَذَا ابْنِي وَثَبَتَ عَلَى ذَلِكَ عَتَقَ أَوْ هَذَا مَوْلايَ أَوْ يَا مَوْلايَ عَتَقَ وَإِنْ قَالَ يَا ابْنِي أَوْ يَا أَخِي لَمْ يَعْتِقْ وَإِنْ قَالَ لِغُلَامٍ لَهُ لَا يُولَدُ مِثْلُهُ لِمِثْلِهِ هَذَا ابْنِي عَتَقَ عَلَيْهِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَإِنْ قَالَ لِأَمَتِهِ أَنْتِ طَالِقٌ يَنْوِي الْحُرِّيَّةَ لَمْ تَعْتِقْ وَإِنْ قَالَ لِعَبْدِهِ : أَنْتَ مِثْلَ الْحُرِّ لَمْ يَعْتِقْ وَإِنْ قَالَ: مَا أَنْتَ إِلَّا حُرٌّ عَتَقَ وَإِذَا مَلَكَ الرَّجُلُ ذَا رَحِمٍ مَحْرَمٍ مِنْهُ عَتَقَ عَلَيْهِ

And if he says: 'I have no ownership over you' and intends thereby freedom, then he becomes free; and if he did not intend, he does not become free. And if he says: 'O my son' or 'O my brother,' he does not become free. And if he says to a male slave of his, for whom no one like him is born to such a person, 'This is my son,' then he becomes free according to Abu Hanifa. And if he says to his female slave: 'You are divorced' intending freedom, she does not become free. And if he says to his male slave: 'You are like a free person,' he does not become free. And if he says: 'You are nothing but free,' he becomes free. And when a person comes into possession of a uterine relative who is a mahram to him, the slave becomes free.

مَحْرَم (mahram): A relative with whom marriage is permanently forbidden, e.g., mother, sister, daughter, aunt, etc.
كِنَايَة (kinaya): An indirect expression that does not explicitly state emancipation but may imply it; intention is required for it to be effective.

A) The slave becomes free because the claim is persisted.
B) The slave does not become free because it is impossible.

D) The slave does not become free unless witnesses confirm.

Automatic Emancipation of Mahram Relatives
Ruling that owning a mahram relative immediately frees the slave.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on owning a mahram slave and apply the hadith proof to determine automatic emancipation.

Core Idea
Owning a mahram relative instantly frees the slave, even without intent.

This lesson addresses a unique Hanafi ruling: if a person acquires ownership of a slave who is a mahram (a relative permanently prohibited in marriage due to blood), the slave is automatically emancipated. This is not optional — freedom is a legal consequence of ownership itself, based on a specific hadith. We will examine the ruling, its proof, and the disagreement with other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the first line of the Arabic passage: 'When a man comes into possession of a mahram relative, it becomes free for him (i.e., the slave is emancipated).' Recognize that this is a rule of immediate, automatic freedom.
The ruling is unconditional — no additional action by the owner is needed.
2
Examine the Dalil (Evidence)
The passage cites the hadith of Samura ibn Jundub: 'Whoever comes into possession of a mahram relative, then he is free.' Note the source: Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi. Understand that this is a zanni (probable) hadith but still binding in Hanafi fiqh.
The phrase 'fahuwa hurr' (he is free) is the operative part.
3
Understand the Legal Principle (Usul)
The Urdu note summarizes: 'A mahram relative upon coming into ownership becomes free.' This is a textual ruling derived directly from the hadith; no qiyas (analogy) is needed.
The principle prevents unnatural ownership of close family.
4
Compare with Other Schools
Note that this ruling is mukhtalaf fih (disputed). The Shafi'i school, for example, does not consider automatic emancipation; the owner may choose to free or retain the slave. Understand that the Hanafi position relies on the literal meaning of the hadith.
This difference illustrates how usul principles affect fiqh rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا مَلَكَ الرَّجُلُ ذَا رَحِمٍ مَحْرَمٍ مِنْهُ عَتَقَ عَلَيْهِ
وجه : (ا) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا مَلَكَ الرَّجُلُ ذَا رَحِمٍ مَحْرَمٍ مِنْهُ عَتَقَ عَلَيْهِ عَنْ سَمُرَةَ بْنِ جُنْدُبٍ فِيمَا يَحْسَبُ حَمَّادٌ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «مَنْ مَلَكَ ذَا رَحِمٍ مَحْرَمٍ فَهُوَ حُرٌّ» (ابوداود شریف، باب فی من ملک ذا رحم محرم، نمبر 3949/ ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی من ملک ذا رحم محرم، نمبر 1365)
اصول: ذی رحم محرم ملکیت میں آتے ہی آزاد ہو جائے گا۔
And when a person comes into possession of a uterine relative who is a mahram to him, the slave becomes free. Proof: (a) The hadith for establishing that when a person comes into possession of a mahram relative, the slave becomes free: From Samura ibn Jundub, as Hammad supposes, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever comes into possession of a mahram relative, then he is free.' (Abu Dawud, Chapter on One Who Owns a Mahram Relative, no. 3949; Tirmidhi, Chapter on One Who Owns a Mahram Relative, no. 1365). Principle: A mahram relative becomes free as soon as he comes into ownership.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage presents a key ruling in Hanafi fiqh: if a person acquires ownership of a slave who is a mahram relative (i.e., a relative whom one cannot marry due to blood ties, such as a father, mother, brother, sister, uncle, aunt, etc.), the slave is automatically emancipated. This is based on the prophetic hadith narrated by Samura ibn Jundub. The reason is to prevent the unnatural situation of a person owning a close relative, which would conflict with family dignity. The Urdu note restates the principle. This ruling is specific to mahram relatives; non-mahram relatives do not trigger automatic emancipation.

Key Terms
ذُو رَحِمٍ مَحْرَمٍ (dhu rahim mahram): A relative through blood who is in the prohibited degrees of marriage, such as father, mother, brother, sister, son, daughter, uncle, aunt, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man buys his own brother as a slave, what happens in Hanafi fiqh?
A) The brother remains a slave because the man intended slavery.
B) The brother becomes free immediately because he is a mahram relative.
C) The brother becomes free only if the man utters words of emancipation.
D) The brother becomes free only if he is under the age of puberty.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, ownership of a mahram relative automatically frees the slave, based on a direct hadith and the principle of preserving family dignity.

Partial Manumission: The Hanafi Position with Proofs
Primary ruling on partial manumission with intra-Hanafi dispute and four hadith proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on partial manumission of one's own slave, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute, and identify the supporting dalil from the text.

Core Idea
Partial freedom is valid; the freed part is free, the rest remains slave with sa'yah.

This passage from Al-Quduri presents the Hanafi ruling on a common scenario: a master frees a portion of his slave. Imam Abu Hanifa rules that only the freed portion becomes free, and the slave must work to pay for the remaining value (sa'yah). His two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, disagree, holding that the entire slave becomes free. The author then provides four hadith proofs to support Abu Hanifa's view. Understanding this dispute reveals the Hanafi principle that freedom can be divided (tajzi'at al-'itq), a key usul point.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and the dispute
Identify what Abu Hanifa says (partial freedom with sa'yah) and what the Sahibayn say (complete freedom).
2
Identify the key hadith proofs
List the four hadith cited: Ibn Umar, Ismail ibn Umayyah, Abu Huraira, and Abul-Malih.
3
Extract the usul principle
Abu Hanifa’s view that freedom can be divided; Sahibayn’s view that it cannot.
4
Apply the proofs
See how the hadith support partial freedom (e.g., "عَتَقَ مِنْهُ مَا عَتَقَ" and "تُعْتَقُ فِي عِتْقِكَ وَتُرَقُ فِي رِقِّكَ").
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Which position is relied upon in the Hanafi school? Abu Hanifa’s view is the mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْعِتْقِ

وَإِذَا أَعْتَقَ الرَّجُلُ بَعْضَ عَبْدِهِ عَتَقَ ذَلِكَ الْبَعْضُ وَسَعَى فِي بَقِيَّةِ قِيمَتِهِ لِمَوْلَاهُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَعِنْدَهُمَا يَعْتِقُ كُلُّهُ

وَجْهٌ (١): الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَإِذَا أَعْتَقَ الرَّجُلُ بَعْضَ عَبْدِهِ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عُمَرَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا: أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «مَنْ أَعْتَقَ شِرْكًا لَهُ فِي عَبْدٍ، فَكَانَ لَهُ مَالٌ يَبْلُغُ ثَمَنَ الْعَبْدِ، فَوَمَ الْعَبْدُ قِيمَةَ عَدْلٍ، فَأَعْطَى شُرَكَاءَهُ حِصَصَهُمْ، وَعَتَقَ عَلَيْهِ، وَإِلَّا فَقَدْ عَتَقَ مِنْهُ مَا عَتَقَ»

وَجْهٌ (٢): الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَإِذَا أَعْتَقَ الرَّجُلُ بَعْضَ عَبْدِهِ حَدَّثَنِي إِسْمَاعِيلُ بْنُ أُمَيَّةَ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، عَنْ جَدِّهِ، قَالَ: كَانَ لَهُمْ غُلَامٌ يُقَالُ لَهُ: طَهْمَانُ، أَوْ ذَكْوَانُ، قَالَ: فَأَعْتَقَ جَدُّهُ نِصْفَهُ، فَجَاءَ الْعَبْدُ إِلَى النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَأَخْبَرَهُ، فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «تُعْتَقُ فِي عِتْقِكَ، وَتُرَقُ فِي رِقِّكَ» قَالَ: فَكَانَ يَخْدُمُ سَيِّدَهُ حَتَّى مَاتَ.

وَجْهٌ (٣): الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَإِذَا أَعْتَقَ الرَّجُلُ بَعْضَ عَبْدِهِ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ: أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «مَنْ أَعْتَقَ نَصِيبًا، أَوْ شَقِيصًا، فِي مَمْلُوكٍ، فَخَلَاصُهُ عَلَيْهِ فِي مَالِهِ، إِنْ كَانَ لَهُ مَالٌ، وَإِلَّا قُوِّمَ عَلَيْهِ، فَاسْتُسْعِيَ بِهِ غَيْرَ مَشْقُوقٍ عَلَيْهِ»

وَجْهٌ (٤): الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَإِذَا أَعْتَقَ الرَّجُلُ بَعْضَ عَبْدِهِ عَنْ أَبِي الْمَلِيحِ، أَنَّ رَجُلًا مِنْ قَوْمِهِ أَعْتَقَ ثُلُثَ غُلَامِهِ، فَرُفِعَ ذَلِكَ إِلَى النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، فَقَالَ: «هُوَ حُرٌّ كُلُّهُ، لَيْسَ لِلَّهِ شَرِيكٌ»

أُصُولٌ: الْإِمَامُ أَبُو حَنِيفَةَ: غُلَامٍ كَا جِتْنَا حِصَّه آزَاد كِیَا وُه حِصَّه آزَاد هُوئے گا اور جو حصہ آزاد نہیں کیا وہ حصہ غلامیت میں باقی رہے گا۔
أُصُولٌ: الْإِمَامُ أَبُو حَنِيفَةَ: آزَادُگِی میں تَجْزِئَى مُمكِن ہے۔ صاحبین: آزادُگِی میں تَجْزِئَى نہیں ہو گی۔
Book of Manumission. And when a man frees part of his slave, that part becomes free, and the slave works (sa'yah) for the remainder of his value for his master according to Abu Hanifa. And according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), all of him becomes free. (Then four hadith proofs are quoted. Usul notes in Urdu: Imam Abu Hanifa: whatever portion of the slave was freed, that portion becomes free, and the portion not freed remains in slavery. Imam Abu Hanifa: division is possible in freedom. The two companions: division is not possible in freedom.)
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on partial manumission of one's own slave. The text states: if a man frees a portion of his slave, that portion becomes free, and the slave must work (sa'yah) to earn the remaining value for his master — this is Abu Hanifa's position. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, the entire slave becomes free. The author then provides four hadith proofs. The first is from Ibn Umar: the Prophet said, 'Whoever frees a share in a slave...' The second is from Ismail ibn Umayyah's grandfather: a man freed half of his slave, and the Prophet said, 'You are free in your freedom, and a slave in your slavery.' The third from Abu Huraira: the Prophet said, 'Whoever frees a portion...' The fourth from Abul-Malih: a man freed a third of his slave, and the Prophet said, 'He is all free, Allah has no partner.' The usul note explains the principle: Abu Hanifa holds that freedom can be divided (the freed part is free, the rest remains slave), while the Sahibayn hold that freedom cannot be divided, so the whole slave becomes free. The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, the slave must work to pay for the non-freed portion; under the Sahibayn, the slave is completely free and the master has no claim.

Key Terms
الْعِتْق (al-'itq): Manumission; freeing a slave from bondage.
السَّعَايَة (al-sa'yah): The slave's working to earn money to pay the remaining value to the master.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a man frees half of his own slave and he is insolvent, what is the status of the slave?
A) The entire slave becomes free immediately.
B) Only the freed half becomes free, and the slave must work to pay for the other half.
C) The manumission is invalid because it is partial.
D) The slave remains fully enslaved until the master pays compensation.

Key Takeaway
Partial manumission is valid in the Hanafi school; the freed part is free, and the slave must work (sa'yah) for the remaining value if the master is insolvent.

Jointly Owned Slave: Partner Frees His Share
Ruling on partner freeing his share

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on partial manumission and explain the options available to the other partner, distinguishing Abu Hanifa's position from that of the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Partial freedom triggers multiple remedies: the partner can free, claim compensation, or seek sa'yah.

This passage addresses a classical scenario where a jointly owned slave is partially freed by one co-owner. The ruling is not simply that the slave becomes free; rather, the other partner is granted options to protect his interest. The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement about the scope of these options, rooted in different interpretations of the relevant hadiths. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to trace how proof texts shape divergent rulings within the same madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is one partner freeing his share in a jointly owned slave. The ruling is that the freed share becomes free (عتق). Then, based on the freeing partner's wealth, the other partner has options.
2
List the options according to Abu Hanifa
Abu Hanifa gives three options if the freeing partner is wealthy: free his own share, claim compensation (daman), or seek sa'yah from the slave. If the freeing partner is insolvent, only free or sa'yah are available (daman is not possible).
Sa'yah means the slave works to earn the value of the other share.
3
State the Sahibayn's restriction
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad limit the partner to compensation (daman) if the freeing partner is wealthy, or sa'yah if insolvent. They do not allow the partner to simply free his own share.
Their view is closer to the literal meaning of the hadith.
4
Examine the hadith proofs
Two hadiths are cited. The first (Ibn Umar) says if the freeing partner has wealth, he must free the whole slave; if not, only his share is free. This supports the Sahibayn. The second (Abu Huraira) commands sa'yah. Abu Hanifa interprets these as giving options, not obligations.
The difference in interpretation (the wajh al-dalalah) leads to different rulings.
5
Identify the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's, as it gives the partner more flexibility. Al-Quduri presents it first and with greater detail, indicating preference.
This is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf where the majority follow Abu Hanifa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا كَانَ الْعَبْدُ بَيْنَ شَرِيكَيْنِ فَأَعْتَقَ أَحَدُهُمَا نَصِيبَهُ عَتَقَ فَإِنْ كَانَ مُوسِرًا فَشَرِيكُهُ بِالْخَيَارِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ إِنْ شَاءَ أَعْتَقَ وَإِنْ شَاءَ ضَمَّنَ شَرِيكَهُ قِيمَةَ نَصِيبِهِ وَإِنْ شَاءَ اسْتَسْعَى الْعَبْدَ وَإِنْ كَانَ الْمُعْتِقُ مُعْسِرًا فَالشَّرِيكُ بِالْخِيَارِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ إِنْ شَاءَ أَعْتَقَ وَإِنْ شَاءَ اسْتَسْعَى الْعَبْدَ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ لَيْسَ لَهُ إِلَّا الضَّمَانُ مَعَ الْيَسَارِ أَوِ السَّعَايَةُ مَعَ الْإِعْسَارِ

وَجْهٌ (١): الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَإِذَا كَانَ الْعَبْدُ بَيْنَ شَرِيكَيْنِ فَأَعْتَقَ أَحَدُهُمَا نَصِيبَهُ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «مَنْ أَعْتَقَ شِرْكًا لَهُ فِي مَمْلُوكٍ فَعَلَيْهِ عِتْقُهُ كُلُّهُ، إِنْ كَانَ لَهُ مَالٌ يَبْلُغُ ثَمَنَهُ، فَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُ مَالٌ يُقَوَّمُ عَلَيْهِ قِيمَةَ عَدْلٍ، فَأُعْتِقَ مِنْهُ مَا أَعْتَقَ»

وَجْهٌ (١): الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ لَيْسَ لَهُ إِلَّا الضَّمَانُ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ: أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «مَنْ أَعْتَقَ نَصِيبًا، أَوْ شَقِيصًا، فِي مَمْلُوكٍ، فَخَلَاصُهُ عَلَيْهِ فِي مَالِهِ، إِنْ كَانَ لَهُ مَالٌ، وَإِلَّا قُوِّمَ عَلَيْهِ، فَاسْتُسْعِيَ بِهِ غَيْرَ مَشْقُوقٍ عَلَيْهِ»

وَجْهٌ (٢): الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ لَيْسَ لَهُ إِلَّا الضَّمَانُ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «مَنْ أَعْتَقَ شِرْكًا لَهُ فِي مَمْلُوكٍ فَعَلَيْهِ عِتْقُهُ كُلُّهُ، إِنْ كَانَ لَهُ مَالٌ يَبْلُغُ ثَمَنَهُ، فَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُ مَالٌ يُقَوَّمُ عَلَيْهِ قِيمَةَ عَدْلٍ، فَأُعْتِقَ مِنْهُ مَا أَعْتَقَ»
And when a slave is between two partners and one of them frees his share, it (the share) becomes free. Then if the freeing partner is wealthy, his partner has a choice according to Abu Hanifa: if he wishes, he may free, or if he wishes, he may hold his partner liable for the value of his share, or if he wishes, he may seek sa'yah from the slave. And if the freeing partner is insolvent, then the (other) partner has a choice according to Abu Hanifa: if he wishes, he may free, or if he wishes, he may seek sa'yah from the slave. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: He has no option except compensation (daman) with wealth, or sa'yah with insolvency. (Then two hadith proofs are quoted.)
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage deals with a situation where a slave is jointly owned by two partners, and one partner frees his share. The freed share becomes free. According to Abu Hanifa, the other partner has multiple options: if the freeing partner is wealthy, the other partner may (1) free his own share, (2) hold the freeing partner liable for the value of his (the other's) share, or (3) require the slave to work (sa'yah) to earn the value. If the freeing partner is insolvent, only options (1) and (3) are available; option (2) is not possible because the freeing partner has no money. In contrast, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad restrict the partner's options: he can only claim compensation (daman) from the freeing partner if he is wealthy, or sa'yah from the slave if he is insolvent; he cannot choose to free his own share. The hadith proofs: The first from Ibn Umar states that a partner who frees his share must free the whole slave if he has money; if not, only the freed portion is free. The second from Abu Huraira emphasizes the sa'yah option. The usul note is implicit in the differing opinions.

Key Terms
الضَّمَان (al-daman): Liability; the freeing partner must pay the other partner the value of his share.
الْخِيَار (al-khiyar): Option or choice given to the partner who did not free his share.
السَّعَايَة (al-sa'yah): The slave working to earn the value of the other partner's share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (mufta bihi), if a wealthy partner frees his share in a jointly owned slave, what are the options for the other partner?
A) He must also free his share.
B) He may only claim compensation from the freeing partner.
C) He may free his share, claim compensation, or seek sa'yah from the slave.
D) He may only seek sa'yah from the slave.

Key Takeaway
Partial manumission gives the other partner flexible remedies: free his share, claim compensation, or require the slave to work, with Abu Hanifa's view being the relied-upon position.

Purchase or Inheritance of a Son: Father's Share Becomes Free
Ruling on two men buying or inheriting the son of one of them

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when two men purchase or inherit the son of one of them, and explain the legal consequences for both the father and the other co-owner.

Core Idea
A father cannot own his son; his share becomes free automatically, with no compensation owed.

This passage addresses a specific scenario: two men jointly acquire a slave who is the biological son of one of them. The Islamic principle that a person cannot own a close blood relative (dhu rahim mahram) triggers automatic freedom for the father's share. The ruling avoids any monetary liability on the father, while the other co-owner retains the option to either free his share or require the slave to work off the value. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its basis in hadith, and the options available to the co-owner.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Clearly state the scenario: two men either buy together or inherit a slave who is the son of one of them. The father is one of the co-owners.
The text covers both purchase and inheritance.
2
Determine the ruling for the father's share
The father's share in the slave becomes free immediately upon acquisition. No compensation (daman) is due from the father to the other co-owner.
The hadith 'Whoever owns a close blood relative becomes free' applies only to the father because he is the mahram relative.
3
Explain the absence of liability
The father is not liable because the freedom of his share is automatic by operation of law; it is not a voluntary act that would require restoring value to the partner.
This differs from cases where a co-owner voluntarily frees his share, where he must compensate the other.
4
Describe the co-owner's options
The other co-owner (partner) has two choices: (1) free his share voluntarily, or (2) require the slave to work (sa'yah) to earn the value of the partner's share and become fully free.
If the partner chooses sa'yah, the slave works to pay off the partner's share; upon payment, he becomes entirely free.
5
Apply the hadith proof
The hadith 'Man malaka dha rahim mahram fahuwa hurr' is the textual evidence. It establishes that ownership of a mahram relative automatically frees the slave. In this case, the father's ownership triggers freedom for his portion.
The hadith is a singular hadith (zanni al-thubut) but accepted as actionable in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا اشْتَرَى رَجُلَانِ ابْنَ أَحَدِهِمَا عَتَقَ نَصِيبُ الْأَبِ لَا ضَمَانَ عَلَيْهِ وَكَذَلِكَ إِذَا وَرِثَاهُ وَالشَّرِيكُ بِالْخِيَارِ إِنْ شَاءَ أَعْتَقَ نَصِيبَهُ وَإِنْ شَاءَ اسْتَسْعَى الْعَبْدَ

وَجْهٌ (١): الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَإِذَا اشْتَرَى رَجُلَانِ ابْنَ أَحَدِهِمَا «مَنْ مَلَكَ ذَا رَحِمٍ مَحْرَمٍ فَهُوَ حُرٌّ» (أَبُو دَاوُدَ، التِّرْمِذِيُّ)

أُصُولٌ: شَرِيكٍ كِي قَرَابَتٍ كِي وَجْهٍ سِے غُلَام أَپْنے حِصَّه كَا آزَاد هُؤا تَو وُه شَرِيك ضَامِن نَهِيں هُو گا، اب دُوسرَا چَاهے تَو آزَاد كَرے يَا غُلَام سِے حِصَّه كے بِقَدَر سِعَايَت كَرا لے.
And when two men purchase the son of one of them, the father's share becomes free, and there is no liability (daman) upon him. Similarly, when they inherit him (the son). And the partner has a choice: if he wishes, he may free his share, and if he wishes, he may seek sa'yah from the slave. (Hadith: 'Whoever owns a close blood relative becomes free.') Usul note: Because of the partner's kinship, the slave became free with respect to his share; that partner will not be liable. Now the other may free or seek sa'yah from the slave to the extent of the share.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage covers the case where two men purchase the son of one of them (i.e., the son is a slave owned jointly by his father and another man). Upon purchase, the father's share in his son becomes free automatically because of the Islamic principle that a person cannot own his own close relative (mahram). No compensation (daman) is due from the father to the other partner. The same ruling applies if they inherit the son (i.e., the father and another inherit a slave who is the father's son). The other partner then has a choice: he may either free his share (voluntarily) or require the slave to work (sa'yah) to pay the value of his share. The hadith proof is: 'Whoever owns a close blood relative (dhi rahim mahram) becomes free' — meaning the slave becomes free by virtue of the owner's kinship. The usul note explains that because the partner's (father's) share of the slave became free due to kinship, he is not liable to compensate the other partner. The other partner's options are as mentioned.

Key Terms
ذُو رَحِمٍ مَحْرَم (dhu rahim mahram): A close blood relative whom one cannot marry, e.g., father, mother, son, daughter.
ضَمَان (daman): Liability or compensation for loss, typically monetary.
اسْتِسْعَاء (istis'a'): A legal arrangement where a slave works to earn money to pay for his freedom; often used when a co-owner does not free his share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If two men jointly purchase the son of one of them, what is the status of the father's share?
A) The father's share remains in slavery.
B) The father's share becomes free, and he must compensate the partner.
C) The father's share becomes free without any compensation due.
D) The entire slave becomes free.

Key Takeaway
When a father co-owns his son, his share becomes free automatically, and he owes no compensation; the other co-owner may free or seek sa'yah.

Emancipation of the Fetus (al-Haml)
Ruling on emancipation of fetus with proof from tabi'i practice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on freeing a fetus independently from its mother and cite the proof from the practice of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.

Core Idea
A fetus can be freed without its mother; each is a separate legal entity.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling from Kitab al-'Itq: the permissibility of emancipating the fetus in utero without freeing the mother. This ruling highlights the Hanafi view that the fetus is a distinct legal person with independent capacity for ownership and freedom. The proof comes from the practice of the tabi'is, particularly Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act is a master freeing the fetus (haml) in his slave-woman's womb. The ruling is that the fetus becomes free and the mother does not become free.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? A statement from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i: 'When a man frees his female slave and excepts what is in her womb, then he has what he excepted.' This is reported in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.
The proof is a qawl tabi'i, considered a valid source in Hanafi fiqh for matters not contradicting Quran and Sunnah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does this proof support the ruling? The tabi'i explicitly states that if the master makes an exception for the fetus, the fetus remains in his ownership; conversely, if he frees the fetus specifically, it becomes free. The exception implies the fetus is a separate entity from the mother.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Does any school disagree? The text does not mention ikhtilaf here, but the Hanafi reliance on qawl tabi'i may be contested by schools that require hadith for such rulings.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi school adopts this view as mufta bihi, as later Hanafi works confirm that a fetus can be freed separately.
Authority weight: nawadir.

Source Text

كِتَابُ الْعِتْقِ
١٨ وَإِنْ أَعْتَقَ الْحَمْلَ خَاصَّةً عَتَقَ وَلَمْ تَعْتِقَ الأُمُّ ول. وَإِذَا أَعْتَقَ عَبْدَهُ عَلَى مَالٍ فَقَبِلَ الْعَبْدُ ذَلِكَ عَتَقَ وَلَزِمَهُ الْمَالُ
٢٠ وَإِنْ قَالَ: إِنْ أَدَّيْت إِلَيَّ أَلْفًا فَأَنْتَ حُرّ صَحَ وَلَوْمَهُ الْمَالُ وَصَارَ مَأْذُونَا
وجه : (ا) قول التابعى لثبوت وَإِنْ أَعْتَقَ الْحَمْلَ خَاصَّةً عَتَقَ \ عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ قَالَ: «إِذَا أَعْتَقَ الرَّجُلُ أَمَتَهُ، وَاسْتَثْنَى مَا فِي بَطْنِهَا فَلَهُ مَا اسْتَغْنَى، مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابُ الرَّجُلِ يُعْتِقُ أَمَتَهُ وَيَسْتَثْنِي مَا فِي بَطْنِهَا وَالرَّجُلُ يَشْتَرِي ابْنَهُ، نمبر 16800)
وجه: (٢) قول التابعى لثبوت وَإِنْ أَعْتَقَ الْحَمْلَ خَاصَّةً عَتَقَ \ وَلَمْ يَعْتِقْهَا لَمْ يُعْتَقْ إِلَّا مَا فِي بَطْنِها ، مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابُ الرَّجُلِ يُعْتِقُ أَمَتَهُ وَيَسْتَغْنِي مَا فِي بَطْنِهَا وَالرَّجُلُ يَشْتَرِي ابنه، نمبر 16800)
19 وجه : (ا) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا أَعْتَقَ عَبْدَهُ عَلَى مَالٍ \ عَنْ سَفِينَةَ قَالَ: «كُنْتُ مَمْلُوكًا لِأُمّ سَلَمَةَ، فَقَالَتْ: أُعْتِقُكَ، وَأَشْتَرِطُ عَلَيْكَ أَنْ تَخْدُمَ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم مَا عِشْتَ فَقُلْتُ: وَإِنْ لَمْ تَشْتَرِطِي عَلَيَّ مَا فَارَقْتُ رَسُولَ اللهِ الله لا مَا عِشْتُ فَأَعْتَقَتْنِي وَاشْتَرَطَتْ عَلَيَّ، (سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ : فِي الْعِتْقِ عَلَى شَرْطِ،نمبر3932)
وجه (۲)قول الصحابي لثبوت وَإِذَا أَعْتَقَ عَبْدَهُ عَلَى مَالٍ أَأَعْتَقَ عُمَرُ بْنُ الْخَطَّابِ كُلَّ مُسْلِمٍ مِنْ رَقِيقِ الْإِمَارَةِ، وَشَرَطَ أَنَّكُمْ تَخْدِمُونَ الْخَلِيفَةَ مِنْ بَعْدِي بِثَلَاثِ سِنِينَ،(مصنف عبدالرزاق بَابُ الْعِتْقِ بِالشَّرْطِ نمبر 16779
٢٠ وجه (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَإِنْ قَالَ: إِنْ أَدَّيْت \ ِإلَى أَلْفًا \ وَسَمِعْتُ أَبَا حَنِيفَةَ، سُئِلَ عَنْ رَجُلٍ قَالَ: لِغُلَامِهِ إِذَا أَدَّيْتَ إِلَيَّ مِائَةَ دِينَارٍ فَأَنْتَ حُرٌّ ، مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابُ الْعِتْقِ بالشَّرْطِ غمبر 16788)
وجه (۲) قول التابعى لثبوت وَإِنْ قَالَ : إِنْ أَدَّيْت إِلَيَّ أَلْفًا \ عَنِ ابْنِ شُبْرُمَةَ قَالَ: «إِذَا قَالَ الرَّجُلُ لِعَبْدِهِ أَنْتَ حُرٌّ عَلَى أَنْ تَخْدِمُني عَشْرَ سِنِينَ فَلَهُ شَرْطُهُ، (مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابُ الْعِتْقِ بالشَّرْطِ نمبر 16787)
اصول : خدمت کی شرط پر غلام آزاد کیا تو غلام آزاد ہو گا اور خدمت لازم ہو گی۔ اصول آزادگی کو مال ادا کرنے پر معلق کیا، لہذا جب تک مال ادا نہیں کرے گا اس وقت تک آزادی نہ ہو گی۔
فَإِنْ أَحْضَرَ الْمَالَ أُجْبِرَ الْمَوْلَى عَلَى قَبْضِهِ وَعَتَقَ الْعَبْدُ ۲۲ وَوَلَدُ الْأَمَةِ مِنْ مَوْلَاهَا حُرٌّ وَوَلَدُهَا مِنْ زَوْجِهَا مَمْلُوكٌ لِسَيّدِهَا وَوَلَدُ الحَرَّةِ مِنْ الْعَبْدِ حُرٌّ
ال وجه (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت فَإِنْ أَحْضَرَ الْمَالَ أُخبِرَ الْمَوْلَى \ عَنِ الثَّوْرِيِّ قَالَ: إِذَا قَالَ لِعَبْدِهِ: " إِذَا أَدَّيْتَ إِلَيَّ أَلْفَ دِرْهَمٍ فَأَنْتَ حُرِّثُمَّ بَدَا لَهُ أَنْ لَا يَقْبَلَ مِنْهُ شَيْئًا كَانَ ذَلِكَ لِلسَّيِّدِ، بَابُ الْعِتْقِ بِالشَّرْطِ، 16799)
۲۲ وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَوَلَدُ الْأَمَةِ مِنْ مَوْلَاهَا حُرٌّ \ عَنْ سَمُرَةَ بْنِ جُنْدُبٍ فِيمَا يَحْسَبُ حَمَّادٌ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «مَنْ مَلَكَ ذَا رَحِمٍ مَحْرَمٍ فَهُوَ حُرٌّ ، ابوداودشريف، بَابٌ : فِيمَنْ مَلَكَ ذَا
رَحِمٍ مَحرَم، نمبر 3949// ترمذي شريف ، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِيمَنْ مَلَكَ ذَا رَحِمٍ مَحْرَمٍ، نمبر 1365)
وجه (۲) قول الصحابى لثبوت وَوَلَدُ الأَمَةِ مِنْ مَوْلاهَا حُرِّ اعَن ابْن عُمَرَ ، قَالَ: «وَلَدُ الْمُدَبَّرَةِ يُعْتَقُونَ بِعِلْقِهَا ، وَيُرَقُونَ بِرِقَهَا، (سنن دارقطني كِتَابُ الْمُكَاتَبِ، نمبر 4257/سنن بيهقي، بَابٌ: مَا جَاءَ فِي وَلَدِ الْمُدَبَّرَةِ مِنْ غَيْرِ سَيّدِهَا بَعْدَ تَدْبِيرِهَا، نمبر 21584)
وجه (۳) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَوَلَدُ الْأَمَةِ مِنْ مَوْلَاهَا حُرّ اعن عَلِي له قَالَ: " وَلَدُهَا منزِلَتِهَا " ، - يَعْنِي الْمُكَاتَبَةَ، (مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابٌ: وَلَدُ الْمُكَاتَبِ مِنْ جَارِيَتِهِ، وَوَلَدُ الْمُكَاتَبَةِ مِنْ زَوْجِهَا ، نمبر 21699)
اصول: آقا شرط پر عمل نہ کرے تو قاضی اس پر اجبار کرے گا۔ اصول: بچہ ماں آزاد ماں کے تابع ہو کر آزاد ہو گا اگر چہ باپ غلام ہو اور ان سے اس بچہ کا نسب ثابت ہو گا۔
Book of Emancipation. 18: If he frees the fetus specifically, it becomes free and the mother does not become free. And if he frees his slave for a consideration and the slave accepts that, he becomes free and the consideration is obligatory upon him. 20: And if he says, 'If you pay me one thousand, then you are free,' it is valid, the payment is obligatory upon him, and he becomes a permitted (ma'dhun). Proof (1): Statement of the Tabi'i for establishing 'And if he frees the fetus specifically, it becomes free': from Ibrahim who said, 'When a man frees his female slave and excepts what is in her womb, then he has what he excepted' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter ...). Proof (2): Statement of the Tabi'i ... Proof for 19(1): Hadith for establishing 'And if he frees his slave for a consideration': from Safinah who said, 'I was a slave of Umm Salamah, and she said, I free you on condition that you serve the Messenger of Allah (SAW) as long as you live...' Proof (2): Statement of the Companion ... Proof for 20(1): Statement of the Tabi'i ... Proof (2): Statement of the Tabi'i ... Principle: If a slave is freed on condition of service, the slave becomes free and service is obligatory. Principle: If emancipation is suspended on payment of money, then as long as he does not pay, he is not free. Then if he brings the money, the master is forced to accept it and the slave becomes free. 22: The child of a female slave from her master is free, her child from her husband is a slave belonging to her owner, and the child of a free woman from a slave is free. Proof (1): Statement of the Tabi'i ... Proof (1) for 22: Hadith ... from Samurah ibn Jundub that the Prophet (SAW) said, 'Whoever owns a close relative (mahram) is free.' Proof (2): Statement of the Companion ... Proof (3): Statement of the Companion ... Principle: If the master does not fulfill the condition, the judge forces him. Principle: A child follows the mother's status; it becomes free if she is free, even if the father is a slave, and lineage is established.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is from the beginning of Kitab al-'Itq (Book of Emancipation) in Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, with the addition of proofs from hadith and athar. The text presents several rulings on emancipating slaves. First: It is permissible to free only the fetus in the womb without freeing the mother; the child becomes free while the mother remains a slave. This is supported by the practice of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i and another tabi'i. Second: If a master frees his slave in exchange for payment and the slave accepts, the emancipation is valid and the payment becomes due. Proof is from a hadith about Safinah freed by Umm Salamah on condition of service, and from the action of Umar ibn al-Khattab. Third: If a master says to his slave, 'If you pay me one thousand, then you are free,' this is a valid conditional emancipation. The slave must pay the amount, and during the period before payment, the slave becomes a ma'dhun (permitted to engage in trade). If the slave brings the money, the master is compelled to accept it and the slave becomes free. Proofs come from tabi'is including a question posed to Abu Hanifah and a statement of Ibn Shubrumah. A key principle is that when emancipation is conditioned on payment, freedom only occurs upon actual payment. Finally, the text addresses lineage: a child of a female slave by her master is free (since the master owns the child); a child of a female slave by another slave is a slave of the master; and a child of a free woman by a slave is free. Proofs include the famous hadith 'Whoever owns a close relative is free' and statements of Ibn Umar and Ali. The Urdu notes clarify that the judge enforces the condition if the master refuses, and that the child's status follows the mother's freedom.

Key Terms
عتق ('Itq): Emancipation of a slave.
حمل (Hamal): Fetus or unborn child.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, if a master frees the fetus of his pregnant slave, what is the status of the mother?
A) She becomes free as well.
B) She remains a slave.
C) She becomes free only if she is also named.
D) Her status depends on whether the master intends it.

Key Takeaway
A fetus can be emancipated separately from its mother; they are distinct legal persons.

Conditional Emancipation for Payment
Rulings on freeing slave for payment and conditional emancipation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on freeing a slave for a consideration (al-'itq 'ala mal) and conditional emancipation suspended on payment, and identify the proofs from hadith and athar.

Core Idea
A slave freed for payment becomes free upon acceptance; if freedom is conditioned on payment, it only occurs upon actual payment.

This lesson covers two related rulings: freeing a slave immediately in exchange for a sum (al-'itq 'ala mal) and suspending emancipation on the condition that the slave pays a specified amount (ta'liq bi'l-ada'). The text provides proofs from a hadith of Safinah and from the practice of 'Umar and the tabi'is. Understanding these rulings is crucial for the concept of mukatabah and ma'dhun status.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two acts and their rulings
First: master says 'I free you for 1000 dirhams' and slave accepts → slave becomes free and must pay. Second: master says 'If you pay me 1000, then you are free' → valid conditional emancipation; slave must pay and becomes ma'dhun in the interim.
The difference is timing of freedom: immediate vs contingent on payment.
2
Locate the proofs for the first ruling
Hadith: Safinah was freed by Umm Salamah on condition of serving the Prophet. Also, 'Umar freed Muslims in the army on condition of service. These show that freeing with a condition is valid.
The hadith is from Sunan Abi Dawud; the athar from Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.
3
Locate the proofs for the second ruling
Tabi'i statements: Abu Hanifah was asked about a man saying 'If you pay me 100 dinars, you are free' and Ibn Shubrumah said if a man says 'You are free on condition you serve me 10 years', the condition is binding.
These establish the validity of conditional emancipation.
4
Understand the effect of the condition
During the period before payment, the slave becomes a ma'dhun (permitted to trade). Once the slave brings the money, the master is forced to accept it and the slave becomes free.
The judge enforces this if the master refuses.
5
Note the principle
The Urdu note says: 'If emancipation is suspended on payment, as long as he does not pay, he is not free. If he brings the money, the master is forced to accept and the slave becomes free.'
This is a key principle of conditional emancipation.

وجه (۲)قول الصحابي لثبوت وَإِذَا أَعْتَقَ عَبْدَهُ عَلَى مَالٍ أَأَعْتَقَ عُمَرُ بْنُ الْخَطَّابِ كُلَّ مُسْلِمٍ مِنْ رَقِيقِ الْإِمَارَةِ، وَشَرَطَ أَنَّكُمْ تَخْدِمُونَ الْخَلِيفَةَ مِنْ بَعْدِي بِثَلَاثِ سِنِينَ،(مصنف عبدالرزاق بَابُ الْعِتْقِ بِالشَّرْطِ نمبر 16779
٢٠ وجه (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَإِنْ قَالَ: إِنْ أَدَّيْت \ ِإلَى أَلْفًا \ وَسَمِعْتُ أَبَا حَنِيفَةَ، سُئِلَ عَنْ رَجُلٍ قَالَ: لِغُلَامِهِ إِذَا أَدَّيْتَ إِلَيَّ مِائَةَ دِينَارٍ فَأَنْتَ حُرٌّ ، مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابُ الْعِتْقِ بالشَّرْطِ غمبر 16788)
وجه (۲) قول التابعى لثبوت وَإِنْ قَالَ : إِنْ أَدَّيْت إِلَيَّ أَلْفًا \ عَنِ ابْنِ شُبْرُمَةَ قَالَ: «إِذَا قَالَ الرَّجُلُ لِعَبْدِهِ أَنْتَ حُرٌّ عَلَى أَنْ تَخْدِمُني عَشْرَ سِنِينَ فَلَهُ شَرْطُهُ، (مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابُ الْعِتْقِ بالشَّرْطِ نمبر 16787)
اصول : خدمت کی شرط پر غلام آزاد کیا تو غلام آزاد ہو گا اور خدمت لازم ہو گی۔ اصول آزادگی کو مال ادا کرنے پر معلق کیا، لہذا جب تک مال ادا نہیں کرے گا اس وقت تک آزادی نہ ہو گی۔
فَإِنْ أَحْضَرَ الْمَالَ أُجْبِرَ الْمَوْلَى عَلَى قَبْضِهِ وَعَتَقَ الْعَبْدُ ۲۲ وَوَلَدُ الْأَمَةِ مِنْ مَوْلَاهَا حُرٌّ وَوَلَدُهَا مِنْ زَوْجِهَا مَمْلُوكٌ لِسَيّدِهَا وَوَلَدُ الحَرَّةِ مِنْ الْعَبْدِ حُرٌّ
ال وجه (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت فَإِنْ أَحْضَرَ الْمَالَ أُخبِرَ الْمَوْلَى \ عَنِ الثَّوْرِيِّ قَالَ: إِذَا قَالَ لِعَبْدِهِ: " إِذَا أَدَّيْتَ إِلَيَّ أَلْفَ دِرْهَمٍ فَأَنْتَ حُرِّثُمَّ بَدَا لَهُ أَنْ لَا يَقْبَلَ مِنْهُ شَيْئًا كَانَ ذَلِكَ لِلسَّيِّدِ، بَابُ الْعِتْقِ بِالشَّرْطِ، 16799)
۲۲ وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَوَلَدُ الْأَمَةِ مِنْ مَوْلَاهَا حُرٌّ \ عَنْ سَمُرَةَ بْنِ جُنْدُبٍ فِيمَا يَحْسَبُ حَمَّادٌ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «مَنْ مَلَكَ ذَا رَحِمٍ مَحْرَمٍ فَهُوَ حُرٌّ ، ابوداودشريف، بَابٌ : فِيمَنْ مَلَكَ ذَا
رَحِمٍ مَحرَم، نمبر 3949// ترمذي شريف ، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِيمَنْ مَلَكَ ذَا رَحِمٍ مَحْرَمٍ، نمبر 1365)
وجه (۲) قول الصحابى لثبوت وَوَلَدُ الأَمَةِ مِنْ مَوْلاهَا حُرِّ اعَن ابْن عُمَرَ ، قَالَ: «وَلَدُ الْمُدَبَّرَةِ يُعْتَقُونَ بِعِلْقِهَا ، وَيُرَقُونَ بِرِقَهَا، (سنن دارقطني كِتَابُ الْمُكَاتَبِ، نمبر 4257/سنن بيهقي، بَابٌ: مَا جَاءَ فِي وَلَدِ الْمُدَبَّرَةِ مِنْ غَيْرِ سَيّدِهَا بَعْدَ تَدْبِيرِهَا، نمبر 21584)
وجه (۳) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَوَلَدُ الْأَمَةِ مِنْ مَوْلَاهَا حُرّ اعن عَلِي له قَالَ: " وَلَدُهَا منزِلَتِهَا " ، - يَعْنِي الْمُكَاتَبَةَ، (مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابٌ: وَلَدُ الْمُكَاتَبِ مِنْ جَارِيَتِهِ، وَوَلَدُ الْمُكَاتَبَةِ مِنْ زَوْجِهَا ، نمبر 21699)
اصول: آقا شرط پر عمل نہ کرے تو قاضی اس پر اجبار کرے گا۔ اصول: بچہ ماں آزاد ماں کے تابع ہو کر آزاد ہو گا اگر چہ باپ غلام ہو اور ان سے اس بچہ کا نسب ثابت ہو گا۔
Book of Emancipation. 18: If he frees the fetus specifically, it becomes free and the mother does not become free. And if he frees his slave for a consideration and the slave accepts that, he becomes free and the consideration is obligatory upon him. 20: And if he says, 'If you pay me one thousand, then you are free,' it is valid, the payment is obligatory upon him, and he becomes a permitted (ma'dhun). Proof (1): Statement of the Tabi'i for establishing 'And if he frees the fetus specifically, it becomes free': from Ibrahim who said, 'When a man frees his female slave and excepts what is in her womb, then he has what he excepted' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter ...). Proof (2): Statement of the Tabi'i ... Proof for 19(1): Hadith for establishing 'And if he frees his slave for a consideration': from Safinah who said, 'I was a slave of Umm Salamah, and she said, I free you on condition that you serve the Messenger of Allah (SAW) as long as you live...' Proof (2): Statement of the Companion ... Proof for 20(1): Statement of the Tabi'i ... Proof (2): Statement of the Tabi'i ... Principle: If a slave is freed on condition of service, the slave becomes free and service is obligatory. Principle: If emancipation is suspended on payment of money, then as long as he does not pay, he is not free. Then if he brings the money, the master is forced to accept it and the slave becomes free. 22: The child of a female slave from her master is free, her child from her husband is a slave belonging to her owner, and the child of a free woman from a slave is free. Proof (1): Statement of the Tabi'i ... Proof (1) for 22: Hadith ... from Samurah ibn Jundub that the Prophet (SAW) said, 'Whoever owns a close relative (mahram) is free.' Proof (2): Statement of the Companion ... Proof (3): Statement of the Companion ... Principle: If the master does not fulfill the condition, the judge forces him. Principle: A child follows the mother's status; it becomes free if she is free, even if the father is a slave, and lineage is established.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is from the beginning of Kitab al-'Itq (Book of Emancipation) in Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, with the addition of proofs from hadith and athar. The text presents several rulings on emancipating slaves. First: It is permissible to free only the fetus in the womb without freeing the mother; the child becomes free while the mother remains a slave. This is supported by the practice of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i and another tabi'i. Second: If a master frees his slave in exchange for payment and the slave accepts, the emancipation is valid and the payment becomes due. Proof is from a hadith about Safinah freed by Umm Salamah on condition of service, and from the action of Umar ibn al-Khattab. Third: If a master says to his slave, 'If you pay me one thousand, then you are free,' this is a valid conditional emancipation. The slave must pay the amount, and during the period before payment, the slave becomes a ma'dhun (permitted to engage in trade). If the slave brings the money, the master is compelled to accept it and the slave becomes free. Proofs come from tabi'is including a question posed to Abu Hanifah and a statement of Ibn Shubrumah. A key principle is that when emancipation is conditioned on payment, freedom only occurs upon actual payment. Finally, the text addresses lineage: a child of a female slave by her master is free (since the master owns the child); a child of a female slave by another slave is a slave of the master; and a child of a free woman by a slave is free. Proofs include the famous hadith 'Whoever owns a close relative is free' and statements of Ibn Umar and Ali. The Urdu notes clarify that the judge enforces the condition if the master refuses, and that the child's status follows the mother's freedom.

Key Terms
عتق على مال ('Itq 'ala mal): Emancipation in exchange for payment.
مأذون (Ma'dhun): Slave permitted to trade.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what happens when a master says to his slave, 'If you pay me 1000, then you are free,' and the slave brings the money?
A) The master can refuse and the slave remains a slave.
B) The master is forced to accept and the slave becomes free.
C) The slave becomes free only if the master also signs a document.
D) The slave becomes free only after paying twice the amount.

Key Takeaway
Immediate freeing for payment creates freedom with a debt; conditional freeing suspends freedom until payment, with the master forced to accept the payment.

Lineage and Status of Children of Slaves and Free Women
Rulings on children's status based on parents' slavery/freedom

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rules on the status of children born to a female slave by her master versus by another slave, and the child of a free woman by a slave, citing the hadith on owning close relatives.

Core Idea
A child's status follows the mother: child of a female slave is a slave unless by master; child of a free woman is free regardless of father.

This lesson addresses the legal status of children born from different types of marriages or unions involving slaves and free persons. The rulings clarify that the mother's status is determinative: the child of a female slave by her master is free (since the master owns the child through ownership), the child of a female slave by another slave is a slave of the master, and the child of a free woman by a slave is free. The proofs include a famous hadith and statements of Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Three scenarios: (1) child of a female slave (amah) from her master, (2) child of a female slave from her husband (a slave), (3) child of a free woman (hurrah) from a slave husband.
2
State the ruling for each
(1) Child is free (because the master owns the child). (2) Child is a slave belonging to the master. (3) Child is free (follows mother's status).
3
Locate the proofs
Proof (1) for 'child of amah from master is free': Hadith: 'Whoever owns a close relative (mahram) is free.' Also, statements of Ibn 'Umar and 'Ali. Proof (2) for 'child of amah from slave is slave': Implied by the rule that child follows mother's status. Proof (3) for 'child of free woman from slave is free': Same principle: child follows mother.
The hadith is from Sunan Abi Dawud and Tirmidhi.
4
Understand the underlying principle
The child's status follows the mother's status (al-walad li'l-firash wa li'l-umm). The father's status is irrelevant for freedom/slavery determination. However, lineage is established from both parents.
An exception: if the father is the master, the child is free because the master cannot own his own child (as per the hadith).
5
Note the Urdu note on lineage
The Urdu note says: 'The child follows the mother's status; it becomes free if she is free, even if the father is a slave, and lineage is established.' This confirms the principle.

كِتَابُ الْعِتْقِ
١٨ وَإِنْ أَعْتَقَ الْحَمْلَ خَاصَّةً عَتَقَ وَلَمْ تَعْتِقَ الأُمُّ ول. وَإِذَا أَعْتَقَ عَبْدَهُ عَلَى مَالٍ فَقَبِلَ الْعَبْدُ ذَلِكَ عَتَقَ وَلَزِمَهُ الْمَالُ
٢٠ وَإِنْ قَالَ: إِنْ أَدَّيْت إِلَيَّ أَلْفًا فَأَنْتَ حُرّ صَحَ وَلَوْمَهُ الْمَالُ وَصَارَ مَأْذُونَا
وجه : (ا) قول التابعى لثبوت وَإِنْ أَعْتَقَ الْحَمْلَ خَاصَّةً عَتَقَ \ عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ قَالَ: «إِذَا أَعْتَقَ الرَّجُلُ أَمَتَهُ، وَاسْتَثْنَى مَا فِي بَطْنِهَا فَلَهُ مَا اسْتَغْنَى، مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابُ الرَّجُلِ يُعْتِقُ أَمَتَهُ وَيَسْتَثْنِي مَا فِي بَطْنِهَا وَالرَّجُلُ يَشْتَرِي ابْنَهُ، نمبر 16800)
وجه: (٢) قول التابعى لثبوت وَإِنْ أَعْتَقَ الْحَمْلَ خَاصَّةً عَتَقَ \ وَلَمْ يَعْتِقْهَا لَمْ يُعْتَقْ إِلَّا مَا فِي بَطْنِها ، مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابُ الرَّجُلِ يُعْتِقُ أَمَتَهُ وَيَسْتَغْنِي مَا فِي بَطْنِهَا وَالرَّجُلُ يَشْتَرِي ابنه، نمبر 16800)
19 وجه : (ا) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا أَعْتَقَ عَبْدَهُ عَلَى مَالٍ \ عَنْ سَفِينَةَ قَالَ: «كُنْتُ مَمْلُوكًا لِأُمّ سَلَمَةَ، فَقَالَتْ: أُعْتِقُكَ، وَأَشْتَرِطُ عَلَيْكَ أَنْ تَخْدُمَ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم مَا عِشْتَ فَقُلْتُ: وَإِنْ لَمْ تَشْتَرِطِي عَلَيَّ مَا فَارَقْتُ رَسُولَ اللهِ الله لا مَا عِشْتُ فَأَعْتَقَتْنِي وَاشْتَرَطَتْ عَلَيَّ، (سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ : فِي الْعِتْقِ عَلَى شَرْطِ،نمبر3932)
وجه (۲)قول الصحابي لثبوت وَإِذَا أَعْتَقَ عَبْدَهُ عَلَى مَالٍ أَأَعْتَقَ عُمَرُ بْنُ الْخَطَّابِ كُلَّ مُسْلِمٍ مِنْ رَقِيقِ الْإِمَارَةِ، وَشَرَطَ أَنَّكُمْ تَخْدِمُونَ الْخَلِيفَةَ مِنْ بَعْدِي بِثَلَاثِ سِنِينَ،(مصنف عبدالرزاق بَابُ الْعِتْقِ بِالشَّرْطِ نمبر 16779
٢٠ وجه (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَإِنْ قَالَ: إِنْ أَدَّيْت \ ِإلَى أَلْفًا \ وَسَمِعْتُ أَبَا حَنِيفَةَ، سُئِلَ عَنْ رَجُلٍ قَالَ: لِغُلَامِهِ إِذَا أَدَّيْتَ إِلَيَّ مِائَةَ دِينَارٍ فَأَنْتَ حُرٌّ ، مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابُ الْعِتْقِ بالشَّرْطِ غمبر 16788)
وجه (۲) قول التابعى لثبوت وَإِنْ قَالَ : إِنْ أَدَّيْت إِلَيَّ أَلْفًا \ عَنِ ابْنِ شُبْرُمَةَ قَالَ: «إِذَا قَالَ الرَّجُلُ لِعَبْدِهِ أَنْتَ حُرٌّ عَلَى أَنْ تَخْدِمُني عَشْرَ سِنِينَ فَلَهُ شَرْطُهُ، (مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابُ الْعِتْقِ بالشَّرْطِ نمبر 16787)
اصول : خدمت کی شرط پر غلام آزاد کیا تو غلام آزاد ہو گا اور خدمت لازم ہو گی۔ اصول آزادگی کو مال ادا کرنے پر معلق کیا، لہذا جب تک مال ادا نہیں کرے گا اس وقت تک آزادی نہ ہو گی۔

۲۲ وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَوَلَدُ الْأَمَةِ مِنْ مَوْلَاهَا حُرٌّ \ عَنْ سَمُرَةَ بْنِ جُنْدُبٍ فِيمَا يَحْسَبُ حَمَّادٌ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «مَنْ مَلَكَ ذَا رَحِمٍ مَحْرَمٍ فَهُوَ حُرٌّ ، ابوداودشريف، بَابٌ : فِيمَنْ مَلَكَ ذَا
رَحِمٍ مَحرَم، نمبر 3949// ترمذي شريف ، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِيمَنْ مَلَكَ ذَا رَحِمٍ مَحْرَمٍ، نمبر 1365)
وجه (۲) قول الصحابى لثبوت وَوَلَدُ الأَمَةِ مِنْ مَوْلاهَا حُرِّ اعَن ابْن عُمَرَ ، قَالَ: «وَلَدُ الْمُدَبَّرَةِ يُعْتَقُونَ بِعِلْقِهَا ، وَيُرَقُونَ بِرِقَهَا، (سنن دارقطني كِتَابُ الْمُكَاتَبِ، نمبر 4257/سنن بيهقي، بَابٌ: مَا جَاءَ فِي وَلَدِ الْمُدَبَّرَةِ مِنْ غَيْرِ سَيّدِهَا بَعْدَ تَدْبِيرِهَا، نمبر 21584)
وجه (۳) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَوَلَدُ الْأَمَةِ مِنْ مَوْلَاهَا حُرّ اعن عَلِي له قَالَ: " وَلَدُهَا منزِلَتِهَا " ، - يَعْنِي الْمُكَاتَبَةَ، (مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابٌ: وَلَدُ الْمُكَاتَبِ مِنْ جَارِيَتِهِ، وَوَلَدُ الْمُكَاتَبَةِ مِنْ زَوْجِهَا ، نمبر 21699)
اصول: آقا شرط پر عمل نہ کرے تو قاضی اس پر اجبار کرے گا۔ اصول: بچہ ماں آزاد ماں کے تابع ہو کر آزاد ہو گا اگر چہ باپ غلام ہو اور ان سے اس بچہ کا نسب ثابت ہو گا۔
Book of Emancipation. 18: If he frees the fetus specifically, it becomes free and the mother does not become free. And if he frees his slave for a consideration and the slave accepts that, he becomes free and the consideration is obligatory upon him. 20: And if he says, 'If you pay me one thousand, then you are free,' it is valid, the payment is obligatory upon him, and he becomes a permitted (ma'dhun). Proof (1): Statement of the Tabi'i for establishing 'And if he frees the fetus specifically, it becomes free': from Ibrahim who said, 'When a man frees his female slave and excepts what is in her womb, then he has what he excepted' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter ...). Proof (2): Statement of the Tabi'i ... Proof for 19(1): Hadith for establishing 'And if he frees his slave for a consideration': from Safinah who said, 'I was a slave of Umm Salamah, and she said, I free you on condition that you serve the Messenger of Allah (SAW) as long as you live...' Proof (2): Statement of the Companion ... Proof for 20(1): Statement of the Tabi'i ... Proof (2): Statement of the Tabi'i ... Principle: If a slave is freed on condition of service, the slave becomes free and service is obligatory. Principle: If emancipation is suspended on payment of money, then as long as he does not pay, he is not free. Then if he brings the money, the master is forced to accept it and the slave becomes free. 22: The child of a female slave from her master is free, her child from her husband is a slave belonging to her owner, and the child of a free woman from a slave is free. Proof (1): Statement of the Tabi'i ... Proof (1) for 22: Hadith ... from Samurah ibn Jundub that the Prophet (SAW) said, 'Whoever owns a close relative (mahram) is free.' Proof (2): Statement of the Companion ... Proof (3): Statement of the Companion ... Principle: If the master does not fulfill the condition, the judge forces him. Principle: A child follows the mother's status; it becomes free if she is free, even if the father is a slave, and lineage is established.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is from the beginning of Kitab al-'Itq (Book of Emancipation) in Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, with the addition of proofs from hadith and athar. The text presents several rulings on emancipating slaves. First: It is permissible to free only the fetus in the womb without freeing the mother; the child becomes free while the mother remains a slave. This is supported by the practice of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i and another tabi'i. Second: If a master frees his slave in exchange for payment and the slave accepts, the emancipation is valid and the payment becomes due. Proof is from a hadith about Safinah freed by Umm Salamah on condition of service, and from the action of Umar ibn al-Khattab. Third: If a master says to his slave, 'If you pay me one thousand, then you are free,' this is a valid conditional emancipation. The slave must pay the amount, and during the period before payment, the slave becomes a ma'dhun (permitted to engage in trade). If the slave brings the money, the master is compelled to accept it and the slave becomes free. Proofs come from tabi'is including a question posed to Abu Hanifah and a statement of Ibn Shubrumah. A key principle is that when emancipation is conditioned on payment, freedom only occurs upon actual payment. Finally, the text addresses lineage: a child of a female slave by her master is free (since the master owns the child); a child of a female slave by another slave is a slave of the master; and a child of a free woman by a slave is free. Proofs include the famous hadith 'Whoever owns a close relative is free' and statements of Ibn Umar and Ali. The Urdu notes clarify that the judge enforces the condition if the master refuses, and that the child's status follows the mother's freedom.

Key Terms
أمة (Amah): Female slave.
محرم (Mahram): Close relative whom one cannot marry.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the status of a child born to a female slave from her master?
A) The child is a slave like the mother.
B) The child is free.
C) The child is free only if the master acknowledges paternity.
D) The child is a slave until the master frees him.

Key Takeaway
A child's freedom or slavery is determined by the mother's status, except when the father is the master, in which case the child is free.

Conditional Emancipation and Lineage of Slave Children
Matn with proofs for conditional emancipation and lineage rules

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on conditional emancipation and apply the lineage rule that a child of a slave woman by her master is free.

Core Idea
A conditional promise of emancipation becomes binding when fulfilled; the master is compelled.

This lesson tackles two interconnected issues from Kitab al-Itq: first, the binding nature of a conditional emancipation promise when the slave fulfills the condition, and second, the status of children born to slave women. The Hanafi position relies on strong proofs, including a hadith of the Prophet and statements of prominent Companions. Understanding these rulings clarifies the master's obligations and the automatic freedom of certain children.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditional emancipation ruling
Find the explicit statement: if the slave brings the money, the master is compelled to accept and the slave becomes free. Note that this makes the promise binding.
The proof cited is a statement of Sufyan al-Thawri (Tabi'i).
2
Examine the lineage rules for slave women
Three cases: child of a slave woman (1) from her master → free; (2) from another man → owned by master; (3) child of a free woman from a slave → free. Memorize these.
The key principle: the child's status follows the mother.
3
Analyze the hadith proof for the child's freedom
The hadith: 'Whoever owns a close relative (mahram), he is free.' This proves that a father owning his child (who is a mahram) results in the child's freedom.
The hadith is ahad but accepted; its implication is that the child is free because the father cannot own a mahram.
4
Review the Companion statements
Ibn Umar said the children of a mudabbara follow her freedom/enslavement. Ali said the child follows the mother's status. These support the same rule.
These athar are considered strong evidence in Hanafi usul.
5
Distinguish the Hanafi view from other schools
The Hanafi ruling makes the conditional promise binding; Shafi'is consider it a mere promise that the master can revoke. Understand the practical difference.
The judge compels the master in the Hanafi view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ أَحْضَرَ الْمَالَ أُجْبِرَ الْمَوْلَى عَلَى قَبْضِهِ وَعَتَقَ الْعَبْدُ وَوَلَدُ الْأَمَةِ مِنْ مَوْلَاهَا حُرٌّ وَوَلَدُهَا مِنْ زَوْجِهَا مَمْلُوكٌ لِسَيّدِهَا وَوَلَدُ الحَرَّةِ مِنْ الْعَبْدِ حُرٌّ ال وجه (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت فَإِنْ أَحْضَرَ الْمَالَ أُخبِرَ الْمَوْلَى \ عَنِ الثَّوْرِيِّ قَالَ: إِذَا قَالَ لِعَبْدِهِ: " إِذَا أَدَّيْتَ إِلَيَّ أَلْفَ دِرْهَمٍ فَأَنْتَ حُرِّثُمَّ بَدَا لَهُ أَنْ لَا يَقْبَلَ مِنْهُ شَيْئًا كَانَ ذَلِكَ لِلسَّيِّدِ، بَابُ الْعِتْقِ بِالشَّرْطِ، 16799) ۲۲ وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَوَلَدُ الْأَمَةِ مِنْ مَوْلَاهَا حُرٌّ \ عَنْ سَمُرَةَ بْنِ جُنْدُبٍ فِيمَا يَحْسَبُ حَمَّادٌ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «مَنْ مَلَكَ ذَا رَحِمٍ مَحْرَمٍ فَهُوَ حُرٌّ ، ابوداودشريف، بَابٌ : فِيمَنْ مَلَكَ ذَا رَحِمٍ مَحرَم، نمبر 3949// ترمذي شريف ، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِيمَنْ مَلَكَ ذَا رَحِمٍ مَحْرَمٍ، نمبر 1365) وجه (۲) قول الصحابى لثبوت وَوَلَدُ الأَمَةِ مِنْ مَوْلاهَا حُرِّ اعَن ابْن عُمَرَ ، قَالَ: «وَلَدُ الْمُدَبَّرَةِ يُعْتَقُونَ بِعِلْقِهَا ، وَيُرَقُونَ بِرِقَهَا، (سنن دارقطني كِتَابُ الْمُكَاتَبِ، نمبر 4257/سنن بيهقي، بَابٌ: مَا جَاءَ فِي وَلَدِ الْمُدَبَّرَةِ مِنْ غَيْرِ سَيّدِهَا بَعْدَ تَدْبِيرِهَا، نمبر 21584) وجه (۳) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَوَلَدُ الْأَمَةِ مِنْ مَوْلَاهَا حُرّ اعن عَلِي له قَالَ: " وَلَدُهَا منزِلَتِهَا " ، - يَعْنِي الْمُكَاتَبَةَ، (مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابٌ: وَلَدُ الْمُكَاتَبِ مِنْ جَارِيَتِهِ، وَوَلَدُ الْمُكَاتَبَةِ مِنْ زَوْجِهَا ، نمبر 21699) اصول: آقا شرط پر عمل نہ کرے تو قاضی اس پر اجبار کرے گا۔ اصول: بچہ ماں آزاد ماں کے تابع ہو کر آزاد ہو گا اگر چہ باپ غلام ہو اور ان سے اس بچہ کا نسب ثابت ہو گا۔
If he brings the money, the master is forced to accept it and the slave becomes free. And the child of a slave woman from her master is free, and her child from her husband is owned by her master, and the child of a free woman from a slave is free. Proof (1): Statement of a follower (Tabi'i) to establish: 'If he brings the money, the master is informed.' From al-Thawri, he said: 'When he says to his slave: "If you pay me one thousand dirhams you are free," then he changes his mind not to accept anything, that is for the master.' Chapter of emancipation by condition. (16799) Proof (1): Hadith to establish: 'The child of a slave woman from her master is free.' From Samurah ibn Jundub, as Hammad thinks, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever owns a close relative (mahram), he is free.' (Abu Dawood, Sunan, Book of emancipation, no. 3949; Tirmidhi, no. 1365) Proof (2): Statement of a Companion to establish: 'The child of a slave woman from her master is free.' From Ibn Umar, he said: 'The children of a mudabbara are freed by her freedom and enslaved by her enslavement.' (Sunan Darqutni, Kitab al-Mukatab, no. 4257; Sunan Bayhaqi, no. 21584) Proof (3): Statement of a Companion to establish: 'The child of a slave woman from her master is free.' From Ali (may Allah be pleased with him), he said: 'Her child follows her status' – meaning the mukataba. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, no. 21699) Principles: If the master does not act upon the condition, the judge will compel him. Principle: The child follows the free mother and becomes free even if the father is a slave, and lineage from them is established.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage presents multiple rulings from Kitab al-Itq under the chapter of emancipation by condition. The first ruling states that when a slave fulfills the condition of paying a specified amount, the master is compelled to accept it and the slave becomes free. The evidence includes the statement of Sufyan al-Thawri, a Tabi'i, who says the master cannot renege once the slave brings the money. The second set of rulings concern lineage: a child born to a slave woman by her master is free; a child born to a slave woman by someone else's slave or free man remains a slave of the master; a child born to a free woman by a slave is free. The proofs for the child of the slave woman from her master include a hadith that whoever owns a close relative (mahram) must free him, meaning the father owns his child, so the child is free. Also the athar of Ibn Umar states that children of a mudabbara follow the mother's status. Ali's statement confirms the child follows the mother's status. The Urdu notes summarize: the judge compels the master; the child follows the free mother and lineage is established.

Key Terms
عتق (itq): Emancipation of a slave, freedom from bondage.
أمة (amah): A female slave owned by a master.
مولى (mawla): Master, owner of a slave.
مدبرة (mudabbara): A slave woman who has been promised freedom upon her master's death.
مكاتبة (mukataba): A slave woman who has made a contract of kitabah to purchase her freedom in installments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on the child of a slave woman from her master?
A) The child is a slave of the master.
B) The child is free.
C) The child is free only if the master acknowledges it.
D) The child is a slave unless freed by a separate act.

Key Takeaway
A conditional emancipation promise is binding when fulfilled, and a child born to a slave woman from her master is automatically free.

Tadbir: Declaration of Freedom Upon Death
Matn and proofs defining tadbir and its legal effects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of tadbir, explain the legal restrictions on the mudabbar, and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i position regarding the sale of a mudabbar.

Core Idea
The mudabbar is free from one-third upon death; during the master's life, he cannot be sold or gifted.

Tadbir is a contract where the master declares that a slave will be free upon his death. This lesson explores the legal effects of tadbir, focusing on what the master may and may not do with the mudabbar during his lifetime. We will also examine the conflicting hadith evidence and the resulting ikhtilaf between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Identify what tadbir is and the ruling (hukm) that it is a valid contract (sahih). Note the specific wordings that create a mudabbar.
The matn lists four valid wordings.
2
Identify the legal restrictions and permissions
The mudabbar cannot be sold, gifted, or possessed by another. However, the master can use his service, hire him out, and if female, have intercourse and marry her off. List these restrictions and permissions.
These are the immediate legal effects.
3
Locate the Hanafi dalil
The Hanafi school relies on the hadith of Ibn Umar: 'The mudabbar is not sold, nor given as a gift, and he is free from one-third.' Identify this as the primary proof.
This hadith is cited in Darqutni and Bayhaqi.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i objection and opposing dalil
The Shafi'i school cites the hadith of Jabir where the Prophet sold a mudabbar. Understand how this appears to contradict the Hanafi proof.
This hadith is in Bukhari and Abu Dawood.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response and tarjih
The Hanafi response is that Jabir's hadith is interpreted as a specific case (e.g., the master needed money) or is abrogated. The ruling of non-sale is mufta bihi.
The tarjih authority is Al-Quduri's matn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ التَّدْبِيرِ
قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ - ! إِذَا قَالَ الْمَوْلَى لِعَبْدِهِ إِذَا مِتُّ فَأَنْتَ حُرٌّ أَوْ أَنْتَ حُرِّ عَنْ دُبُرٍ مِنِّي أَوْ أَنْتَ مُدَبَّرٌ أَوْ قَدْ دَبَّرْتُكَ فَقَدْ صَارَ مُدَبَّرًا لـ وَلَا يَجُوزُ لَهُ بَيْعُهُ وَلَا هِبَتُهُ وَلَا تَلِيكُهُ . وَلِلْمَوْلَى أَنْ يَسْتَخْدِمَهُ وَيُؤَاجِرَهُ وَإِنْ كَانَتْ أَمَةً وَطِئَهَا وَلَهُ أَنْ يُزَوّجَهَا
لوجه: (ا) الحديث لثبوت إِذَا قَالَ الْمَوْلَى لِعَبْدِهِ إِذَا مِتُّ فَأَنْتَ حُرٌّ \ جَابِرَ بْنَ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ رضِي الله عنهما قَالَ: «أَعْتَقَ رَجُلٌ مِنَّا عَبْدًا لَهُ عَنْ دُبُرٍ ، فَدَعَا النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِهِ فَبَاعَهُ، قَالَ جَابِرٌ: مَاتَ الْغُلَامُ عَامَ أَوَّلَ، بخاري شريف، بَابُ بَيْعِ الْمُدَبَّرِ ، نمبر 2534/ابوداود شريف،باب في بيع المدبر، نمبر 3955)
وجه : (٢) الحديث لثبوت إِذَا قَالَ الْمَوْلَى لِعَبْدِهِ إِذَا مِتُّ فَأَنْتَ حُرِّ ا عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «الْمُدَبَّرُ لَا يُبَاعُ وَلَا يُوهَبُ وَهُوَ حُرٌّ مِنَ الثُّلُثِ، سنن دارقطني، كِتَابُ الْمُكَاتَب ، غمبر 4264)
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ لَهُ بَيْعُهُ وَلَا هِبَتُهُ وَلَا تَلِيكُهُ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «الْمُدَبَّرُ لَا يُبَاعُ وَلَا يُوهَبُ وَهُوَ حُرٌّ مِنَ القُلُثِ، (سنن دارقطني، كتاب المكاتب، نمبر 4264 / سنن بيهقي، بَابٌ: مَنْ قَالَ: لَا يُبَاعُ الْمُدَبَّرُ ، 21572)
وجه (۱) دليل الشافعى الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ لَهُ بَيْعُهُ وَلَا هِبَتُهُ وَلَا تَعْلِيكُهُ \ جَابِرَ بْنَ عَبْدِ الله رضي الله عنهما قَالَ: «أَعْتَقَ رَجُلٌ مِنَّا عَبْدًا لَهُ عَنْ دُبُرٍ، فَدَعَا النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِهِ فَبَاعَهُ، قَالَ جَابِرٌ: مَاتَ الْغُلَامُ عَامَ أَوَّلَ ، بخاري شريف، بَابُ بَيْعِ الْمُدَبَّرِ ، نمبر 2534/ابوداود شريف،باب في بيع المدبر،نمبر 3955)
وجه: (ا) الحديث لثبوت وَلِلْمَوْلَى أَنْ يَسْتَخْدِمَهُ وَيُؤَاجِرَهُ \ عَنْ جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «لَا بَأْسَ بِبَيْعِ خَدَمَةِ الْمُدَبَّرِ إِذَا احْتَاجَ (سنن داروطني، كِتَابُ الْمُكَاتَبِ، غمبر (4261) وجه : (۲) قول الصحابى لثبوت وَلِلْمَوْلَى أَنْ يَسْتَخْدِمَهُ وَيُؤَاجِرَهُ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ، أَنَّهُ دَبَّرَ جَارِيَتَيْنِ لَهُ، فَكَانَ يَطَؤُهُمَا وَهُمَا مُدَبَّرَتَانِ، سنن بيهقي، بَابٌ: وَطْءُ الْمُدَبَّرَةِ، نمبر 21581) اصول: مد بر غلام کو صرف آزاد کیا جا سکتا ہے، شبہ آزادگی کی وجہ سے ہبہ اور فروخت نہیں کیا جاسکتا۔
Book of Tadbir. He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: When the master says to his slave: 'If I die you are free' or 'you are free upon my death' or 'you are mudabbar' or 'I have made you mudabbar,' he becomes mudabbar. It is not permissible for him to sell him, nor to give him as a gift, nor to give him as a possession. The master may use him for service and hire him out. If she is a female slave, he may have intercourse with her and he may marry her off. Proof (1): Hadith to establish: 'When the master says to his slave: If I die you are free.' from Jabir ibn Abdullah (may Allah be pleased with them both) who said: 'A man from among us freed his slave upon his death (mudabbar), then the Prophet (peace be upon him) called for him and sold him.' Jabir said: 'The boy died the first year.' (Bukhari, Book of selling the mudabbar, no. 2534; Abu Dawood, no. 3955) Proof (2): Hadith to establish: 'When the master says to his slave: If I die you are free.' from Ibn Umar, that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The mudabbar is not sold, nor given as a gift, and he is free from one-third.' (Sunan Darqutni, no. 4264) Proof (1) to establish: 'It is not permissible to sell him, nor give him as a gift, nor give him as a possession.' from Ibn Umar, that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The mudabbar is not sold, nor given as a gift, and he is free from one-third.' (Sunan Darqutni, no. 4264; Bayhaqi, no. 21572) Proof (1) for the Shafi'i argument to establish: 'It is not permissible to sell him, nor give him as a gift, nor give him as a possession (tamlik).' from Jabir ibn Abdullah (may Allah be pleased with them both) who said: 'A man from among us freed his slave upon his death (mudabbar), then the Prophet (peace be upon him) called for him and sold him.' (Bukhari, no. 2534; Abu Dawood, no. 3955) Proof (1) to establish: 'The master may use him for service and hire him out.' from Jabir ibn Abdullah, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no harm in selling the service of the mudabbar when he needs it.' (Sunan Darqutni, no. 4261) Proof (2) to establish: 'The master may use him and hire him out.' from Ibn Umar, that he made two slave girls mudabbar and then had intercourse with them while they were mudabbar. (Sunan Bayhaqi, no. 21581) Principle: The mudabbar slave can only be freed; due to the semblance of freedom, he cannot be gifted or sold.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage defines tadbir, a contract where the slave becomes free upon the master's death. The matn states that if the master uses any of the specified wordings (e.g., 'you are free after my death'), the slave becomes mudabbar. Once mudabbar, the master cannot sell or gift the slave because he has a right to future freedom. However, the master may still use his services, hire him out, and if the slave is female, he may have intercourse with her and arrange her marriage. The proofs include conflicting hadith: one where the Prophet sold a mudabbar (used by Shafi'i to allow sale), and another where the Prophet said the mudabbar is not sold (Hanafi position). The Hanafi response is indicated by the second hadith, and the first is interpreted as applying before the master's death? The text also cites Ibn Umar's practice. The Urdu note clarifies: the mudabbar can only be freed; due to the semblance of freedom, he cannot be gifted or sold.

Key Terms
تدبير (tadbir): A declaration by the master that a slave will be free upon the master's death.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave who has been promised freedom upon the master's death.
دبر (dubur): Literally 'back', used idiomatically for 'after (my death)'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Permissible because the master owns him.
B) Not permissible, based on the hadith of Ibn Umar.
C) Permissible only with the slave's consent.
D) Not permissible, based on the hadith of Jabir.

Key Takeaway
The mudabbar cannot be sold or gifted due to his vested right to freedom upon the master's death.
