Tadbir: Definition and Prohibition of Sale (Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute)
Definition of tadbir and prohibition of sale/gift with proofs and inter-school dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on selling a mudabbar and defend it against the Shafi'i counter-argument using the hadith of Ibn Umar.

Core Idea
Tadbir creates a right to freedom; the mudabbar cannot be sold or gifted.

Tadbir is a unique form of manumission that takes effect upon the master's death. Once a master declares a slave mudabbar, the slave acquires a 'semblance of freedom' that restricts the master's power over him. This lesson examines the definition, the immediate legal consequences, and the inter-madhhab dispute with the Shafi'i school regarding the permissibility of selling or gifting the mudabbar.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of tadbir
Identify the precise phrases that create tadbir: 'If I die, you are free', 'You are free after my death', or 'You are mudabbar'. Recognise that the declaration alone establishes the mudabbar status.
The slave becomes mudabbar immediately upon the master's statement.
2
State the Hanafi ruling on disposal
The master cannot sell, gift, or otherwise dispose of the mudabbar. This prohibition is a necessary consequence of the right to freedom that tadbir creates.
The mudabbar retains his service obligations but cannot be alienated.
3
Analyse the Hanafi proof (Ibn Umar hadith)
The Prophet said: 'The mudabbar is not sold nor given as a gift, and he is free from the third.' This is a clear prohibition directly from the Sunnah.
This hadith is the primary evidence for the Hanafi position.
4
Examine the Shafi'i counter-proof (Jabir hadith)
The Shafi'i school cites the incident where the Prophet sold a mudabbar owned by a man with no other property. This appears to contradict the prohibition.
The challenge is to reconcile these two hadiths.
5
Understand the Hanafi response and tarjih
The Hanafi response interprets the Jabir hadith as a specific case (e.g., debts or the one-third limit) and not a general permission. The general rule remains the prohibition, as supported by the Ibn Umar hadith.
The thamarah (practical consequence) is that in Hanafi law, a sale of a mudabbar is invalid; in Shafi'i law, it is valid.

Source Text

وجه (۱) دليل الشافعى الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ لَهُ بَيْعُهُ وَلَا هِبَتُهُ وَلَا تَعْلِيكُهُ \ جَابِرَ بْنَ عَبْدِ الله رضي الله عنهما قَالَ: «أَعْتَقَ رَجُلٌ مِنَّا عَبْدًا لَهُ عَنْ دُبُرٍ، فَدَعَا النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِهِ فَبَاعَهُ، قَالَ جَابِرٌ: مَاتَ الْغُلَامُ عَامَ أَوَّلَ ، بخاري شريف، بَابُ بَيْعِ الْمُدَبَّرِ ، نمبر 2534/ابوداود شريف،باب في بيع المدبر،نمبر 3955)

Book of Tadbir. Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Tadbir (manumission contingent upon the master's death) presents the foundational ruling. It begins with the definition: if the master uses certain phrases (e.g., 'you are free after my death', 'you are mudabbar'), the slave becomes a mudabbar. The immediate legal consequence is that the master loses the right to sell, gift, or otherwise dispose of the slave. However, this is not full freedom; the master can still use his services. The text then provides hadith evidence for the prohibition of sale and gift. It notes a dispute with the Shafi'i school: Imam al-Shafi'i uses the hadith of Jabir (where the Prophet sold a mudabbar) as evidence that sale is permitted. The Hanafi response is to interpret this hadith as applying to a case where the master had debts or where the mudabbar's freedom was contingent on the one-third, not as a general ruling. The Urdu principle explains that the mudabbar can only be freed, not sold or gifted, due to the semblance of freedom.

Key Terms
تدبير (tadbir): A legal declaration by a master that his slave will be free upon the master's death.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave who has been promised freedom upon the master's death through tadbir.
شبه حرية (shubhat al-hurriyyah): The semblance of freedom that attaches to the mudabbar due to the promise of future manumission, which restricts the master's power of disposal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The mudabbar's right to future freedom restricts the master's power of sale and gift, making such transactions invalid in Hanafi law.

Basic Ruling of Tadbir: Slave Freed from Third of Estate
States the primary ruling of tadbir upon master's death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of tadbir upon the master's death and apply the one-third limit rule, including the sa'yah requirement.

Core Idea
A mudabbar is freed from only one-third of the estate, like a bequest.

This lesson explains the primary ruling of tadbir (future manumission). Upon the master's death, the mudabbar slave is freed from one-third of the master's wealth. If the mudabbar himself constitutes the entire estate, he must work (sa'yah) to earn two-thirds of his value for the heirs. The ruling is supported by hadith and grounded in the principle that tadbir is a bequest.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is tadbir (a contract promising emancipation after the master's death). The ruling: upon death, the mudabbar is freed from one-third of the master's estate.
2
Understand the two scenarios
If the mudabbar's value is within the one-third limit (or if the estate can cover that third), he is freed immediately. If the master has no other wealth besides the mudabbar, he must work (sa'yah) to pay two-thirds of his value to the heirs.
The sa'yah is forced labor to earn the excess beyond the third.
3
Examine the dalil
The hadith 'al-mudabbaru la yuba' wa la yuhabu wa huwa hurrun min al-thuluth' explicitly states that the mudabbar is free from the third. Also the hadith from Imran ibn Husayn illustrates the third limit in case of multiple slaves.
The hadith are ahad but have strong indication (dalala qati) on the meaning.
4
Link to bequest rules
Tadbir is treated as a bequest (wasiyyah) in Hanafi fiqh. Bequests are limited to one-third of the estate by ijma, hence the same limit applies to tadbir.
This explains why the third limit is used, not the entire estate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا مَاتَ الْمَوْلَى عَتَقَ الْمُدَبَّرُ مِنْ ثُلُثِ مَالِهِ إِنْ خَرَجَ مِنْ الثُّلُثِ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُ مَالٌ غَيْرَهُ سَعَى فِي ثُلُثَيْ قِيمَتِهِ ه توجيه: (ا) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا مَاتَ الْمَوْلَى عَتَقَ الْمُدَبَّرُ مِنْ ثُلُثِ مَالِهِ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «الْمُدَبَّرُ لَا يُبَاعُ وَلَا يُوهَبُ وَهُوَ حُرٌّ مِنَ الثُّلُثِ، (سنن دارقطني، كتاب المكاتب، نمبر 4264/ سنن بيهقي، بَابٌ : مَنْ قَالَ: لَا يُبَاعُ الْمُدَبَّرُ ، 21572) وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا مَاتَ الْمَوْلَى عَتَقَ الْمُدَبَّرُ مِنْ ثُلُثِ مَالِهِ أَعَنْ عِمْرَانَ بْنِ حُصَيْنٍ : «أَنَّ رَجُلًا أَعْتَقَ سِتَّةَ أَعْبُدٍ عِنْدَ مَوْتِهِ، وَلَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُ مَالٌ غَيْرُهُمْ، فَبَلَغَ ذَلِكَ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَقَالَ لَهُ قَوْلًا شَدِيدًا، ثُمَّ دَعَاهُمْ، فَجَزَاهُمْ ثَلَاثَةَ أَجْزَاءِ، فَأَقْرَعَ بَيْنَهُمْ: فَأَعْتَقَ اثْنَيْنِ، وَأَرَقَّ أَرْبَعَةً،(ابوداود شريف، بَابٌ : فِيمَنْ أَعْتَقَ عَبِيدًا لَهُ لَم يَبْلُغْهُمُ القُلتُ، غمبر 3958) اصول: مدبر غلام آقا کے مرنے کے بعد آقا کے تہائی مال سے آزاد ہو گا، کیونکہ مدبر وصیت کا مال ہے اور وصیت صرف تہائی مال میں جاری ہوتی ہے۔
And when the master dies, the mudabbar is freed from one-third of his wealth, if it comes out of the third. And if he has no other wealth, he works to pay two-thirds of his value. Direction: (1) The hadith for establishing: 'And when the master dies, the mudabbar is freed from one-third of his wealth' from Ibn Umar that the Prophet (PBUH) said: 'The mudabbar is not sold nor given as a gift, and he is free from the third.' (Sunan Darqutni, Book of Mukatab, no. 4264 / Sunan Bayhaqi, chapter: Whoever said the mudabbar is not sold, 21572). Aspect: (2) The hadith for establishing: 'And when the master dies, the mudabbar is freed from one-third of his wealth' from Imran ibn Husayn: 'A man freed six slaves at the time of his death, and he had no wealth other than them. That reached the Prophet (PBUH), so he spoke harshly to him, then he called them and divided them into three parts, and cast lots among them: he freed two and enslaved four.' (Abu Dawud, chapter: Regarding one who freed slaves without sufficient wealth, no. 3958). Principle: The mudabbar slave will be freed from one-third of the master's wealth after the master's death, because the mudabbar is the property of bequest, and bequest is only executed from one-third of the wealth.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage presents the primary ruling of tadbir (contract of future manumission upon the master's death). It is a ruling with proof from hadith. The matn states that upon the master's death, the mudabbar slave is freed from one-third of the master's estate. This is because tadbir is considered a type of bequest (wasiyyah), and bequests are limited to one-third of the estate. If the mudabbar's value is within the one-third limit, he is freed immediately. If the master has no other wealth besides this slave, then the mudabbar must work (sa'yah) to earn two-thirds of his value to pay to the heirs, and then he is freed. The hadith from Ibn Umar establishes the general ruling that the mudabbar is free from the third. The hadith from Imran ibn Husayn illustrates the principle that when a dying person frees slaves without enough wealth, the Prophet limited the emancipation to the third of the estate, casting lots among them. The Urdu usul clarifies the legal basis: tadbir is akin to a bequest, and bequests operate within the one-third limit.

Key Terms
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave who has been promised emancipation upon the master's death, contingent on the master's death.
تدبير (tadbir): The act of a master saying to his slave 'you are free after my death' or similar words creating a contract of future manumission.
سعاية (sa'yah): The mudabbar's effort to earn money to pay off his value when the estate is insufficient.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The slave is sold and the proceeds distributed to heirs.

Key Takeaway
The mudabbar is freed from one-third of the master's estate; if he is the only asset, he must work to earn the remaining two-thirds for the heirs.

Debt of Master Takes Precedence Over Mudabbar's Freedom
Ruling on mudabbar when master owes debt equal to his value

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a master dies with debts equal to the mudabbar's value and explain the evidence from hadith and the principle of debt priority.

Core Idea
Debt overrides tadbir: mudabbar must work to pay master's debt before freedom.

This lesson explores a specific scenario in Hanafi fiqh: what happens when a master who has made a mudabbar (a slave whose freedom is tied to the master's death) dies while owing a debt that consumes the slave's entire value? The mudabbar's freedom is conditional on the master's debts being paid first, based on clear proof from the Sunnah and the principles of inheritance and bequests.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and ruling
The passage states: 'If the master owes a debt that consumes his [the mudabbar's] value, he works to pay his entire value to his creditors.' The ruling is that the mudabbar must earn his full value to satisfy the debt before becoming free.
2
Examine the hadith proof
The primary evidence is the hadith of Jabir ibn Abdullah where the Prophet ordered the sale of a mudabbar to settle the master's debt. This shows that debt takes precedence over the tadbir contract.
The hadith is reported by Abu Dawud and Bukhari, and is considered sound (zanni al-thubut but clear in dalala).
3
Understand the underlying principle
The passage concludes: 'Before the freeing of the mudabbar, the master's debt will be paid, because the debt is paid first, then the bequest is executed.' Tadbir is treated as a bequest; therefore, debt takes priority.
This aligns with the broader Hanafi rule that debts must be settled before any bequests are fulfilled.
4
Apply to a scenario
Consider: Zaid makes his slave Amr a mudabbar, then dies with debts of 1000 dirhams, and Amr's value is 1000 dirhams. According to this ruling, Amr must work (sa'yah) to earn 1000 dirhams to pay the creditors. Only after full payment does he become free.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ كَانَ عَلَى الْوَلِي دَيْنٌ يَسْتَغْرِقُ قِيمَتَهُ سَعَى فِي جَمِيعِ قِيمَتِهِ لِغُرَمَائِهِ ل د وجه : (ا) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ كَانَ عَلَى الْوَلِي دَيْنٌ يَسْتَغْرِقُ قِيمَتَهُ عَنْ جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللهِ : «أَنَّ رَجُلًا أَعْتَقَ غُلَامًا لَهُ عَنْ دُبُرٍ مِنْهُ، وَلَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُ مَالٌ غَيْرُهُ، فَأَمَرَ بِهِ النَّي فَبِيعَ بِسَبْعِمِائَةٍ، أَوْ بِتِسْعِمِائَةٍ،( ابوداودبَابٌ : فِي بَيْعِ الْمُدَبَّرِ ، 3955/ بخاري شريف ، باب بيع المدبر،نمبر2534) وجه: (٢)قول التابعى لثبوت فَإِنْ كَانَ عَلَى الْوَلِيِّ دَيْنٌ يَسْتَغْرِقُ قِيمَتَهُ سَعَى أَعَنْ قَتَادَةَ قَالَ: «إِذَا كَانَ عَلَى سَيِّدِهِ دَيْنُ اسْتَسْعَى فِي ثَنِهِ، (مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابُ بَيْعِ الْمُدَبَّرِ، 16669/مصنف سبن ابي شيبه ، في الرجل يعتق عبده وليس له مال غيره، 23134) اصول: مدبر کی آزادگی سے پہلے آقا کا قرض ادا ہو گا، کیونکہ اول قرض ادا ہو گا ثانیا وصیت کا نفاذ ہو گا،۔
If the master owes a debt that consumes his value, the mudabbar works to pay his entire value to his creditors. Proof: (1) Hadith for establishing 'If the master owes a debt that consumes his value' from Jabir ibn Abdullah: 'A man freed his slave as a mudabbar, and he had no other wealth, so the Prophet ordered him to be sold for seven hundred or nine hundred.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on selling mudabbar, 3955 / Bukhari, chapter on selling mudabbar, no. 2534). Aspect: (2) Saying of a tabi'i for establishing 'If the master owes a debt that consumes his value, he works' from Qatada: 'If his master owes a debt, he seeks to earn in his [payment].' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on selling mudabbar, 16669 / Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, regarding a man who frees his slave and has no other wealth, 23134). Principle: Before the freeing of the mudabbar, the master's debt will be paid, because the debt is paid first, then the bequest is executed.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage addresses the situation where the master has a debt that equals the full value of the mudabbar. Since debt takes priority over bequests (and tadbir is treated as a bequest), the mudabbar must work (sa'yah) to pay his entire value to the creditors. The hadith from Jabir shows that the Prophet ordered the sale of a mudabbar to settle a debt. The statement of Qatada (a tabi'i) supports the same. The Urdu usul explains the priority: debt comes before bequest, so the mudabbar's freedom is delayed until the debt is paid. Thus, the mudabbar must earn his full value to satisfy the creditors.

Key Terms
دين (dayn): A debt owed by the master that equals or exceeds the value of the mudabbar.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave whose freedom is deferred until the master's death, akin to a bequest.
سعى (sa'yah): To work and earn money, here meaning the mudabbar's obligation to labor for his value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a master dies with debts equal to the mudabbar's value, what must the mudabbar do?
A) He is freed and the heirs must pay the debt from other assets.
B) He works to pay his entire value to the creditors, then becomes free.
C) He is sold and the proceeds go to the heirs.
D) He remains a slave and the debt is void.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, debt claims take priority over tadbir, so the mudabbar must work to pay the creditor before obtaining freedom.

Offspring of a Mudabbara Are Mudabbar
Ruling on the status of children born to a female mudabbar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a child born to a mudabbara is also mudabbar and identify the proof from the Companion's statement.

Core Idea
The child of a mudabbara follows the mother's status: mudabbar if she is, free if freed, slave if sold.

This lesson clarifies the legal status of children born to a female slave who has been promised freedom upon her master's death (tadbir). The Hanafi school holds that such children automatically share her mudabbar status. The proof comes from a saying of Ibn Umar, a Companion, which explicitly links the child's fate to the mother's. Understanding this rule helps apply the tadbir contract comprehensively.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? Here, it is the birth of a child to a female slave who is mudabbara. The ruling is that the child is also mudabbar.
The key term 'mudabbara' refers to a female slave with a tadbir contract.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is the saying of the Companion Ibn Umar (qawl sahabi). This is a recognized source of law in Hanafi usul.
The hadith is recorded in Sunan Darqutni and Sunan Bayhaqi.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Ibn Umar explicitly states that the children of a mudabbara are freed when she is freed and enslaved when she is enslaved. This directly indicates that their status follows her status.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
This is the Hanafi position. Some other schools may not automatically extend the tadbir to offspring unless specified in the contract.
The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih.
5
Evaluate the authority
The proof is a qawl sahabi, which has zanni thubut but clear dalala. It is relied upon in the Hanafi school.
Authority weight: Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَوَلَدُ الْمُدَبَّرَةِ مُدَبَّرٌ د وجه (۱) قول الصحابى لثبوت وَوَلَدُ الْمُدَبَّرَةِ مُدَبَّرٌ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ ، قَالَ: «وَلَدُ الْمُدَبَّرَةِ يُعْتَقُونَ بِعِتْقِهَا ، وَيُرَقُونَ بِرقِهَا ، ( سنن دارقطني كِتَابُ الْمُكَاتَبِ، 4257/سنن بيهقي: ، 21584)
And the child of a mudabbara is mudabbar. Proof: (1) Saying of the Companion for establishing 'And the child of a mudabbara is mudabbar' from Ibn Umar, who said: 'The children of a mudabbara are freed with her emancipation and enslaved with her enslavement.' (Sunan Darqutni, Book of Mukatab, 4257 / Sunan Bayhaqi, 21584)
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage adds a supplementary ruling: if a female slave is mudabbar, any child she bears after the tadbir contract also becomes mudabbar. The child's status follows the mother: if she is freed upon the master's death, the child is also freed; if the mother is sold or the tadbir is revoked, the child remains a slave. The proof is the saying of Ibn Umar, which explicitly states this rule. This is consistent with the Hanafi principle that the offspring of a slave woman follow her in status.

Key Terms
مدبرة (mudabbara): A female slave who has been given the tadbir contract, promised freedom upon her master's death.
مُدَبَّر (mudabbar): A slave who has been promised freedom upon the master's death. Here, the child of a mudabbara.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The child is free immediately.
B) The child is a regular slave not affected by tadbir.
C) The child is mudabbar, sharing the mother's status.
D) The child is free only if the mother is freed.

Key Takeaway
The offspring of a mudabbara is mudabbar, following the mother's status.

Conditional Tadbir: Suspended on a Specific Condition
Ruling on tadbir made conditional upon a specific event like death from a particular illness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on conditional tadbir and identify the Hadith evidence that supports its validity.

Core Idea
A tadbir is valid even when conditional; freedom occurs if the specified condition is met at death.

In this lesson, we examine a specific type of tadbir where the master sets a condition, such as 'if I die from this illness.' The Hanafi school holds such conditional manumission as valid. We will explore the ruling, the key Hadith that the Hanafis use as evidence, and how to apply it in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditional tadbir
Read the condition the master attaches: e.g. 'If I die from this illness or travel.' Note that the condition is about the cause of death.
The condition must be specific and possible.
2
State the ruling
If the master dies under the specified condition, the slave is freed just like an absolute mudabbar (from one-third of the estate).
The ruling is sahih (valid).
3
Examine the Hadith evidence
The text cites two hadith: Bukhari 2534 (Prophet sold a mudabbar) and Ibn Abi Shayba 21578 (Prophet sold a mudabbar for debt). These prove that tadbir can be conditional and that sale is allowed when needed.
The hadith from Ibn Umar (mudabbar not sold) is reconciled by permitting sale in specific cases.
4
Apply the rule
Confirm that if the condition is met, the slave is freed from the one-third of the estate, following the general rule for mudabbar.
If condition not met, the tadbir is void.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ عَلَّقَ التَّدْبِيرَ بِمَوْتِهِ عَلَى صِفَةٍ مِثْل أَنْ يَقُولَ: إِنْ مِتَ مِنْ مَرَضِي هَذَا أَوْ سَفَرِي هَذَا أَوْ مِنْ مَرَضِ كَذَا ه فَإِنْ مَاتَ الْمَوْلَى عَلَى الصِّفَةِ الَّتِي ذَكَرَهَا عَتَقَ كَمَا يَعْتِقُ الْمُدَبَّرُ ى وجه : (ا) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ عَلَّقَ التَّدْبِيرَ بِمَوْتِهِ عَلَى صِفَةٍ \ سَمِعْتُ جَابِرَ بْنَ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ رضِي الله عنهما قَالَ: «أَعْتَقَ رَجُلٌ مِنَّا عَبْدًا لَهُ عَنْ دُبُرٍ ، فَدَعَا النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِهِ فَبَاعَهُ، قَالَ جَابِرٌ: مَاتَ الْغُلَامُ عَامَ أَوَّلَ ، بخاري شريف ، بَابُ بَيْعِ الْمُدَبَّرِ، غبر 2534) وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ عَلَّقَ التَّدْبِيرَ بِمَوْتِهِ عَلَى صِفَةٍ \ عَنْ جَابِرٍ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم بَاعَ مُدَبَّرًا فِي دَيْنٍ، مصنف ابن ابي شيبه بَابٌ الْمُدَبَّرُ يَجْنِي فَيُبَاعُ فِي أَرْشِ جِنَايَتِهِ، إِلَّا أَنْ يَفْدِيَهُ سَيِّدُهُ، غمبر 21578) عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «الْمُدَبَّرُ لَا يُبَاعُ وَلَا يُوهَبُ وَهُوَ حُرٌّ مِنَ الثُّلُثِ،(سنن دارقطني كتاب المكاتب ، نمبر 4264 سنن بيهقي، بَابٌ: مَنْ قَالَ: لَا يُبَاعُ الْمُدَبَّرُ ، 21572) اصول: مدیر کی آزادگی کو کسی شرط پر معلق کرنا جائز اور مباح ہے، اگر شرط پائی جائے تو آزادی متحقق ہو گی۔ :اصول: مقید مدبر کو فروخت کرنا جائز ہے۔
If he suspends the tadbir upon his death on a condition, such as saying: 'If I die from this illness or this travel or from such illness', then if the master dies under the condition he mentioned, the slave is freed just as the mudabbar is freed. Direction: (1) Hadith for establishing 'If he suspends tadbir on a condition' from Jabir ibn Abdullah: 'A man from among us freed his slave as a mudabbar, so the Prophet called for him and sold him.' Jabir said: 'The boy died the following year.' (Bukhari, chapter on selling mudabbar, no. 2534). Aspect: (2) Hadith for establishing 'If he suspends tadbir on a condition' from Jabir: 'The Messenger of Allah sold a mudabbar for a debt.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, chapter on mudabbar who commits an injury, no. 21578) And from Ibn Umar: the Prophet said: 'The mudabbar is not sold nor given as a gift, and he is free from the third.' (Sunan Darqutni, Book of Mukatab, no. 4264 / Sunan Bayhaqi, chapter: Whoever said the mudabbar is not sold, 21572). Principle: Suspending the mudabbar's freedom on a condition is permissible and lawful; if the condition is met, freedom is realized. Principle: It is permissible to sell a restricted mudabbar.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage explains conditional tadbir. The master may say, 'If I die from this illness/travel, you are free.' This is valid and the slave becomes a mudabbar restricted to that condition. If the master dies under that condition, the slave is freed like any mudabbar. The hadith from Jabir shows that the Prophet sold a mudabbar (in a debt case), indicating that a mudabbar can be sold under certain circumstances, even though another hadith says he is not sold. The apparent contradiction is resolved by context: the mudabbar is not sold unless there is a need to settle debts. The Urdu usul notes that suspending freedom on a condition is permissible, and if the condition occurs, freedom takes effect. It also states that selling a restricted mudabbar is allowed (though this seems to contradict the first hadith, but the context is debt).

Key Terms
صِفَة (sifah): A condition or description attached to the tadbir, such as a specific illness or travel.
تدبير (tadbir): A declaration by a master that his slave will be free after his death (posthumous manumission).
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave for whom tadbir has been declared; he will be freed from one-third of the estate upon the master's death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a master says 'If I die from this disease, you are free,' and dies from that disease, what happens to the slave?
A) The slave remains a slave because the condition is invalid.
B) The slave is freed like any mudabbar, from the one-third of the estate.
C) The slave is freed immediately without any deduction.
D) The master's heirs can revoke the condition.

Key Takeaway
Conditional tadbir is valid in Hanafi fiqh; freedom is contingent upon the condition occurring at death.

Conditional Tadbir: Validity and Evidence
Ruling on tadbir conditioned on a specific description of death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for conditional tadbir and explain the hadith evidence supporting its validity.

Core Idea
A conditional tadbir is valid: freedom occurs only if the master dies under the specified condition.

Tadbir is a deferred emancipation where a master declares that his slave will be free upon his death. But what if the master conditions this on a specific description of death—like dying from a particular illness or during a journey? Is such a conditional tadbir valid? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling and its proof from the Prophet's practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the matn: conditional tadbir is valid and takes effect if the master dies under the stated condition.
2
Locate the condition
The master specifies a description (e.g., 'if I die from this illness'). Freedom is contingent on that exact description.
If the master dies from a different cause, the condition fails and the slave remains a slave.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
The commentator cites the Prophet's sale of a mudabbar (Sahih Bukhari). This shows that a mudabbar can be sold, implying that conditional tadbir is permissible and that the slave's status is not absolute.
The hadith also supports selling a muqayyad (restricted) mudabbar.
4
Understand the usul principles
Two usul principles are extracted: (1) Conditioning freedom on a condition is permissible; (2) Selling a restricted mudabbar is permissible.
These follow from the Prophet's action and the general permissibility of transactions.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, if the condition is met, the slave is freed from one-third of the master's estate (like an absolute mudabbar). If not met, no emancipation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ التَّدْبِيرِ فَإِنْ عَلَّقَ التَّدْبِيرَ بِمَوْتِهِ عَلَى صِفَةٍ مِثْل أَنْ يَقُولَ: إِنْ مِتَ مِنْ مَرَضِي هَذَا أَوْ سَفَرِي هَذَا أَوْ مِنْ مَرَضِ كَذَا فَإِنْ مَاتَ الْمَوْلَى عَلَى الصِّفَةِ الَّتِي ذَكَرَهَا عَتَقَ كَمَا يَعْتِقُ الْمُدَبَّرُ

وجه: (ا) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ عَلَّقَ التَّدْبِيرَ بِمَوْتِهِ عَلَى صِفَةٍ \ سَمِعْتُ جَابِرَ بْنَ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ رضِي الله عنهما قَالَ: «أَعْتَقَ رَجُلٌ مِنَّا عَبْدًا لَهُ عَنْ دُبُرٍ ، فَدَعَا النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِهِ فَبَاعَهُ، قَالَ جَابِرٌ: مَاتَ الْغُلَامُ عَامَ أَوَّلَ ، بخاري شريف ، بَابُ بَيْعِ الْمُدَبَّرِ، غبر 2534)

وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ عَلَّقَ التَّدْبِيرَ بِمَوْتِهِ عَلَى صِفَةٍ \ عَنْ جَابِرٍ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم بَاعَ مُدَبَّرًا فِي دَيْنٍ، مصنف ابن ابي شيبه بَابٌ الْمُدَبَّرُ يَجْنِي فَيُبَاعُ فِي أَرْشِ جِنَايَتِهِ، إِلَّا أَنْ يَفْدِيَهُ سَيِّدُهُ، غمبر 21578) عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «الْمُدَبَّرُ لَا يُبَاعُ وَلَا يُوهَبُ وَهُوَ حُرٌّ مِنَ الثُّلُثِ،(سنن دارقطني كتاب المكاتب ، نمبر 4264 سنن بيهقي، بَابٌ: مَنْ قَالَ: لَا يُبَاعُ الْمُدَبَّرُ ، 21572)

اصول: مدیر کی آزادگی کو کسی شرط پر معلق کرنا جائز اور مباح ہے، اگر شرط پائی جائے تو آزادی متحقق ہو گی۔ :اصول: مقید مدبر کو فروخت کرنا جائز ہے۔
Book of Tadbir: If he attaches the tadbir to his death on a condition, such as saying: 'If I die from this my illness or this my travel or from such an illness,' then if the master dies under the description he mentioned, he becomes free just as the mudabbar becomes free. Evidence (1) hadith to establish... (Hadith of Jabir). Evidence (2) hadith to establish... (Hadith of Jabir and Ibn Umar). Principle: It is permissible and mubah to condition the freedom of a mudabbar on a condition; if the condition occurs, freedom is realized. Principle: Selling a restricted mudabbar is permissible.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Tadbir presents a ruling on conditional tadbir. The matn states that if a master makes the emancipation of his slave contingent upon his own death under a specific description (such as dying from a particular illness or travel), then if he indeed dies under that description, the slave becomes free just like an absolute mudabbar. The commentator then provides two hadith as evidence. The first (from Jabir) shows that the Prophet sold a mudabbar, indicating that a mudabbar may be sold under certain circumstances. The second set of hadith further supports that a mudabbar can be sold for debt or for the value of injuries. The Urdu usul note summarizes: it is permissible to condition a mudabbar's freedom on a condition, and if the condition is met, freedom occurs. Additionally, a restricted mudabbar (muqayyad) may be sold.

Key Terms
التَّدْبِيرُ (al-tadbir): A declaration by a master that his slave will be free upon the master's death.
الْمُدَبَّرُ (al-mudabbar): A slave whose emancipation has been deferred to the master's death (via tadbir).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What condition must be fulfilled for a conditional tadbir to take effect?
A) The master dies from any cause.
B) The master dies under the specific description he mentioned.
C) The slave commits a crime.
D) The master sells the slave.

Key Takeaway
A conditional tadbir is valid in the Hanafi school; freedom is contingent on the master's death occurring precisely under the specified condition.

The Rulings of Umm Walad (Mother of the Child)
Rulings on umm walad with evidence from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the legal consequences of a slave woman becoming an umm walad and explain the condition for establishing the child's lineage.

Core Idea
A slave woman becomes umm walad by bearing her master's child, but lineage requires acknowledgment.

This passage from al-Quduri's matn presents the core rulings on the mother of the child (umm walad). It outlines the restrictions and permissions for the master, and crucially, the condition for establishing paternity. The evidence provided from hadith and a Companion's action reinforces these rulings and clarifies their basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal consequences
The act is a slave woman giving birth to her master's child. The ruling: she gains the status of umm walad, which brings specific prohibitions (no sale, etc.) and permissions (master may have intercourse, etc.).
Focus on the rights and restrictions listed.
2
Locate the main dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith from Ibn Abbas: 'Any man whose slave woman gives birth to his child, she is free upon his death.' This establishes her freedom at the master's death and, by implication, the prohibition of sale.
Other hadith explicitly forbid the sale of umm walads.
3
Understand the condition for lineage
The matn states: 'The lineage of her child is not established unless he acknowledges it.' The Companion Ibn Abbas refused to acknowledge his slave's child, showing that mere birth does not establish paternity.
Acknowledgment is required for the child to be considered the master's and for full umm walad status.
4
Summarize the established rulings
The umm walad cannot be sold, transferred, or gifted. The master retains rights to intercourse, service, rental, and marriage. She becomes free upon the master's death. Without acknowledgment, she does not attain full umm walad status.
These rulings are consistent across the Hanafi school.

Source Text

بَابُ الِاسْتِيلَادِ قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ - ! إِذَا وَلَدَتْ الأَمَةُ مِنْ مَوْلَاهَا فَقَدْ صَارَتْ أُمَّ وَلَدٍ لَهُ لَا يَجُوزُ بَيْعُهَا وَلَا تَلِيكُهَا وَلَا هِبَتُهَا . وَلَهُ وَطْؤُهَا وَاسْتِخْدَامُهَا وَإِجَارَتُهَا وَتَزْوِيجُهَا ۳. وَلَا يَثْبُتُ نَسَبُ وَلَدِهَا إِلَّا أَنْ يَعْتَرِفَ بِهِ

وجه: (ا) الحديث لثبوت إِذَا وَلَدَتْ الْأَمَةُ مِنْ مَوْلَاهَا فَقَدْ صَارَتْ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «أَيُّمَا رَجُلٍ وَلَدَتْ أَمَتُهُ مِنْهُ، فَهِيَ مُعْتَقَةٌ عَنْ دُبُرٍ مِنْهُ، (ابن اماجه، بَابُ أُمَّهَاتِ الأولاد، نمبر 2515)

وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت إِذَا وَلَدَتْ الْأَمَةُ مِنْ مَوْلَاهَا فَقَدْ صَارَتْ \ فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: مَنْ وَلِيُّ الْحَبَابِ؟ قِيلَ: أَخُوهُ أَبُو الْيَسَرِ بْنُ عَمْرٍو، فَبَعَثَ إِلَيْهِ فَقَالَ: أَعْتِقُوهَا، فَإِذَا سَمِعْتُمْ بِرَقِيقِ قَدِمَ عَلَيَّ فَأْتُونِي أَعَوَضْكُمْ مِنْهَا قَالَتْ : فَأَعْتَقُونِي، وَقَدِمَ عَلَى رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم رَقِيقٌ، فَعَوَّضَهُمْ مِنْ غُلَامًا، (ابوداود شريف، باب في عِتْق أُمَّهَاتِ الأولاد، غبر (3953

وجه: (ا) الحديث لثبوت إِذَا وَلَدَتْ الْأَمَةُ مِنْ مَوْلَاهَا فَقَدْ صَارَتْ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ ، قَالَ: «نَهَى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَنْ بَيْعِ أُمَّهَاتِ الْأَوْلَادِ ، لَا يُبَعْنَ وَلَا يُوهَبْنَ وَلَا يُورَثْنَ ، يَسْتَمْتِعُ بِمَا سَيِّدُهَا مَا بَدَا لَهُ فَإِذَا مَاتَ فَهِيَ حُرَّةً، سنن دارقطني كِتَابُ الْمُكَاتَبِ،نمبر4250/سنن بيهقي ، بَابُ : الرَّجُلُ يَطَأُ أَمَتَهُ بِالْمِلْكِ فَتَلِدُ لَهُ، نمبر 21763)

وجه: (١) الحديث لثبوت وَلَهُ وَطْؤُهَا وَاسْتِخْدَامُهَا وَإِجَارَتُهَا وَتَزْوِيجُهَا اعَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ ، قَالَ: «نَهَى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَنْ بَيْعِ أُمَّهَاتِ الْأَوْلادِ ، لا يُبَعْنَ وَلا يُوهَبْنَ وَلَا يُورَثْنَ ، يَسْتَمْتِعُ بِمَا سَيِّدُهَا مَا بَدَا لَهُ فَإِذَا مَاتَ فَهِيَ حُرَّةٌ، سنن دارقطني، كِتَابُ الْمُكَاتَبِ، نمبر 4250)

وجه : (۱)قول الصحابي لثبوت وَلَا يَثْبُتُ نَسَبُ وَلَدِهَا إِلَّا أَنْ يَعْتَرِفَ بِهِ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ كَانَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ يَأْتِي جَارِيَةً لَهُ ، فَحَمَلَتْ ، فَقَالَ: لَيْسَ مِنِّي ، إِنِّي أَتَيْتُهَا إِثْيَانًا ، لَا أُرِيدُ بِهِ الْوَلَدَ، (طحاوي شريف، بَابُ الأَمَةِ يَطَؤُهَا مَوْلاهَا ثُمَّ يَمُوتُ ، وَقَدْ كَانَتْ جَاءَتْ بِوَلَدٍ فِي حَيَاتِهِ هَلْ يَكُونُ ابْنَهُ وَتَكُونُ بِهِ أُمَّ وَلَدٍ أَمْ لا ، نمبر 4331)

اصول: ام ولد آقا کے مرنے کے بعد آزاد ہو جائے گی، اور ام ولد کو نہ بیچا جاسکتا ہے اور نہ مالک بنایا جاسکتا ہے۔
اصول: ام ولد کے بچہ کا نسب پہلی مرتبہ آقا کے اعتراف کے بعد ہی ثابت ہوتا ہے۔
Chapter of Istilad. He (rahimahullah) said: When a slave woman gives birth from her master, she becomes an umm walad for him. It is not permissible to sell her, nor to transfer ownership of her, nor to gift her. He has the right to have intercourse with her, employ her services, rent her out, and marry her off. And the lineage of her child is not established unless he acknowledges it. Evidence (1) hadith... (Ibn Abbas). Evidence (2) hadith... (Abu Dawud). Evidence (3) hadith... (Ibn Umar). Evidence (4) hadith... (Ibn Umar again). Evidence (5) saying of a Companion (Ibn Abbas). Principle: The umm walad becomes free after the master's death; she cannot be sold nor made property of another. Principle: The lineage of the child of an umm walad is established only after the master's first acknowledgment.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This is the chapter on Istilad (making a woman an umm walad). The matn states that when a master's slave woman gives birth to his child, she becomes an umm walad. The legal consequences are: (1) she cannot be sold, transferred, or gifted; (2) the master retains rights of intercourse, service, renting, and marrying her off; (3) the child's lineage to the master is not automatic—he must acknowledge paternity. The commentator then provides multiple ahadith and a Companion's saying as evidence. Key hadith: Ibn Abbas reports the Prophet said that any slave woman who bears her master's child becomes free upon his death (a type of tadbir). Ibn Umar reports the Prophet forbade selling umm walads. The Urdu usul notes summarize: she becomes free at the master's death, and her child's lineage, and thus her status, depends on the master's acknowledgement.

Key Terms
الِاسْتِيلَادُ (al-istilad): The act of a slave woman bearing her master's child, which grants her the status of umm walad.
أُمَّ وَلَدٍ (umm walad): A slave woman who gives birth to her master's child; she gains special protections and becomes free upon the master's death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens to an umm walad upon the death of her master?
A) She remains a slave.
B) She is freed automatically.
C) She becomes property of the master's heirs.
D) She must be sold to pay debts.

Key Takeaway
The umm walad's freedom at the master's death and her protection from sale are established by hadith, but her full status depends on the master's acknowledgment.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Ta'jiz of Mukatab
Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Ta'jiz of Mukatab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on ta'jiz of the mukatab, explain Abu Yusuf's opposing view, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) of the dispute.

Core Idea
The master can declare the mukatab incapable immediately if he has no means; Abu Yusuf requires two missed payments.

This passage from al-Quduri presents a dispute between the eponymous founders of the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa and his leading disciple Abu Yusuf. The issue is when a master can have the kitaba contract rescinded due to the mukatab's inability to pay. The disagreement turns on the interpretation of a companion report and has a direct practical impact on the rights of both parties.

Guided Path
1
State the position from the matn (Abu Hanifa)
Identify what the matn explicitly says: if the mukatab has no source of income (wajh) and the master requests ta'jiz, the judge declares him incapacitated and rescinds the kitaba. This is the default Hanafi view.
The matn does not mention any waiting period.
2
Identify Abu Yusuf's objection
Abu Yusuf directly opposes: 'He does not incapacitate him until two stars (installments) consecutively pass over him.' So he requires two consecutive missed payments.
This is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf; both are Hanafi.
3
Examine Abu Yusuf's proof
The passage quotes a hadith from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) recorded in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba: if two consecutive installments pass and the mukatab fails to pay, he is returned to slavery.
This is a mawquf hadith (companion statement).
4
Note the Hanafi response (implied)
The matn does not provide Abu Hanifa's counter-proof. However, the default position suggests that lack of wajh is sufficient grounds for ta'jiz, possibly based on istihsan or a broader view of loss of capacity.
Abu Hanifa may consider immediate inability as equivalent to effective default.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Abu Hanifa, the master can act after a single missed payment (or even before if no wajh). Under Abu Yusuf, the master must wait until two payments are missed consecutively. This affects how quickly the kitaba can be terminated.
The difference is procedural: one missed payment vs. two.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَزِيدُ عَلَى ذَلِكَ فَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُ وَجْهٌ وَطَلَبَ الْمَوْلَى تَعْجِيزَهُ عَجَّزَهُ وَفَسَخَ الْكِتَابَةَ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ لَا يُعَجِرُهُ حَتَّى يَتَوَالَى عَلَيْهِ نَجْمَانِ ه (ا) دليل ابي يوسف قول الصحابي لثبوت وَإِذَا عَجَزَ الْمُكَاتَبُ عَنْ نَجْمِ نَظَرَ الْحَاكِمُ \ عَنْ عَلِي، قَالَ: «إِذَا تَتَابَعَ عَلَى الْمُكَاتَبِ نَجْمَانِ فَدَخَلَ فِي السَّنَةِ، فَلَمْ يُؤَدِ نُجُومَهُ، رُدَّ فِي الرق»، (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه مَنْ رَدَّ الْمُكَاتَبَ إِذَا عَجَزَ ، غبر 21413)
He does not increase upon that. If he has no means and the master requests his incapacitation, he incapacitates him and rescinds the kitaba. Abu Yusuf said: He does not incapacitate him until two stars (payments) consecutively pass over him. (Proof of Abu Yusuf: Saying of the Companion for establishing: When the mukatab becomes incapable of a star, the judge looks... from Ali, he said: When two stars consecutively pass over the mukatab and he enters the year and does not pay his stars, he is returned to slavery. (Mushannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, number 21413)
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the invalidation of the kitaba contract due to the mukatab's inability to pay. According to the matn from al-Quduri, if the mukatab has no source of income (wajh), the master may request the judge to declare him incapacitated (ta'jiz), nullifying the kitaba. However, Abu Yusuf holds the opinion that mere lack of income is insufficient; the master must wait until the mukatab misses two consecutive installments (najman). This stricter requirement is based on a hadith from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) which prescribes returning the mukatab to slavery only after two consecutive missed payments. The proof explicitly quotes Ali's wording. This ikhtilaf remains; the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is typically the view of Abu Hanifa as recorded in the matn, but Abu Yusuf's view is also transmitted. The practical difference is that under Abu Yusuf's view, the master cannot rush to invalidate the contract after a single missed payment if the mukatab has no means.

Key Terms
تَعْجِيز (ta'jiz): Declaring the mukatab incapable of paying, leading to rescission of kitaba.
نَجْم (najm): Installment payment of the kitaba; also the time period for payment.
وَجْه (wajh): Source of income or means to earn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf, what condition must be met before the master can have the mukatab declared incapacitated?
A) The mukatab gives up hope of earning.
B) The mukatab misses two consecutive installments.
C) The master simply requests it.
D) The mukatab must be absent for one year.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the default position allows immediate ta'jiz upon lack of wajh, but Abu Yusuf restricts it to two consecutive missed payments based on a companion report.

Ruling on Incapacity and Death of the Mukatab with Proofs
Ruling with proofs on mukatab's incapacity and death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two rulings concerning a mukatab's incapacity and death, and identify the hadith proofs for each.

Core Idea
A mukatab who cannot pay returns to slavery; one who dies with enough wealth becomes free at death.

The mukatab is a slave who has contracted with his master to earn his freedom by paying installments. Islamic law carefully regulates his status to protect both his rights and the master's property. This passage presents two key rulings – one for incapacity during the contract, another for death while still indebted – and supports each with explicit proofs from the Sunnah and early practice. Understanding these rulings clarifies the binding nature of the kitaba contract and its consequences.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two scenarios
Identify the two different situations: (1) the mukatab becomes unable to pay (incapacity) during his lifetime, and (2) the mukatab dies while still owing part of the kitaba but leaving enough wealth.
The first leads to return to slavery; the second leads to freedom at death.
2
Extract the ruling for each scenario
For incapacity: the mukatab returns to the rulings of slavery, and his earnings become the master's property. For death with wealth: the kitaba is not rescinded; the estate pays the remaining debt, and he is considered free in the last part of his life.
The ruling on death implicitly treats the kitaba as a binding debt on the estate.
3
Locate the proofs for incapacity
The text cites two hadith: (a) the story of Bar'ira from Aisha, where the Prophet ﷺ stated 'al-wala' li man a'taq' (patronage is for the emancipator), establishing that the mukatab's earnings belong to the master; (b) a saying of Jabir that 'what they took from him is for them' when he fails to complete payment.
These hadith indicate the master's ownership of earnings upon incapacity.
4
Locate the proofs for death with wealth
The text cites a hadith from Umm Salamah: the Prophet ﷺ instructed a woman to veil from her mukatab if he has the means to pay, implying he is effectively free. It also reports that 'Ali ibn Abi Talib judged that the estate pays the debt and the surplus goes to the mukatab's free children.
The hadith shows the mukatab's freedom is effective at death if the estate can pay.
5
Understand the legal principle
The passage ends with a general rule: 'The slave's wealth is permissible for the master, even if acquired through charity.' This supports the first ruling that earnings from a mukatab who becomes incapacitated go to the master.
This principle is based on the master's ownership of the slave's acquisitions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا عَجَزَ الْمُكَاتَبُ عَادَ إِلَى أَحْكَامِ الرِّقِ وَكَانَ مَا فِي يَدِهِ مِنْ الْاكْتِسَابِ لِمَوْلَاهُ فَإِنْ مَاتَ الْمُكَاتَبُ وَلَهُ مَالٌ لَمْ تَنْفَسِخَ الْكِتَابَةُ وَقُضِيَ مَا عَلَيْهِ مِنْ اكْتِسَابِهِ وَحُكِمَ بِعِتْقِهِ فِي آخَرِ جُزْءٍ مِنْ أَجْزَاءِ حَيَاتِهِ (ا) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا عَجَزَ الْمُكَاتَبُ عَادَ إِلَى أَحْكَامِ الرِّقِ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ قَالَتْ : «كَانَ فِي بَرِيرَةَ ثَلَاثُ سُنَنٍ: عَتَقَتْ فَخَيَرَتْ وَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: الْوَلَاءُ لِمَنْ أَعْتَقَ وَدَخَلَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَبُرْمَةٌ عَلَى النَّارِ، فَقُرَبَ إِلَيْهِ خَيْرٌ وَأَدْمٌ مِنْ أَدْمِ الْبَيْتِ، فَقَالَ: لَمْ أَرَ الْبُرْمَةَ فَقِيلَ: حمْ تُصْدِقَ عَلَى بَرِيرَةَ وَأَنْتَ لَا تَأْكُلُ الصَّدَقَةَ، قَالَ: هُوَ عَلَيْهَا صَدَقَةٌ وَلَنَا هَدِيَّةٌ.» (صحيح البخاري، بَابُ الْحُرَّةِ تَحْتَ الْعَبْدِ، نمبر 5097) وَالْحَدِيثُ الثَّانِي لثبوت وَإِذَا عَجَزَ الْمُكَاتَبُ عَادَ إِلَى أَحْكَامِ الرِّق عَنْ جَابِرٍ، قَالَ: " لَهُمْ مَا أَخَذُوا مِنْهُ "، يَعْنِي إِذَا لَمْ يُكْمِل، فَرُدَّ فِي الرّقِ، فَمَا أَخَذَ فَلَهُ " (السنن الكبري لليبيهقي، باب: عَجْزُ الْمُكَاتَبِ ، نمبر 21759) (ا) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ مَاتَ الْمُكَاتَبُ وَلَهُ مَالٌ لَمْ تَنْفَسِخُ الْكِتَابَةُ \ سَمِعْتُ أُمَّ سَلَمَةَ، تَقُولُ: قَالَ لَنَا رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «إِنْ كَانَ لإحْدَاكُنَّ مُكَاتَبٌ، فَكَانَ عِنْدَهُ مَا يُؤَدِّي فَلْتَحْتَجِبْ مِنْهُ» (سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي الْمُكَاتَبِ يُؤَدِّي بَعْضَ كِتَابَتِهِ فَيَعْجِرُ أَوْ يَمُوتُ، نمبر 3928) (۲)قول التابعى لثبوت فَإِنْ مَاتَ الْمُكَاتَبُ وَلَهُ مَالٌ لَمْ تَنْفَسِخُ الْكِتَابَةُ \ قُلْتُ لِعَطَاءِ: الْمُكَاتَبُ يَمُوتُ وَلَهُ وَلَدٌ أَحْرَارٌ وَيَدَعُ أَكْثَرَ مِمَّا بَقِيَ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ كِتَابَتِهِ قَالَ: «يُقْضَى عَنْهُ مَا بَقِيَ مِنْ كِتَابَتِهِ وَمَا كَانَ مِنْ فَضْلٍ فَلِبَنِيهِ»، قُلْتُ: أَبَلَغَكَ هَذَا عَنْ أَحَدٍ؟ قَالَ: زَعَمُوا أَنَّ عَلِيًّا كَانَ يَقْضِي بِذَلِكَ، (مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابٌ : مِيرَاثُ وَلَدِ الْمُكَاتَبِ وَلَهُ وَلَدٌ أَحْرَارٌ، نمبر 15654) أصول : غلام کا مال آقا کے لئے حلال ہے، خواہ غلام کو صدقہ و خیرات ہی کا مال ملا ہو۔
And when the mukatab becomes incapacitated, he returns to the rulings of slavery, and what is in his hand of earnings is for his master. If the mukatab dies and has wealth, the kitaba is not rescinded, and what is owed from his earnings is paid, and he is judged to be free in the last part of the parts of his life. (a) The hadith for establishing: when the mukatab becomes incapacitated, he returns to the rulings of slavery: from Aisha, she said: 'There were three sunnahs in Bar'ira: she was freed and given choice, and the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: patronage is for the one who frees, and the Messenger of Allah ﷺ entered and a pot was on the fire, and bread and condiment from the house's condiment were brought near him, so he said: I did not see the pot, so it was said: it was given in charity to Bar'ira and you do not eat charity, he said: It is charity for her and a gift for us.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter: free woman under slave, no. 5097) And the second hadith for establishing: when the mukatab becomes incapacitated, he returns to the rulings of slavery: from Jabir, he said: 'They have what they took from him,' meaning when he did not complete, he is returned to slavery, and what he took is his. (Sunan al-Kubra by al-Bayhaqi, chapter: incapacity of mukatab, no. 21759) (a) The hadith for establishing: if the mukatab dies and has wealth, the kitaba is not rescinded: I heard Umm Salamah say: the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said to us: 'If one of you has a mukatab, and he has what he can pay, let her veil from him.' (Sunan Abu Dawud, chapter: about mukatab who pays part of his kitaba then becomes incapacitated or dies, no. 3928) (2) Saying of the tabi'i for establishing: if the mukatab dies and has wealth, the kitaba is not rescinded: I said to 'Ata': 'The mukatab dies and has free children and leaves more than what remains of his kitaba.' He said: 'What remains of his kitaba is paid from it, and whatever surplus is for his children.' I said: 'Has this reached you from anyone?' He said: 'They claim that Ali used to judge by that.' (Mushannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter: inheritance of mukatab's child and he has free children, no. 15654) Principle: The slave's wealth is permissible for the master, even if the slave acquired it through charity.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage states two rulings with their proofs. First ruling: If a mukatab becomes unable to pay his installments (incapacity), he returns to slavery, and any earnings he had become the property of his master. This is supported by two hadiths: one from Aisha regarding Bar'ira, where the Prophet ﷺ clarified the rules of charity and patronage, and another from Jabir indicating that if the mukatab does not complete payment, he returns to slavery and the master keeps what was paid. Second ruling: If the mukatab dies and has sufficient wealth to cover the remaining kitaba, the contract is not nullified. Instead, his estate pays off the debt, and he is considered to have become free at the last moment of his life. This is proven by a hadith from Umm Salamah where the Prophet ﷺ instructed her to veil from her mukatab if he has the means to pay, implying he is effectively free. Additionally, a statement of 'Ata' (a tabi'i) reports that Ali ibn Abi Talib judged similarly. The Urdu principle at the end summarises that a slave's wealth is halal for the master even if obtained through charity, which relates to the first ruling where earnings go to the master upon incapacity.

Key Terms
مُكَاتَب (mukatab): Slave who has a contract of kitaba with master to earn and purchase freedom.
كِتَابَة (kitaba): Contract of manumission by payment in installments.
عَجْز (ʿajz): Incapacity or inability to pay the installments.
الْوَلَاءُ لِمَنْ أَعْتَقَ (al-walā'u liman aʿtaq): Patronage (right of inheritance from freed slave) belongs to the emancipator.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens to the kitaba contract if the mukatab dies leaving sufficient wealth to pay the remaining installments?
A) The kitaba is invalidated and the wealth goes to the master.
B) The kitaba is not rescinded; the estate pays and the mukatab is considered free at death.
C) The children become slaves.
D) The master must free the mukatab's children.

Key Takeaway
The mukatab's kitaba is a binding contract: incapacity returns him to slavery with earnings to the master; death with sufficient wealth results in freedom via estate payment.

Children of a Mukatab Who Dies Insolvent
Ruling on children of mukatab with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a child born during kitaba and a purchased child, and state the Hanafi ruling for each.

Core Idea
A child born during kitaba is bound by the father's contract; a purchased child must pay in full or be enslaved.

This lesson examines the Hanafi fiqh regarding the children of a mukatab who dies before completing his kitaba. The key distinction is whether the child was born during the kitaba or purchased by the mukatab. We will see how the child's status determines their obligation and path to freedom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of children
Read the passage and note the two categories: walad mawlud (child born during kitaba) and walad mushtarā (child purchased by mukatab during kitaba).
2
State the ruling for each type
For the born child: he must work and pay the remaining installments of his father's kitaba; upon payment, both are freed. For the purchased child: he must choose to pay the entire kitaba immediately or be returned to slavery.
3
Identify the proofs cited
The passage cites two proofs: (1) Ali's statement 'Her child is in her position' indicating the child follows the mother's status, and (2) a statement from al-Tawri distinguishing the child of a mukatabah from that of an umm walad.
4
Analyze how the proofs support the ruling
Ali's statement equates the child's status with the mother's, meaning the child is subject to the same kitaba contract. Al-Tawri's statement reinforces that the child born during kitaba is freed when the mother is freed, while the child of an umm walad is not freed until the master dies.
5
Apply to a hypothetical scenario
Consider a mukatab who dies with unpaid installments, leaving a born son and a purchased daughter. Determine the obligations of each child and the final outcome if both pay.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ لَمْ يَتْرُكْ وَفَاءً وَتَرَكَ وَلَدًا مَوْلُودًا فِي الْكِتَابَةِ سَعَى فِي كِتَابَةِ أَبِيهِ عَلَى نُجُومِهِ فَإِذَا أَدَّى حَكَمْنَا بِعِتْقِ أَبِيهِ قَبْلَ مَوْتِهِ وَعَتَقَ الْوَلَدُ وَإِنْ تَرَكَ وَلَدًا مُشْتَرَى قِيلَ لَهُ إِمَّا أَنْ تُؤَدِّيَ الْكِتَابَةَ حَالَّةً وَإِلَّا رُدِدْت إِلَى الرّقِ وجه (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَإِنْ لَمْ يَتْرُكْ وَفَاءً وَتَرَكَ وَلَدًا مَوْلُودًا فِي الْكِتَابَةِ عَنْ عَلِي قَالَ : " وَلَدُهَا بِمَنْزِلَتِهَا "، - يَعْنِي الْمُكَاتَبَةَ، السنن الكبري لليبيهقي، بَابٌ: وَلَدُ الْمُكَاتَبِ مِنْ جَارِيَتِهِ، وَوَلَدُ الْمُكَاتَبَةِ مِنْ زَوْجِهَا، نمبر 21699) وجه : (۲) قول التابعى لثبوت وَإِنْ لَمْ يَتْرُكُ وَفَاءً وَتَرَكَ وَلَدًا مَوْلُودًا فِي الْكِتَابَةِ عَنِ التَّوْرِي قَالَ: الْمُكَاتَبَةُ إِذَا أُعْتِقَتْ عُتِقَ وَلَدُهَا، إِذَا وَلِدُوا فِي كِتَابَتِهَا، وَأُمُّ الْوَلَدِ إِذَا أُعْتِقَتْ لَمْ يُعْتَقْ وَلَدُهَا حَتَّى يَمُوتَ سَيِّدُهَا» . (مصنف عبد الرزاق بَابٌ : كِتَابَتُهُ وَلَا وَلَدَ لَهُ، وَمِيرَاثُ الْمُكَاتَبِ،نمبر 15651)
And if he does not leave sufficient (wealth) and leaves a child born during the kitaba, he (the child) works for his father's kitaba according to its installments, and if he pays, we judge that his father was freed before his death, and the child becomes free. And if he leaves a purchased child, it is said to him: Either you pay the kitaba immediately, or you are returned to slavery. Proof (1): Saying of the companion for establishing: And if he does not leave sufficient and leaves a child born during the kitaba, from Ali, he said: 'Her child is in her position,' meaning the mukatabah (female). (Sunan al-Kubra by al-Bayhaqi, chapter: child of mukatab from his slave woman, and child of mukatabah from her husband, no. 21699) Proof (2): Saying of the tabi'i for establishing: And if he does not leave sufficient and leaves a child born during the kitaba, from al-Tawri (?), he said: 'The mukatabah, when she is freed, her child is freed, if they were born during her kitaba; and the umm walad, when she is freed, her child is not freed until her master dies.' (Mushannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter: his kitaba and no child for him, and inheritance of mukatab, no. 15651)
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage deals with two scenarios concerning the children of a mukatab who dies insolvent (without sufficient wealth to pay the kitaba). First: if he leaves a child who was born during the kitaba (i.e., while the father was still under the contract), that child is required to work and pay the remaining installments of his father's kitaba. Once the child completes payment, we retrospectively judge that the father became free before his death, and consequently the child also becomes free. Second: if the child is purchased (i.e., the mukatab had bought a slave child), then that child is given a choice: either pay the full remaining kitaba immediately in a lump sum, or be returned to slavery. The proofs cited are: (1) a statement of Ali ibn Abi Talib that the child of a mukatabah is in her position, meaning the child follows the mother's status regarding freedom; (2) a statement of the tabi'i al-Tawri (perhaps al-Thawri) distinguishing between the child of a mukatabah (freed when she is freed) and the child of an umm walad (concubine mother, who is freed only upon master's death). These reports support the Hanafi ruling that the child born during kitaba is bound by the father's contract and can earn freedom by completing the payments.

Key Terms
وَلَد مَوْلُود (walad mawlud): Child born during the kitaba contract, considered part of the contract.
وَلَد مُشْتَرَى (walad mushtarā): Child purchased by the mukatab during his contract, not born to him.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens to a child born during the mukatab's kitaba if the father dies insolvent?
A) The child is immediately free.
B) The child becomes a slave of the master.
C) The child must work and pay the remaining kitaba to free himself and his father.
D) The child inherits the father's debt and must pay it instantly.

Key Takeaway
The child born during kitaba is bound by the father's contract; the purchased child has a stark choice: pay all or return to slavery.

Invalid Kitaba Contracts: Khamr, Khinzir, and Unspecified Items
Ruling on invalid kitaba contracts with wine, pork, self-price, and unspecified items.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three rulings on invalid considerations in kitaba and explain the distinction between fasid and batil in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A kitaba with invalid consideration is fasid, not batil — the slave can still be freed by paying, but must compensate the master with his value.

In the Hanafi school, the contract of kitaba (manumission by payment) is governed by strict conditions on what constitutes valid consideration. When a Muslim master contracts kitaba for wine, pork, or the slave's own value, the contract is not void but defective (fasid). This lesson unpacks the precise consequences and the critical difference between fasid and batil in the context of kitaba.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three invalid considerations
List the three items mentioned in the passage that cannot serve as valid consideration in a kitaba contract: wine, pork, and the slave's own price (value of himself).
Wine and pork are not permissible property for a Muslim; the slave's own price is circular.
2
Classify the kitaba's validity
The kitaba with such consideration is classified as fasid (defective), not batil (void). In Hanafi fiqh, a fasid contract can produce legal effects under certain conditions.
Fasid contracts are invalid in their essence but can be rectified; batil contracts are null from the outset.
3
Determine the consequence if payment occurs
If the slave actually delivers the invalid consideration (e.g., wine), he becomes free. However, he must then work to pay his actual market value (qimah) to the master, not the named amount.
The slave does not get freedom for free; he must compensate the master properly.
4
Distinguish between unspecified garment and undescribed animal
If kitaba is made for a garment without specifying its type (e.g., just 'a cloth'), the contract is invalid and the slave does not become free even if he delivers it. But if kitaba is for an animal without description (e.g., just 'an animal'), the contract is valid.
Animals as a category are considered wealth (mal); ambiguous garments may not be.
5
Extract the underlying principle
The principle is that kitaba becomes fasid if the consideration is not valid mal (weath) for a Muslim. However, actual delivery can still effect freedom with a compensation adjustment. Unspecified items that are not clearly mal render the contract totally invalid.
This shows the Hanafi pragmatic approach: preserving the goal of freedom while preventing injustice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا كَاتَبَ الْمُسْلِمُ عَبْدَهُ عَلَى خَمْرٍ أَوْ خِنْزِيرٍ أَوْ عَلَى قِيمَةِ نَفْسِهِ فَالْكِتَابَةُ فَاسِدَةٌ فَإِنْ أَدَّى الْخَمْرَ عَتَقَ وَلَزِمَهُ أَنْ يَسْعَى فِي قِيمَتِهِ لَا يَنْقُصُ مِنْ الْمُسَمَّى وَيُزَادُ عَلَيْهِ وَإِنْ كَاتَبَهُ عَلَى ثَوْبِ لَمَّ يُسَمِّ جِنْسَهُ لَمْ يَجْزْ وَإِنْ أَدَّاهُ لَمْ يَعْتِقْ إِنْ كَاتَبَهُ عَلَى حَيَوَانٍ غَيْرِ مَوْصُوفٍ فَالْكِتَابَةُ جَائِزَةٌ أصول : کتابت میں غیر مال کو بدل کتابت طے کیا تو معاملہ کتابت فاسد ہو گا، لیکن اگر مکاتب نے غیر مال کو بدل کتابت کے طور پر ادا کر دیا تو مکاتب آزاد ہو گا، البتہ اپنی قیمت کے بقدر سعایت کر کے آقا کو ادا کرے گا۔
And when a Muslim makes a kitaba with his slave for wine or pork or for the price of himself, the kitaba is invalid. If he pays the wine, he becomes free, and he is required to work for his price, not less than the named amount and increased over it. And if he makes a kitaba for a garment without specifying its type, it is not valid, and if he pays it, he does not become free. If he makes a kitaba for an undescribed animal, the kitaba is valid. Principle: If in kitaba, a non-wealth (non-commodity) is fixed as the consideration, the transaction of kitaba is invalid, but if the mukatab pays that non-wealth as the consideration, the mukatab becomes free, however he must work (sai) to pay his price to the master.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage lists several invalid kitaba contracts and their consequences. If a Muslim master contracts kitaba with his slave in exchange for wine or pork (which are not permissible property for a Muslim), or for the slave's own price (i.e., the value of his person), the kitaba is fasid (defective). However, if the slave actually delivers the wine, he becomes free, but he must then work to pay his actual price (qimah) to the master – not less than the named amount, and even exceeding it. If the kitaba is for an unspecified garment (e.g., just 'a cloth' without specifying type), the contract is invalid; even if the slave pays it, he does not become free. But if the kitaba is for an undescribed animal (e.g., 'an animal' without specifying type), the kitaba is valid because animals as a category are considered wealth and the uncertainty is tolerable. The Urdu principle summarises: if non-wealth (like wine) is fixed as consideration, the kitaba is invalid, but if the slave actually gives it, he is freed and must pay his value.

Key Terms
كِتَابَة فَاسِدَة (kitaba fasidah): Invalid kitaba contract due to flawed consideration, but can lead to freedom upon payment.
قِيمَة (qimah): Market value of the slave, used as basis for payment after invalid kitaba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a Muslim master makes a kitaba with his slave in exchange for wine?
A) The kitaba is valid and the slave becomes free upon delivery of wine.
B) The kitaba is invalid; the slave does not become free.
C) The kitaba is invalid; if the slave pays the wine, he becomes free and must work to pay his price.
D) The kitaba is void and the slave remains a slave forever.

Key Takeaway
A fasid kitaba can still free the slave upon payment of invalid consideration, but the slave must compensate the master with his own value.

Joint Kitaba of Two Slaves: Rulings and Guarantee
Ruling statement on joint kitaba contract for two slaves

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on joint kitaba for two slaves and distinguish the effects when a mutual guarantee condition is included.

Core Idea
A single kitaba for two slaves is valid; if one pays all, both are freed and the payer recovers half.

The Hanafi school permits a master to make a single kitaba contract for two slaves jointly. This passage from Al-Quduri states the basic ruling: both slaves are freed upon full payment, both return to slavery if they fail. It then covers an additional condition of mutual guarantee, which is also valid and creates a right of recourse between the slaves. Understanding this structure is essential for correctly applying the kitaba contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract type
Recognize that the passage deals with a single kitaba (مكاتبة واحدة) covering two slaves for one total sum.
This is a joint kitaba, not two separate contracts.
2
State the basic ruling without guarantee
If both slaves pay the entire sum, both become free. If both are unable to pay (عجز), both return to slavery.
There is no partial freedom; it's all or nothing for both.
3
Analyse the ruling with mutual guarantee
If the master includes a condition that each slave is guarantor for the other, the kitaba remains valid. In this case, if either slave pays the full amount, both are freed immediately.
The guarantee condition does not invalidate the contract; it only changes the payment dynamics.
4
Understand the right of recourse
The paying slave can recover half of what he paid from the other slave, because they are equal partners in the debt.
This is a debt between the slaves, not a new obligation to the master.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ كَاتَبَ عَبْدَيْهِ كِتَابَةً وَاحِدَةً عَلَى أَلْفِ دِرْهَم إِنْ أَدَّيَا عَتَقَا وَإِنْ عَجَزَا رُدَّا فِي الرِقِ وَإِنْ كَاتَبَهُمَا عَلَى أَنَّ كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا ضَامِنٌ عَنْ الْآخَرِ جَازَتْ الْكِتَابَةُ وَأَيُّهُمَا أَدَّى عَتَقَا وَيَرْجِعُ عَلَى شَرِيكِهِ بِنِصْفِ مَا أَدَّى
And if he makes a kitaba for his two slaves as one kitaba for one thousand dirhams, if they both pay, they both become free; if they both become incapacitated, they are both returned to slavery. And if he makes a kitaba for them on condition that each one of them is guarantor for the other, the kitaba is valid, and whichever of them pays, they both become free, and he has recourse against his partner for half of what he paid.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage covers the joint kitaba (mukataba) of two slaves together. If the master contracts a single kitaba for both slaves with a total sum (e.g., 1000 dirhams), the contract is valid. If both slaves together pay the full amount, both become free. If both fail to pay (become incapacitated), both return to slavery. If the master includes a condition of mutual guarantee (i.e., each is responsible for the other), the kitaba is still valid. In that case, if one slave pays the entire amount, both slaves become free immediately. The paying slave then has the right to recover half of what he paid from his partner (since they are equal partners in the debt).

Key Terms
كِتَابَة وَاحِدَة (kitaba wahidah): Single kitaba contract covering two or more slaves jointly.
ضَامِن (damin): Guarantor; each slave guarantees payment for the other.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a joint kitaba with mutual guarantee, if one slave pays the entire amount, what happens?
A) Only that slave becomes free; the other remains a slave.
B) Both become free, and the paying slave can recover half from his partner.
C) Both become free, and the paying slave cannot reclaim anything.
D) The kitaba is invalid because of guarantee.

Key Takeaway
A joint kitaba contract with mutual guarantee allows either slave to free both by paying the full sum, with a right to recover half from the partner.

Ruling on Master Freeing Mukatab or Dying
Ruling on master freeing mukatab or master's death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the master freeing a mukatab and the effect of the master's death on the kitaba contract, and apply these rulings to scenarios involving partial freeing by heirs.

Core Idea
A master's direct freeing frees the mukatab and waives the debt; death does not dissolve the contract.

In this lesson, we examine the interplay between the kitaba contract and the master's actions or death. The Hanafi school holds that if the master freely grants freedom to the mukatab, the debt is waived, but if the master dies, the contract continues with the heirs. A single heir cannot free the mukatab alone; all must agree. The Prophet's hadith on Bar'ira supports the principle that freedom is effective regardless of conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Note the two distinct situations: (1) the master directly frees the mukatab, and (2) the master dies. Each has a different ruling.
2
Determine the ruling for direct freeing
When the master frees the mukatab directly, the mukatab becomes free immediately and the entire remaining kitaba debt is waived. This is a voluntary act by the master.
3
Determine the ruling for the master's death
The kitaba contract is not dissolved by the master's death. The mukatab continues to pay the installments to the master's heirs.
4
Analyze the role of the heirs in freeing
If one heir alone tries to free the mukatab, it is ineffective because the right to free is shared. Only if all heirs collectively free him does he become free, and the debt is waived.
This preserves the interests of all heirs.
5
Connect to the prophetic proof
The hadith of Bar'ira (al-wala' li man a'taqa) establishes that freeing overrides any stipulations, confirming that a valid freeing (by the master or all heirs) takes effect irrespective of conditions.
The hadith is cited in Sahih al-Bukhari.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا أَعْتَقَ الْمَوْلَى مُكَاتَبَهُ عَتَقَ بِعِتْقِهِ وَسَقَطَ عَنْهُ مَالُ الْكِتَابَةِ وَإِذَا مَاتَ مَوْلَى الْمُكَاتَبِ لَم تَنْفَسِخُ الْكِتَابَةُ، وَقِيلَ لَهُ: أَذِ الْمَالَ إِلَى وَرَثَةِ الْمَوْلَى عَلَى نُجُومِهِ فَإِنْ أَعْتَقَهُ أَحَدُ الْوَرَثَةِ لَمْ يَعْتِقْ وَإِنْ أَعْتَقُوهُ جَمِيعًا عَتَقَ وَسَقَطَ عَنْهُ مَالُ الْكِتَابَةِ وجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا أَعْتَقَ الْمَوْلَى مُكَاتَبَهُ عَتَقَ بِعِتْقِهِ \ فَذَكَرَ لِعَائِشَةَ، فَذَكَرَتْ عَائِشَةُ مَا قَالَتْ لَهَا، فَقَالَ: اشْتَرِيهَا وَأَعْتِقِيهَا، وَدَعِيهِمْ يَشْتَرِطُونَ مَا شَاؤُوا فَاشْتَرَتْهَا عَائِشَةُ فَأَعْتَقَتْهَا، وَاشْتَرَطَ أَهْلُهَا الْوَلاءَ، فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ : الْوَلاءُ لِمَنْ أَعْتَقَ، وَإِنِ اشْتَرَطُوا مِائَةَ شرط. »، بخاري شريف، بَابٌ : إِذَا قَالَ الْمُكَاتَبُ اشْتَرِنِي وَأَعْتِقْنِي فَاشْتَرَاهُ لِذَلِكَ، نمبر 2565)
And when the master frees his mukatab, he becomes free by his freeing, and the kitaba wealth is waived from him. And when the master of the mukatab dies, the kitaba is not dissolved, and it is said to him (the mukatab): Pay the wealth to the heirs of the master according to its installments. If one of the heirs frees him, he does not become free; if all of them free him, he becomes free and the kitaba wealth is waived from him. Proof: Hadith for establishing: When the master frees his mukatab, he becomes free by his freeing: mentioned to Aisha, and Aisha mentioned what was said to her, so he (the Prophet) said: Buy her and free her, and let them stipulate whatever they wish. So Aisha bought her and freed her, and her (Bar'ira's) family stipulated patronage, so the Prophet said: Patronage is for the one who frees, even if they stipulate a hundred conditions. (Bukhari, chapter: When the mukatab says 'buy me and free me', and he buys him for that, no. 2565)
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage deals with two situations affecting the kitaba contract. First: if the master directly frees the mukatab (i.e., grants him freedom without payment), then the mukatab becomes free immediately and the entire remaining debt of kitaba is waived. This is supported by the hadith of Bar'ira where the Prophet instructed Aisha to buy and free her, and ruled that patronage belongs to the one who frees, regardless of conditions. Second: if the master dies, the kitaba contract does not dissolve; the mukatab continues to pay the installments to the master's heirs. If only one heir tries to free the mukatab, it is ineffective because the right of ownership is shared; all heirs must consent to free him. If they all free him together, he becomes free and the kitaba debt is waived, similar to the master's direct freeing.

Key Terms
عَتَقَ بِعِتْقِهِ (ataqa bi'itqihi): The mukatab becomes free by the act of the master freeing him, without payment.
وَرَثَة (warathah): Heirs of the master who inherit the right to receive kitaba payments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if the master of a mukatab dies?
A) The kitaba is dissolved and the mukatab becomes free.
B) The kitaba continues; the mukatab pays the heirs in installments.
C) The mukatab becomes the property of the heirs but must be freed immediately.
D) The kitaba becomes void and the mukatab returns to slavery.

Key Takeaway
The kitaba contract survives the master's death; only the master's direct freeing or unanimous freeing by all heirs terminates the contract and waives the debt.

Kitabah of Umm Walad
Ruling on kitabah of umm walad and her options

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of kitabah for an umm walad and explain the consequences when the master dies or when she bears his child during the contract.

Core Idea
Kitabah of an umm walad is valid; upon master's death her debt drops, and if she bears his child she may choose to continue or revert to umm walad status.

This passage from Al-Quduri's matn presents two key scenarios at the intersection of kitabah (manumission contract) and the status of umm walad (a slave woman who has borne her master's child). The rulings protect her interests and reflect the Hanafi approach to gradual freedom. Understanding these rules requires grasping the legal leverage an umm walad holds due to her anticipated freedom upon the master's death.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its basic ruling
The act is the master writing a kitabah contract for his umm walad. State the ruling: it is valid (jāza).
This establishes that the contract is legally binding and effective.
2
Consequence on master's death
If the master dies, the outstanding kitabah payment is dropped (saqata). Explain why: because the umm walad becomes free upon his death, and the debt is tied to the contract's continuation.
This is a unique benefit for the umm walad; a regular mukatab would still owe the heirs.
3
Scenario: birth of a child from the master
If the mukatabah bears a child from the master after the kitabah, she is given a choice (khiyār).
The child's paternity is linked to the master, affecting her status.
4
First option: continue the kitabah
She may choose to proceed with the kitabah, paying the installments to earn her freedom earlier.
This option makes sense if she prefers immediate freedom over waiting for the master's death.
5
Second option: declare incapacity and become umm walad
She may declare ta‘jīz (incapacity to complete payments) and revert to being an umm walad, securing freedom upon the master's death without further payment.
This option leverages her existing status and may be beneficial if she cannot afford payments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا كَاتَبَ الْمَوْلَى أُمَّ وَلَدِهِ جَازَ فَإِنْ مَاتَ الْمَوْلَى سَقَطَ عَنْهَا مَالُ الْكِتَابَةِ وَإِنْ وَلَدَتْ مُكَاتَبَتُهُ مِنْهُ فَهِيَ بِالْخِيَارِ إِنْ شَاءَتْ مَضَتْ عَلَى الْكِتَابَةِ وَإِنْ شَاءَتْ عَجَّزَتْ نَفْسَهَا وَصَارَتْ أُمَّ وَلَدٍ لَهُ
And when the master writes kitabah for his umm walad, it is valid. If the master dies, the kitabah payment drops from her. And if his mukatabah gives birth to a child from him, she has the choice: if she wishes, she continues on the kitabah; if she wishes, she declares herself incapable and she becomes his umm walad.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This is a ruling from Al-Quduri's matn on the kitabah of an umm walad. The master may validly contract kitabah with her. Upon his death, her obligation to pay the remaining kitabah is waived because she automatically becomes free as an umm walad. If she bears a child from the master after the kitabah, she has an option: she may either continue the kitabah and gain freedom through payment, or she may declare ta'jiz (incapacity) and revert to being an umm walad, gaining freedom upon the master's death without further payment.

Key Terms
أم الولد (umm al-walad): A slave woman who has borne a child to her master; she becomes free upon his death.
كتابة (kitabah): A contract between master and slave for the slave's freedom in exchange for fixed payments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a master dies after writing kitabah for his umm walad, what happens to the kitabah payment?
A) She must continue paying to the heirs
B) The payment is cancelled
C) She must pay half
D) She must pay double

Key Takeaway
Kitabah of an umm walad is valid and provides her with flexibility: upon master's death her debt is dropped, and if she bears his child she can choose between continuing payments or reverting to umm walad status.
