Wine Turning into Vinegar: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on wine vinegar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on wine turning into vinegar, contrast it with the Shafi'i position, and evaluate the proofs for each school.

Core Idea
Wine that becomes vinegar is halal and pure; intentional transformation is permissible and not disliked.

The Hanafi school holds that wine which turns into vinegar—whether spontaneously or by adding something—becomes permissible (halal) and ritually pure. This includes intentionally making wine into vinegar, which is not disliked. The Shafi'i school disagrees, ruling that intentional transformation is forbidden. This lesson unpacks the proofs and the practical impact of the difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling from Al-Quduri's matn: wine that becomes vinegar is halal, regardless of how the transformation occurred.
The ruling covers both spontaneous and intentional transformation.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that intentionally making wine into vinegar is haram, based on an explicit hadith.
The Shafi'i school permits spontaneous vinegar but considers the act of making it sinful.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the hadith of Anas (ra) where the Prophet (saw) answered 'No' when asked about making wine into vinegar.
This hadith is the primary evidence for the Shafi'i position.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds by citing the practice of the Companions (Aisha, Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz) and the general hadith praising vinegar as a condiment. They interpret the prohibition in Anas's hadith as discouragement in a specific context or abrogated.
The later practice of the Salaf is given precedence over isolated narrations.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: Hanafis may intentionally make vinegar from wine, consume it, and consider the vessel pure. Shafi'is may only consume spontaneous vinegar and consider the act of making it sinful.
This difference affects daily practice for Muslims in contexts where wine is available.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْأَشْرِبَةِ. وَإِذَا تَخَلَّلَتْ الْخَمْرُ حَلَّتْ سَوَاءٌ صَارَتْ خَلَّا بِنَفْسِهَا أَوْ بِشَيْءٍ طُرِحَ فِيهَا وَلَا يُكْرَهُ تَخْلِيلُهَا. مُسْكِرٍ حَرَامٌ. وَجْهٌ قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَإِذَا تَخَلَّلَتْ الْخَمْرُ حَلَّتْ سَوَاءٌ صَارَتْ خَلَّا بِنَفْسِهَا: سَأَلْتُ عَائِشَةَ عَنْ خَلِّ الْخَمْرِ، قَالَتْ: «لَا بَأْسَ بِهِ، هُوَ إِدَامٌ». وَجْهُ دَلِيلِ الشَّافِعِيِّ الْحَدِيثِ لِثُبُوتِ وَإِذَا تَخَلَّلَتْ الْخَمْرُ حَلَّتْ سَوَاءٌ صَارَتْ خَلَّا بِنَفْسِهَا: عَنْ أَنَسٍ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم سُئِلَ عَنِ الْخَمْرِ تُتَّخَذُ خَلَّا؟ فَقَالَ: (لَا). وَوَجْهُ قَوْلِ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَلَا يُكْرَهُ تَخْلِيلُهَا: قَالَ: شَهِدْتُ عُمَرَ بْنَ عَبْدِ الْعَزِيزِ كَتَبَ إِلَى عَامِلِهِ بِوَاسِطَ: «أَنْ لَا تَحْمِلُوا الْخَمْرَ مِنْ قَرْيَةٍ إِلَى قَرْيَةٍ، وَمَا أَدْرَكْتَ فَاجْعَلْهُ خَلَّا». وَوَجْهُ الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَلَا يُكْرَهُ تَخْلِيلُهَا: عَنْ جَابِرٍ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «نِعْمَ الْإِدَامُ الْخَلُّ». أصول: حرام ہونے تک رس ڈالا تو حرام ہو گا اور اگر کم ڈالا تو حلال رہے گا۔ أصول: حرمت ثابت ہونے کے بعد جلانے سے حرمت ختم نہیں ہو گی۔ أصول: شراب کو سرکہ بنا دیا جائے تو اسکا استعمال جائز ہو گا۔ أصول: خمر سرکہ بن جائے تو پاک ہو گا اور وہ برتن بھی پاک ہو گا جس میں پہلے خمر تھی۔
Book of Beverages. And when wine becomes vinegar, it becomes permissible, whether it becomes vinegar by itself or by something thrown into it. And it is not disliked to intentionally make it vinegar. An intoxicant is forbidden. Evidence: Statement of a Companion for establishing 'when wine becomes vinegar, it becomes permissible, whether it becomes vinegar by itself': I asked Aisha about vinegar made from wine; she said: 'There is no harm in it; it is a condiment.' Evidence of al-Shafi'i's proof for establishing 'when wine becomes vinegar, it becomes permissible, whether it becomes vinegar by itself': From Anas that the Prophet was asked about wine being made into vinegar; he said: 'No.' Evidence: Statement of a Tabi'i for establishing 'it is not disliked to make it vinegar': He said: I witnessed that Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz wrote to his governor in Wasit: 'Do not carry wine from one village to another, and whatever you obtain, make it into vinegar.' And evidence: the hadith for establishing 'it is not disliked to make it vinegar': From Jabir from the Prophet: 'What an excellent condiment is vinegar!'. Principles: If an intoxicating substance is added to wine until it becomes forbidden, then if added in small quantity? Actually principles state: If an intoxicant is added until it becomes forbidden, then it becomes forbidden; if added less, it remains permissible. Principle: After prohibition is established, burning does not remove prohibition. Principle: If wine is made into vinegar, its use becomes permissible. Principle: If wine becomes vinegar, it becomes pure, and the vessel that previously contained wine also becomes pure.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on the ruling of wine that turns into vinegar. The Hanafi position, as stated in the matn of Al-Quduri, is that wine that becomes vinegar is permissible to consume, whether it transformed spontaneously or by something added (like salt or onion). Furthermore, it is not disliked to intentionally make wine into vinegar. This is based on the practice of the Companions and Tabi'in, as shown by the narration from Aisha and the directive of Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz. The opposing school, represented by al-Shafi'i, holds that intentionally making wine into vinegar is prohibited, based on the hadith of Anas where the Prophet answered 'No' when asked about making wine into vinegar. The Hanafi response is that the prohibition in that hadith is understood as discouragement in the context of certain vessels used for nabidh, or that the hadith is abrogated. The Hanafi school gives greater weight to the later practice and the general principle that vinegar is a permissible condiment. The Urdu principles summarize: the key point is that once wine becomes vinegar, it becomes both permissible to consume and pure; the vessel also becomes pure. However, if an intoxicating substance is added to wine and it becomes forbidden, it does not become permissible by simply burning it.

Key Terms
تخللت (takhallalat): It became vinegar; transformation of wine into vinegar.
تخليل (takhleel): The act of intentionally making wine into vinegar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on wine that spontaneously becomes vinegar?
A) It remains impure and haram.
B) It becomes halal but the vessel remains impure.
C) It becomes halal and pure, and the vessel is also purified.
D) It is only permissible if no foreign substance was added.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, wine that becomes vinegar is halal and pure regardless of the method of transformation, and it is not disliked to intentionally make it.
